602 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Rupe v. Shaw


No. 36947


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 223; 286 P.2d 1094; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 471



July 20, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied August 2, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner taxpayer filed a petition to enjoin respondent state auditor from issuing, and respondent state treasurer from paying, any state warrants out of two separate funds established by the state legislature.


OVERVIEW: The legislature passed two amendments that established funds. House Bill No. 786 generated funds to be used to build a dam. House Bill No. 941 was enacted pursuant to a general referendum and generated funds for state institutions. The taxpayer sought to prevent fund being used for various state institutions, a memorial, and a state park. The court denied the taxpayer's petition. The taxpayer challenged the language of Bill. No. 941, claiming that it was misleading. The court found the bill's general purpose was sufficiently declared in the resolution and that the details provided for its accomplishment in the law thereafter enacted were incidents necessary or convenient or tending to the accomplishment of one general design. The taxpayer made no showing of the alleged effect, or invalidity under the Okla. Const. art. 24, § 1, of the questioned proposal for said document's alteration, except the allegations of the taxpayer herself. The court further held that the taxpayer's cause of action relating to House Bill No. 786 established no sound basis sufficiently justifying holding the law unconstitutional and/or granting the injunction prayed for.


OUTCOME: The court denied the taxpayer's petition seeking to enjoin the expenditure of state funds pursuant to recent enactments.

 

603 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Panhandle Eastern Pipe Line Co. v. Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 36312, 36483, 36484, 36501


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 161; 285 P.2d 847; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 725; 4 Oil & Gas Rep. 1769



May 24, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Amended June 14, 1955. Rehearing Denied July 5, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, a natural gas producer and a royalty owner, sought review of orders entered by appellee, the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma, which concerned the drilling and production of gas wells, and which that pooled the interests of leaseholders of certain land.


OVERVIEW: The Commission entered an order that established well-spaced units on land acreage shown on a plat adopted with its order. Under that order, only one well could be drilled in each unit, and wells that were then producing gas in certain units were designated as the wells for those units. In new proceedings that followed the entry of that order, the Commission entered pooling orders, which pooled the interests of all lessors of certain units and specified the interests to be shared by lessors in those working gas wells that were located on certain of the units. The original order provided that royalty owners in each unit were to participate in the royalty from the well drilled in that unit in that same proportion that the acreage owned by a royalty owner bore to the total acreage of the unit. The pooling orders contemplated subsequent determinations for sharing of working interests and production from the wells. The court held that interests in certain land as found by the Commission to have overlaid the common source of supply was the minimum requirement for participation in well production on the part of others than the owners under a well lease under a valid order.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's orders.

 

604 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hicks v. Hamilton


No. 36506


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 149; 283 P.2d 1115; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 676



May 17, 1955 


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from from order sustaining defendant's petition to vacate default judgment. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff passenger appealed an order from the trial court (Oklahoma) sustaining a petition by defendant driver to vacate a default judgment upon the grounds that the statutory requirements for service upon non-residents, Okla. Stat. tit. 47, §§ 391-403 (1951), were to be strictly construed, and failure to attach and file the return registered receipt as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 395 (1951) invalidated the attempted service.


OVERVIEW: This was a case of first impression arising out of an automobile accident in which the passenger was injured when the car in which he was riding was struck by the driver, a nonresident. The passenger contended that service was sufficient because the parties' stipulated that the essential steps for service were taken, except for attaching the receipt as required by § 395. The court disagreed and found that if this requirement was an integral step in establishing proof of service, there was no merit to the argument because the parties could not have conferred jurisdiction upon the trial court by agreeing that this requirement was immaterial. The passenger also contended that the nonresident service statutes did not require actual receipt of notice as long as the notice was sent to the "last known address." The court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 394 (1951) required mailing of a notification by restricted registered mail, which would require the signature of the addressee. The court held that strict compliance with the provisions providing for service of process upon a non-resident defendant was mandatory and that the passenger failed to fully comply with such requirements.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court sustaining the driver's petition and motion to vacate the default judgment.

 

605 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re City Council of Tahlequah


No. 36799


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 136; 285 P.2d 418; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 717



May 3, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 7, 1955. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied July 19, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicants, a city counsel on behalf of a city applying for bonds to be issued, filed an action in compliance with Okla. Stat. tit. 11, §§ 449.1 to 449.20 (Supp. 1953) seeking approval of the bonds to be issued by the city after the issuance had been approved by a majority of the tax paying voters of the city. Protestants contested the issuance.


OVERVIEW: The applicants filed an original proceeding seeking the approval of bonds to be issued by the city. The protestants argued that §§ 449.1 to 449.20 violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 27. The court found that the bonds were proposed to be issued for the purpose of purchasing and installing a natural gas distribution system in said city. The bonds were not general obligations of the city, but were payable from funds to be accumulated by income from the use and operation of the gas distribution system. No part was to be paid from money derived from ad valorem taxes. For that reason, no provision was made in the bonds or the proceedings in connection therewith for the levy of a tax to pay said bonds or the interest thereon; therefore, a violation of art. X, § 27 existed. Because not only did the bonds and the proceedings in connection therewith fail to make any provision of a tax levy for their payment, they had the effect so as to negative any such provision, they were in contravention of Okla. Const. art. X, § 27 and were void. The court denied the application.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application.

 

606 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Matlock v. Bd. of County Comm'rs


No. 36608


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 36; 281 P.2d 169; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 405



February 15, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 22, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Wagoner County; E. A. Summers, Judge.

Action by plaintiffs to enjoin sale of bonds or further proceedings under provisions of 70 O.S.1951 Sec. 15-7 et seq. attacking validity of statutes involved. Judgment sustaining demurrer to plaintiffs petition and plaintiffs appeal. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error taxpayers appealed a decision by the District Court of Wagoner County (Oklahoma), which sustained the demurrer by defendants in error, a board of county commissioners and others, to the taxpayers' petition in their action to enjoin sale of bonds or further proceedings under provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 15-7 et seq. (1951) attacking validity of statutes involved.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers argued that because Okla. Stat. tit. 70, §§ 15-7 to 15-13 (1951) dealt solely with maintenance of separate schools under Oklahoma's system of segregation, §§ 15-7 to 15-13 were in violation of the Due Process and Equal Protection Clauses of U.S. Const. amends. V, XIV. The court found that the School Code of the State of Oklahoma, of which §§ 15-7 to 15-13 were a part, covered the entire field of public education, such as the organization of school districts, employment and qualification of teachers, the acquisition, management and control of school facilities, and tax levies, to mention only a few. The court determined that these were purely local problems not involved in the United States Supreme Court segregation cases. Sections 15-7 to 15-13 had to do with the acquisition and maintenance of school property. If it could have been said that property so acquired could not have been used for any purpose other than the education of children of the colored race, because it was for separate schools, there might have been some merit in the taxpayers' contention. However, such contention could not have been sustained.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

607 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Updike Adver. Sys. v. State Indus. Comm'n


No. 35637


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 19; 282 P.2d 759; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 453



February 1, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 29, 1955. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied May 3, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its insurance carrier, sought review of a decision of respondent State Industrial Commission (Oklahoma), which awarded workmen's compensation benefits to respondents, the widow and minor children of a deceased employee.


OVERVIEW: The employer was an outdoor billboard company. The employee was the president of the employer. The employee was killed in an automobile accident that occurred when he was taking a trip in a company owned vehicle to inspect and repair signs owned by the employer. The Commission awarded benefits to the employee's widow and children. The court sustained the award of the Commission. The court held: (1) a corporate officer may serve both as an officer and workman under circumstances making him an employee within the meaning of the Workmen's Compensation Law, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 1 et seq. (1951); (2) if he sustains injuries while performing duties in the latter capacity, he is entitled to compensation; (3) the Commission's findings that the employee, at the time of his death, was engaged in a hazardous occupation covered by the Act and that his death resulted from an accidental injury arising out of and in the course of his employment was supported by competent evidence; (3) Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 44(b) (1951), which provides that there shall be no subrogation to recover money paid by the employer or his insurance carrier for death claims under the Act, is constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the award of the Commission.

 

608 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Panoma Corp. v. Tex. Co.


No. 36111


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1955 OK 5; 284 P.2d 716; 1955 Okla. LEXIS 685; 4 Oil & Gas Rep. 375



January 7, 1955 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 10, 1955. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied June 14, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County; A. P. Van Meter, Judge.

Action instituted by The Texas Company, as plaintiff, against D. D. Harrington and Panoma Corporation, as defendants, for an accounting of gas produced under a contract entered into by plaintiff and Harrington (from whom Panoma Corporations rights are deraigned), and for a money judgment for the difference between the price paid The Texas Company for the gas produced thereunder and the price specified for gas taken from said field by Order No. 19514, subsequently entered by the State Corporation Commission. From a judgment for The Texas Company against Panoma Corporation, the latter appeals. Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant oil producers sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which awarded judgment to plaintiff oil producer in an action for an accounting of gas produced under a contract and for a money judgment for the difference between the contract price paid for the gas produced and the price allegedly specified by the Corporation Commission.


OVERVIEW: There were a series of gas leases involved, but the dispute was to one particular field. No testimony was taken and all of the facts being shown by exhibits and a stipulation between counsel. The issue on appeal was whether plaintiff was due an extra fee for the gas produced on the lease in question based on an order of the Corporation Commission. Plaintiff contended that it was entitled to be paid at the same rate as specified in the Commission's order for another gas field. Plaintiff had contended that unless the Commission's fixed price was made to supersede the contract price, the price-fixing order would not be uniformly and indiscriminately protect correlative rights which was one of the purposes of the conservation order. The court disagreed. The court held that "correlative rights" was not synonymous with equal rights. The court held that plaintiff was not an ordinary royalty owner and the only price prescribed in the contract was the one paid by defendants.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed and the cause was remanded to said court with directions to set it aside and enter a new judgment denying plaintiff any recovery.

 

609 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Comm'r of Land Office v. Laughlin


No. 36124


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 342; 277 P.2d 683; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 719



December 7, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the Commissioners of the Land Office, appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Latimer County (Oklahoma), which overruled the Commissioners' motion for new trial. The Commissioners had instituted an action to recover the amount due upon a deficiency judgment against the decedent. The trial court found defendant, the administrator of the decedent's estate, liable for the amount of the deficiency judgment.


OVERVIEW: The School Land Commission obtained a personal judgment against the decedent at a rate of 10 percent per annum. A real estate mortgage was given as security for the obligation. Real estate was sold and the amount of the sale was credited on the judgment. There was left unpaid on the judgment a certain sum together with interest at 10 percent. After the death of the decedent, the cause was revived in the name of the administrator of the decedent's estate. The trial court found that the Commissioners of the Land Office were required under Okla. Stat. tit. 64, § 82.2 to release all deficiency judgments resulting from the judicial sale of lands encumbered by mortgages where the State was a mortgagee, upon payment by a judgment debtor of the amount of the judgment rendered, plus interest at the rate of five percent per annum from the date of the judgment. The court ruled that the trial court's decision to remit one-half the interest due upon the judgment was void under Okla. Const. art. VII, § 34, 35, 53; Okla. Const. art. VI, § 11; and Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 681 (1951) because Okla. Stat. tit. 64, § 82.2 attempted to extinguish in part an obligation due the State.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court. The court directed the trial court to enter judgment for the Commissioners with accrued interest at 10 percent and with attorney's fees.

 

610 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ray v. Williams


No. 34827


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 339; 278 P.2d 550; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 735



November 30, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 7, 1955.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, a husband and a wife, and defendant minor landowner appealed a judgment of the District Court of Pittsburg County (Oklahoma), which held the resale tax deed of the husband and the wife was legal and valid and their title perfect; that the minor had a right to redeem the real estate by paying all taxes within 120 days, and that upon payment by the minor the minor's title to the property be quieted in her.


OVERVIEW: The husband and the wife and the minor appealed the trial court's denial of their motions for a new trial following the trial court's decision. The husband and the wife argued that Okla. Stat. tit. 38, §§ 432f and 433a (1951) were unconstitutional because the titles said nothing about allowing persons under disability to have one year after removal of the disability within which to redeem the real estate and therefore violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 57. The minor argued that the trial court erred in limiting her time to pay the taxes to 120 days. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 38, §§ 432f and 433a regulated the procedure by which the county could sell real estate for delinquent taxes, and provisions for redemption by persons under disability were incidental to the main purpose. Thus, §§ 432f and 433a did violate Okla. Const. art. V, § 57. Okla. Stat. tit. 38, § 433a (1951) clearly provided that minors had the right to redeem any land owned by them or in which they had a legal or equitable interest from the lien resulting from tax sale within one year after the expiration of their disability. Thus, the trial court erred in requiring the minor to pay the taxes in 120 days.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and found that the husband and the wife were the lawful owners of the property subject to the minor's right to redeem at any time within one year after expiration of her disability.

 

611 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Munson v. Snyder


No. 36338


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 257; 275 P.2d 249; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 635



October 5, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Contestant decedent's daughter appealed a decision of an Oklahoma trial court that found for proponent decedent's son and admitted a disputed will into probate. The decedent's daughter asserted that the will was improperly signed in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 55 (1951), that the court lacked jurisdiction over this matter, and that Okla. Stat. tit. 20, § 289 (1951), under which a judge pro tempore was appointed, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: A decedent's daughter challenged the decedent's son and sought to prevent a will from being admitted into probate. The trial court admitted the will into probate and that decision was affirmed by the court. Although the decedent's daughter asserted that the will was improperly signed in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 84, § 55 (1951), the court declared that in determining a will's validity, form could not be placed above substance. A will would not be voided for having been improperly signed unless dispositive provisions followed the testator's signature. The decedent's daughter challenged the trial court's jurisdiction but the court noted that this matter involved a question of fact and as such the trial court's decision thereto could not be disturbed unless it clearly ran against the weight of the evidence. Further, the court found that the appointment of a judge pro tempore pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 20. § 289 (1951), was not unlawful because that statute was constitutional. Finally, the court found no evidence that the will was tainted by undue influence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment that admitted the will into probate.

 

612 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


BRYANT v. MITCHELL


No. 35975


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 259; 275 P.2d 271; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 640



October 5, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individuals appealed a decision of the district court (Oklahoma), which upheld an election held by defendant county superintendent at which election the majority of the electors voting voted in favor of annexation of a school district to another district in the county.


OVERVIEW: The individuals filed an action in the district court contending that an election held by the county superintendent was void and sought an order declaring the resulting annexation vacated. The district court upheld the process and the results and the individuals appealed. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the decision of the district court that two of the voters lived within the county was not clearly against the weight of the evidence and that the election was free from fraud and each and every elector was given the opportunity to freely express his or her choice for or against annexation. The court found that the election was properly had by the county superintendent, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 7-1 (1951), and that § 7-1 was not unconstitutional in that it did not violate Okla. Const. art. III, § 6, which did not apply to school district elections, as the individuals contended.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's judgment.

 

613 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sullivan v. Okla. Tax Comm'n


No. 33469


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 266; 283 P.2d 521; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 763



October 5, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 3, 1955.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from the District Court of Oklahoma County; Lewis R. Morris, Judge.

Action by H. L. Sullivan as the assignee of J. A. and Lina J. Hull to recover income taxes paid in 1923 on income accruing in 1922 from the sale of stock in a corporation. The action was tried to the court and upon judgment being rendered in favor of the defendant this appeal was perfected.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, an assignee of two taxpayers, appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) in favor of defendant, the Oklahoma Tax Commission. The assignee sought to recover income taxes paid by the taxpayers from the sale of stock. The basis of the action was the alleged payment of the tax under a mistake of fact and because of notice from the State Auditor.


OVERVIEW: The Commission contended that the assignee was without statutory authority to maintain this action and that he did not have an action at law. The assignee contended that the taxpayers did not voluntarily pay the taxes. The court disagreed and found that the record showed that the taxpayers reported the taxes in their return as being due, paid them without protest before they became delinquent, and therefore before the taxes became a lien, and before process could issue to enforce payment. Therefore, there was no mistake of fact because the taxpayers knew the taxes were voluntarily paid. The assignee also asserted that Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 910 (1941) granted authority to maintain an action at law. However, the court found that this contention was not borne out by the language of § 910 to the effect that a taxpayer resisting the collection of any income tax could pay his tax under protest and file suit to recover. While neither the taxpayers nor the assignee at any time had a remedy at law, a remedy was in fact afforded by statute under Okla. Stat. § 12665 (1931). Because the taxpayers failed to pursue their statutory remedy, the assessments were final.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court in favor of the Tax Commission.

 

614 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Chi., Rock Island & Pac. R.R. Co. v. State


No. 36138


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 250; 274 P.2d 549; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 624; 7 P.U.R.3d 321



September 28, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railroad sought review of an order from the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma which directed the railroad to install a warning signal where its right-of-way crossed a particular street.


OVERVIEW: The sole argument on appeal was that the act of the Corporation Commission in ordering the railroad to install and maintain the warning signal, without making provision for the payment of at least part of the cost of the installation by the Federal Government, was an unconstitutional act amounting to a taking of property without due process of law. The court found that the Corporation Commission had heard and determined the necessity for the construction of the signal under Okla. Stat. tit. 17, § 84 (1951), and the fact that there could be means by which the railroad could be partially reimbursed was incidental and without legal significance to the issues involved. The court found that the Corporation Commission had the power to order the signal, as provided by Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 124 (1941), and therefore sustained the order.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the order directing the railroad to install a warning signal.

In re Okla. Planning & Res. Bd.


No. 36547


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 226; 274 P.2d 61; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 604



August 9, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 13, 1954.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oklahoma Planning and Resources Board filed an application for the approval of state park improvement bonds, which it proposed to issue for the making of park improvements on numerous state-owned parks and for refunding a certain sum of park bonds it issued.


OVERVIEW: The Oklahoma Planning and Resources Board filed an application for the approval of state park improvement bonds, which it proposes to issue for the making of park improvements on numerous state owned parks and for refunding a certain sum of park bonds issued and improved by the court. The amount of bonds proposed to be issued was in the sum of $ 7.2 million. Notice of the hearing of the application was duly published; no protests were filed nor objections made, and the matter came on for hearing. The prospective purchasers of the bonds raised certain questions as to the constitutionality of the issuance of the bonds, and also as to the plan of the operation of the development program as set out in the resolution of the Board authorizing the issuance of the bonds. The court approved the bonds issued in the sum of $ 7.2 million. The court held that the bonds were not violative of Okla. Const. art. 10, §§ 23, 24 or 25. Because the bonds expressly provided that they were payable solely from the revenues to be derived from the operation of the state parks and not an indebtedness of the State of Oklahoma or the Oklahoma Planning and Resources Board.


OUTCOME: The court approved the bonds issued in the sum of $ 7.2 million and it fixed the time within which a petition for rehearing could be filed at five days from the date the opinion was promulgated.

 

616 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


In re Okla. Educ. TV Auth.


No. 36411


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 219; 272 P.2d 1027; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 589



July 9, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oklahoma Educational Television Authority applied for the approval of bonds under Okla. Stat. Ann. tit. 70 §§ 2141-2165 (1953).


OVERVIEW: The bonds for $ 1,450,000 were for the construction and operation of a television facility. Denying approval, the court said that the debt for the bond issue violated Okla. Const. art. XX, § 23 (1941), which prohibited the creation or authorization of debts or obligations against the state or its institutions. All of the revenue accruing to a state Public Building Fund in future years was pledged to the payment of the bonds. The bond issue created a debt against the Fund. It pledged Fund revenues to the payment of the bonds. By the Act, the state attempted to authorize the creation of a debt against the Fund, a valuable state asset. The Fund was not created by the facility to be constructed or operated, nor did the facility nor the Authority add anything to the Fund. In adopting the constitutional amendment, the people intended to prohibit the creation of debts except in stated exceptions. The proposed bonded debt was not self-liquidating. The revenue from this facility, if any, was to be expended in operating the facility. The bonded debt was a debt against an existing, permanent state fund and its future revenues.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for the approval of the bonds.

 

617 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Natural Gas Pipeline Co. of Am. v. Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 35731, 35732, 35734


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 133; 272 P.2d 425; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 583; 5 P.U.R.3d 1



April 27, 1954 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 13, 1954.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent producers of gas appealed the order of the Corporation Commission (Oklahoma), which fixed the minimum price at which gas produced from a certain industrial field must be purchased or sold, following the Commission's review of the application of petitioner mineral owners.


OVERVIEW: The Commission fixed the minimum price at which residue gas might be produced and taken from an industrial field. Since the effective date of the order, the price of all other industrial fuels substantially increased. There had also been an increase in demand for natural gas and the costs of production materially increased. The producers argued that the cost of gathering and processing the gas from the industrial field was higher because it was not sold at the wellhead but rather sold in interstate commerce. On appeal, the producers first contended that the order of the Commission was not predicated upon adequate findings. The court affirmed that the evidence supported the regulatory order. The State had an interest in conserving its natural resources. The court concluded that the Commission had the power to fix the price of residue gas as a necessary incident, under the facts shown in the record, to the regulation of the sale of raw gas as taken from the structures. The residue gas was the only fairly stable constituent of raw gas. The formula and method established was both reasonable and practical.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order of the Commission that fixed the minimum price at which gas produced from a certain industrial field must be purchased or sold.

 

618 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Combs v. Hopping Inv. Co.


No. 35960


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 125; 269 P.2d 997; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 506



April 27, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the State and the county attorney, sought review of a judgment from the trial court (Oklahoma), which sustained the general demurrer of appellee trust company and entered judgment in favor of the company in appellants' action alleging a violation of Okla. Const. art. XXII, § 2, and seeking to recover penalties under Okla. Stat. tit. 18, § 1.23 (1951).


OVERVIEW: The State and the county attorney filed an action against the trust company to recover penalties for allegedly holding county real estate in violation of Okla. Const. art. XXII, § 2, and to recover penalties as provided by Okla. Stat. tit. 18, § 1.23 (1951). Upon judgment in favor of the company, the State and county attorney sought review, contending that Okla. Stat. tit. 18, § 1.20 (1951), which stated that the inhibition against a corporation holding land for more than seven years did not apply to one holding as a trustee of an express or testamentary trust for the benefit of natural persons, was unconstitutional because it attempted to enlarge the restrictions placed in Okla. Const. art. XXII, § 2. On appeal, the court affirmed. Specifically, the court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 18, § 1.20, did not violate the broad authority granted to the legislature in Okla. Const. art. XXII, § 2. Because the inhibition applicable to corporations holding land was not applicable to business trusts such as the company, the petition filed by the State and county attorney did not state a cause of action. The trial court did not err in sustaining the company's demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

 

619 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Kelly v. Okla. Tpk. Auth.


No. 35772


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 112; 269 P.2d 359; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 495



April 13, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners sought review of a decision by an Oklahoma trial court, which entered judgment in favor of plaintiff, a turnpike authority, in the authority's action to condemn two tracts and an easement over the landowners' property.


OVERVIEW: The authority brought three separate condemnation suits. The trial court appointed condemnation commissioners who returned their report awarding the landowners damages for condemnation of the three tracts. The authority then deposited the exact amount of the awards with the court clerk and thereafter took possession of the property. Then, the authority filed demand for a jury trial and the landowners then secured disbursement orders for the condemnation money, and upon such orders the court clerk paid over the condemnation money, less one percent poundage fee. Subsequently, the landowners filed motion to re-tax the costs and, following a hearing the authority deposited a sum equal to the poundage fee on the amount of damages awarded in one case. The court ruled that it was error for the assessment of the statutory one percent poundage fee charged under Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 921 (1951), tit. 28, 31 (1951), to have been put upon the landowners' withdrawal of the commissioners' award, as it constituted a part of the costs of the first assessment required to be paid by the authority under Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 56 (1951).


OUTCOME: The judgment rendered charged the landowners with the poundage fee as part of the costs of the action, and also charged them with interest upon the balance or difference between the amount of the commissioners' award and the amount allowed by the jury from the date of withdrawal of such funds. The judgment was reversed with directions to enter judgment for the landowners as to these items. In all other respects the judgment was affirmed.

 

620 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Darnell


No. 35478


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 95; 268 P.2d 860; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 481



March 30, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff former county school superintendent sought review of the order of the trial court (Oklahoma) that denied plaintiff's action in quo warranto brought to determine the eligibility of defendant, the newly elected superintendent. Plaintiff argued that defendant lacked the required certificate from the state board of education.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff brought a quo warranto action against defendant after his election as county school superintendent. Plaintiff claimed defendant was not qualified because he did not hold an administrator's certificate at the time he filed for candidacy nor on the date of the primary or general elections. The court affirmed and held that the question was defendant's eligibility to hold office since there had been no challenge to his candidacy. The court held that plaintiff did not utilize the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 26, § 165a (1951) to question the eligibility of defendant as a candidate. The court found that defendant had been issued a proper certificate several days before his induction into office and that made him qualified to hold office. The court also found that the scope of review was only as to defendant's eligibility to hold office, not for nomination or election to that office.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

621 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sinclair Ref. Co. v. Brumett


No. 36059


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 65; 267 P.2d 576; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 443



March 2, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Respondent refining company sought review of a judgment of the Oklahoma State Industrial Commission, which rendered judgment in favor of the claimant son in his claim for death benefits under the Oklahoma Workmen's Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11 (1951), following the death of the son's father.


OVERVIEW: The son's father was working for an independent contractor who had been engaged by the refining company to erect sign. The father was killed when he came into contact with an electric wire. The son sought death benefits under the Workmen's Compensation Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 11 (1951). The Commission determined that the independent contractor had not complied with the Act with regard to securing the payment of awards thereunder, and awarded the son death benefits primarily against the independent contractor and secondarily against the refining company. The refining company sought review, contended that an amendment to the statute that referred to an employer's obligation to pay workmen's compensation benefits, was unconstitutional under Okla. Const. art. V, § 57, because it had not re-enacted and published another part of the former Act. The court held that the amendment was constitutional because the Act was comprised of three parts and the amendment only amended one part. The court ruled that amendment did not tend to mislead or deceive and no mischief which the Oklahoma Constitution was intended to prohibit had been worked.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the award of death benefits to the claimant, son of the deceased employee.

 

622 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


S. Okla. Royalty Owners Ass'n v. Stanolind Oil & Gas Co.


Nos. 35737-35739


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 36; 266 P.2d 633; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 426; 3 Oil & Gas Rep. 1407



February 2, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error royalty association sought review of a decision by the Corporation Commission (Oklahoma), which granted defendant in error oil company's applications for location exceptions to spacing orders previously issued by the commission with respect to an oil field.


OVERVIEW: The oil company filed applications to drill for oil in a field that had three producing formations. The Corporation Commission granted the applications and issued spacing orders covering the drilling. Subsequently, the oil company filed applications for exceptions to the spacing orders, claiming that time, money, and labor would be saved if the exceptions were granted. The royalty association objected to the applications. The commission granted the exception applications and the association sought review. The court affirmed the orders. The court found that the commission did not err when it granted the applications in order to prevent economic waste and the drilling of unnecessary wells. The court said that there was substantial evidence that if additional drilling were required instead of permitting the oil company to use wells that were already drilled, the operator would sustain a loss. The court said that the oil company likely would not drill on the property if new wells were required because the cost of the wells would outweigh the profit to be made by recovering the oil. Also, the court said, the oil company would be able to recover more oil by using the existing wells.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's order granting the oil company's applications for location exceptions to previously issued spacing orders over the association's objection.

 

623 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Woody v. State Corp. Comm'n


Nos. 35684, 35821


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1954 OK 14; 265 P.2d 1102; 1954 Okla. LEXIS 413; 3 Oil & Gas Rep. 465



January 19, 1954 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant royalty owners sought review of an order of the State Corporation Commission (Oklahoma), which adjudicated the ratification of a former order. The two cases were consolidated for briefing and decision.


OVERVIEW: The royalty owners contended that the Commission's order was not sustained by substantial evidence and that the provision for the allocation of unit production under the 50/50 formula approved by the Commission deprived the owners of their property without due process of law and in violation of U.S. Const. amend. XIV and Okla. Const. art. II, § 7. The court noted that the law as applied to the unitized management of common sources of supply was governed by the Unitization Act of 1951, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 287.1 to 287.15 (1951). The court held that the fact that the act required notice to and consent of royalty owners on a comparable basis with lease owners placed the act beyond any challenge on constitutional grounds. The court affirmed the Commission's order because it found that it was sustained by substantial evidence and did not deprive the owners of any constitutional guarantees.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the Commission's order.

 

624 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State ex rel. Comm'rs of Land Office v. Keller


No. 35351


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 371; 264 P.2d 742; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 642



December 15, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants, the Oklahoma State Commissioners of the Land Office, challenged a decision from the District Court of Love County (Oklahoma), which, in appellee putative property owners' motion to set aside a prior judgment of foreclosure, sale, and confirmation rendered in favor of the Commissioners, granted the motion and set aside the prior judgment.


OVERVIEW: The debtors gave a note and mortgage on certain real estate to the Commissioners for a loan. Upon default, the Commissioners filed a foreclosure action, which also joined other inferior claimants, grantees of the debtors who purportedly acquired an interest during the pendency of the foreclosure proceedings. Some of the inferior claimants were not served. Later, the debtors filed a motion alleging that a money judgment previously entered against them by stipulation was with the proviso that no deficiency judgment was to be entered against them. A nunc pro tunc entry to that effect was issued, and the Commissioners filed a motion to modify the provision that excluded any deficiency judgment. The property was sold to the State. The trial court vacated the judgment, sale, and order of confirmation, but the court reversed. The Commissioners could proceed just against the parties served. The money judgment and foreclosure was a final determination of the rights and liabilities of the debtors and also valid and binding as to their grantees who undertook to acquire an interest in the land pendente lite. When unappealed, it was a final adjudication unassailable by collateral attack.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision with instructions to enter judgment for the Commissioners.

 

625 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


St. Louis-San Francisco Ry. Co. v. State


No. 34271


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 335; 268 P.2d 845; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 675; 2 P.U.R.3d 506



November 10, 1953 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 23, 1954. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied April 6, 1954.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant railway company sought review of an order of the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma requiring the company and its hospital association to furnish hospital facilities and medical services to injured or sick employees of the company employed by it in Oklahoma.


OVERVIEW: The hospital association was a corporation which was organized with the object of providing medical and surgical attention and hospitalization to its members who were also employees of the railway company. The hospital association was not made a party to the action in the trial court, and the court held that the association was entitled to notice and a hearing before the Commission prior to the promulgation of the order against it under Okla. Const. art. 9. § 18. Thus, the trial court's order against the association could not be sustained because the trial court did not have jurisdiction over the association. The court further held that Okla. Stat. tit. 17, §§ 111, 112, 113 requiring the railway company to furnish hospital facilities to its employees could not be construed as within the powers referred to in either Okla. Const. art. 9, §§ 18 or 19, and, therefore, the legislation was neither an alteration, amendment, revision or repeal of any of the provisions of Okla. Const. art. 9 §§ 18 to 34 as authorized under Okla. Const. art. 9, § 35 and therefore could not be constitutionally sustained.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the order of the Commission.

 

626 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 1 v. Williamson


No. 36071


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 306; 262 P.2d 701; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 570



October 27, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Independent School District No. 1 of Custer County sought a peremptory writ of mandamus against defendant Attorney General and the Bond Commissioner of the State of Oklahoma to compel his approval of bonds issued by the District. The Commissioner had refused approval.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioner had refused approval on the basis that, upon issuance as to a part of the school district, the debt would be in excess of 5 percent of the assessed valuation of the taxable property in violation of the Okla. Const. art. X, § 26. The debt upon issuance would be in excess of 5 percent only in part of the District that had been absorbed into the District as a result of annexation of another school district. Okla. Stat. tit. 70, § 7-3 (1951) provided, inter alia, that the district or districts to which a district was annexed were to assume a full proportion of all legal, bonded debt of the district annexed. Ergo, if § 7-3 were constitutional, then its application would prevent the debt from exceeding 5 percent in the case sub judice. The court stated that the annexed part was only a small part and that it would be ridiculous to say that, by its attachment to a larger and practically debt-free school district, it could prevent the latter from acquiring facilities necessary for the proper education of its children. Such a result was not the intention of the constitutional framers. The court held that paragraph A of § 7-3 was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court ordered that a peremptory writ of mandamus issue as prayed for by the District.

 

627 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Johnson v. Conley


No. 34973


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 222; 259 P.2d 1021; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 493



July 14, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, the former owners of certain property, appealed a judgment of a trial court (Oklahoma), which, after the close of the evidence, sustained the demurrer to plaintiffs' evidence by defendant, who acquired the property by tax resale deed. The issues were whether the resale deed was invalid because the tax resale included two annual assessments of $ 1 penalty assessed under an unconstitutional statute and included excess tax and interest.


OVERVIEW: The $ 1 penalty for each of two years was assessed under authority of 1933 Okla. Sess. Laws 115, § 3, which purportedly amended Okla. Stat. § 12582 (1931). On appeal, the court reviewed the title of 1925 Okla. Sess. Laws 282, which later became § 12582, and the title of 1933 Okla. Sess. Laws 115. 1933 Okla. Sess. Laws 115, § 3 extended the penalty for failure to list property for taxation by a stated time to every county in the state; otherwise its provisions were essentially the same as in the original act. The court rejected plaintiffs' argument that the subject matter of the original act was penalties in Oklahoma County and that only a penalty in Oklahoma County could be fixed in the act. Nor was it beyond the subject matter of the original act in violation of Okla. Const. art. V, § 57. In fact, it was specifically within its provisions. The court held that the act was constitutional and the $ 2 assessment was proper. As to the alleged improper inclusion of excess tax and interest in the tax resale, the court pointed out that the amounts at issue were a $ .02 overcharge on the tax and a miscalculated interest charge of $ .13. Such discrepancies would not vitiate the tax resale.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

628 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Seltzer v. Commissioners of Land Office


No. 35829


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


258 P.2d 1172; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 470



June 30, 1953 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant lessee and owner of improvements on state school land, challenged the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which sustained respondent state Land Commission's motion to dismiss the lessee's challenge against the Commission's decision to reject the purchase bid on sale of the state school land and allow the lessee to exercise his preferential right.


OVERVIEW: The question before the court was whether the Commissioners of the Land Office had the power to reject the highest bid made at the sale of public land where the bid was in excess of the appraised value and all other statutory requirements of the sale had been met. The lessee contended that the portion of Okla. Stat. tit. 64, § 82(a) authorizing the Commissioners of the Land Office to reject bids was unconstitutional because it was an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power contrary to Okla. Const. art. 4, § 1 that provided for the separation of powers. The Commissioners contended that their right to reject bids was an administrative rather than a legislative function and was simply a necessary part of their discretion over the sale of school lands. On appeal the court held that the power of the Commissioners of the Land Office over the sale of school lands was not vested in them by statute, but was originally given to them by Okla. Const. art. 6, § 32. Therefore, Okla. Stat. tit. 64, § 82(a) was not a delegation of any power that the Commissioners did not already have and the constitutional inhibition contained in Okla. Const. art. 4, § 1 did not apply.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the lower court that sustained the Land Commission's motion to dismiss the claim of the lessee of state school land.

 

629 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Indep. Sch. Dist. No. 65 v. Stafford


No. 35399


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 172; 208 Okla. 542; 257 P.2d 1092; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 843



June 2, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Wagoner County; E. G. Carroll, Judge.

Suit to recover damages for defendant's breach of written contract. Plaintiff had judgment, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant independent school district appealed a judgment of the District Court, Wagoner County (Oklahoma), which found in favor of plaintiff teacher in her action to recover damages for breach of a written employment contract. The independent school district also appealed the trial court's addition of interest to the jury verdict.


OVERVIEW: The teacher entered into an employment contract with a dependent school district, which was approved by the county superintendent. There were funds available to pay her salary. She began teaching, but her pupils were transferred to the independent school district. She reported to the independent school district, which advised her that her contract was void because no money was on hand to pay her when the contract was signed and no funds had been appropriated. The teacher sued for breach of contract, and she recovered a judgment. In affirming, the court held that the teacher introduced evidence to support her claim that she had entered into a valid and approved contract, that there were funds available at the time the agreement was approved, and that the contract was breached by the independent school district without justification. Consequently, the teacher was entitled to damages for breach of contract. Moreover, the nature of teacher's cause of action and the fact that her damages were capable of calculation justified the trial court's addition of interest to the recovery allowed by the jury.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

630 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Dobbs v. Bd. of County Com'Rs


No. 35947


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 159; 208 Okla. 514; 257 P.2d 802; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 827



May 26, 1953, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, county resident (resident), brought an action seeking a writ to prohibit defendant, County Commissioners of Oklahoma County, from appointing defendant judge as a second county judge, alleging that H.B. No. 646, 1953 Leg., (Okla. 1953), which authorized the appointment of a second county judge in counties with more than 300,000 residents, violated Okla. Const. art. VII, § 11 and as such, was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The resident argued that because Okla. Const. art. VII, §11 provided that "a" county judge was to be elected in each county and each reference to "a" county judge was in the singular, the legislature was prohibited from authorizing the appointment of two county judges in any particular county. The court disagreed and denied the resident's requested relief. The court explained that there was no express limitations in the Oklahoma Constitution placed upon the power of the legislature to enact a general law authorizing the appointment and election of two county judges in counties having a population in excess of 300,000. The court noted that every presumption was to be indulged in favor of the validity of a legislative act and that that presumption was to continue until its invalidity was made to appear beyond a doubt. The court overruled the decision in Nichols v. Levy, 151 Okla. 245, 1 P.2d 766, and held that H.B. No. 646, 1953 Leg., (Okla. 1953) was constitutional. As such, the court approved the acts of Commissioners in electing a second county judge.


OUTCOME: The court denied the resident's request for a writ to prohibit the Commissioners from appointing a second county judge in Oklahoma County.

 

631 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Chastain v. Okla. City


No. 35490


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 166; 208 Okla. 604; 258 P.2d 635; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 867



May 26, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Albert C. Hunt, Judge.

Suit by J. D. Chastain, as plaintiff, to enjoin the defendant, City of Oklahoma City, from enforcing city ordinance providing for sewer service charge because of alleged unconstitutionality. Defendant's demurrer to petition being sustained and plaintiff electing not to amend, cause was dismissed, from which judgment plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff homeowner brought an action to recover a sewer charge and to restrain defendant City from collecting future sewer charges on the grounds that a City ordinance establishing the sewer charge was unconstitutional. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) sustained the City's demurrer to the petition and dismissed the case. The homeowner appealed the judgment.


OVERVIEW: The homeowner sought a refund a City sewer charge and a restraining order prohibiting the collection of any future charges on the basis that the City ordinance levying the charge was unconstitutional because it was insufficient, it impaired the obligation of contract, and violated the provisions of Okla. Const. art. X, § 27 that required the passage of a tax by a vote to fund a public utility. On review, from an adverse decision, the court found that the ordinance did not deprive the homeowner of due process of law because it was a public utility that provided a service and the City could charge a reasonable amount for the service. The court also found the ordinance sufficient under Okla. Const. art. V, § 57 because it dealt with one general purpose and did not encompass tow different subjects. Lastly, the court found that there was impairment of contract because the homeowner's petition did not contain any allegation that a contract had existed with the City for sewer service. Moreover, the court held that a private individual could not acquire a private interest in the continued service of a public utility. The homeowner was not obligated to purchase the service.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

632 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


ATCHLEY v. BOARD OF BARBER EXAMINERS OF STATE


No. 35475


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 146; 208 Okla. 453; 257 P.2d 302; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 815



May 12, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; W. A. Carlile, Judge.

Action by Ralph Atchley against the Board of Barber Examiners of the State of Oklahoma and A. A. Pursley, Secretary, seeking injunction. Injunction denied, and plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, a barber and the operator of a barber shop, sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his request for an injunction to prevent defendants, the Board of Barber Examiners of the State of Oklahoma and its secretary, from proceeding against him by criminal complaint or in a civil action for the violation of rules promulgated by the Board pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 77 (1951).


OVERVIEW: The Board prescribed rules and regulations under the authority of § 77, which set forth sanitary requirements for barbershops. The secretary of the Board charged defendant with a violation of a rule. The barber sought an injunction to prevent the Board from proceeding against him by criminal complaint or in a civil action. The trial court denied his application. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court held that although § 77 had been repealed and although it was inserted by the code commission into a later compilation contrary to the provisions of the act creating the commission and authorizing the compilation, it was legally re-enacted and became operative when the legislature adopted the 1941 statutes. Section 77 was not an unconstitutional delegation of legislative power. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 59, § 61 et seq. (1951), the legislature declared a policy of regulating the practice of barbering to avoid the spread of disease. Having declared the policy and purpose and provided standards for the exercise of the power, the legislature could confer upon the Board the power to enact rules and regulations to promote the purpose of the law and to carry it into effect.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment for the Board and its secretary and denying the barber's application for an injunction.

 

633 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Rice v. State Bd. of Med. Examiners


No. 35622


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 143; 208 Okla. 440; 257 P.2d 292; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 812



May 12, 1953, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Marshall County; W. J. Monroe, Judge.

Action to enjoin defendant from alleged illegal practice of medicine. From trial court's order directing defendant's production of records in response to plaintiff's subpoena duces tecum, the defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff state board of medical examiners brought an action in the District Court of Marshall County (Oklahoma) seeking to enjoin defendant physician from unlawfully practicing medicine without a license under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 491-492, and §§ 731.1-731.6 (1951). The trial court denied the physician's motion to quash a subpoena duces tecum seeking a list of his patients. The physician appealed.


OVERVIEW: The medical board sought the physician's patent records in order to prove that he was practicing medicine without a license. The physician resisted the subpoena on the grounds that he would be forced to incriminate himself. On review from an order denying his motion to quash, the physician argued that that enforcement of the subpoena violated Okla. Const. art. 2, § 21. The court agreed with his reasoning, rejecting the medical board's argument that no pending criminal charge was pending and that the privilege against self-incrimination did not apply. The court reasoned that the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 491, 500 and 731.4 (1951) were penal in nature and that it had a duty to protect the constitutional rights of the state's citizens from modern tendencies to abrogate individual rights on the ground that exigent circumstances required it. The court reasoned that the subpoena was nothing more that an attempt to work a compulsory production of the physician's records into court in order that they could be used in evidence against him.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed with directions to sustain the physician's motion to quash.

Garr v. Collins


No. 35403


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1953 OK 46; 208 Okla. 113; 253 P.2d 838; 1953 Okla. LEXIS 723



February 17, 1953, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Award sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner employer appealed a decision of the State Industrial Commission (Oklahoma), which modified a trial commissioner's ruling and awarded workmen's compensation benefits to respondent employee, finding that, at the time of an accident, he was acting within the scope of his employment. The issues included whether the employee was engaged in a hazardous employment and whether his injury arose out of and in the course of his employment.


OVERVIEW: Having been asked to come to work on a Sunday, the employee was helping a foreman in starting a truck. To do that, the truck had to be pulled by a tractor, but the air in one of its tires was low. Nevertheless, they got the truck started. Then, the employee brought the tractor into a garage on the premises to fill the tire, which was one of his general duties anyway. He also decided to fill the tires on his own car. In the process of maneuvering the hose on the compressor, he caught his hand and amputated parts of two fingers. On appeal, the employee conceded that his employment was not defined as hazardous under the Workmen's Compensation Law. But, the employer stipulated that that he carried compensation insurance for his employees, including respondent. The court pointed out that Okla. Stat. tit. 85, § 65.2 (1951), which the employee argued estopped the employer from denying that the employee was engaged in a hazardous employment at the time he sustained his injury, had been held to be not unconstitutional. Further, the court held that the evidence taken as a whole was sufficient to sustain the finding that the employee's injury arose out of and in the course of his employment.


OUTCOME: The court sustained the award.

Jenkins v. Frederick


No. 35360


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 456; 208 Okla. 583; 257 P.2d 1058; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 915; 2 Oil & Gas Rep. 1289



December 16, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 17, 1953. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied June 17, 1953. As Corrected June 18, 1953.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Horace D. Ballaine, Judge.

Action to quiet title to real estate commenced by one who held a deed from the holder of a resale tax deed. Defendant was owner of an undivided one-half interest in the minerals acquired by deed from former owner. Judgment for defendant as to her claimed interest and in favor of plaintiff as against all other defendants. Plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual, who held a deed from the holder of a resale tax deed, sought review of a decision from the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which entered judgment in favor of appellee, a mineral rights claimant who asserted that she was the owner of an undivided one-half interest in minerals acquired by deed from a former owner. The trial court had entered judgment for the mineral rights claimant as to her alleged interest.


OVERVIEW: The individual had filed his petition against a county treasurer, the board of county commissioners, and several other defendants, including the mineral rights claimant, asserting that the parties claimed some right, title, or interest in a section of land in Tulsa county. He argued that he was the owner of the legal title in fee simple and in possession of the real estate. Judgment was rendered for the individual quieting his title as against all defendants except the mineral rights claimant. Judgment was in her favor, quieting her title to an undivided one-half interest in and to all oil, gas, and other minerals in and under the real property. The individual argued that the judgment was contrary to the evidence and the law. The court held that the individual was in possession of the property at all times after his deed was recorded and for more than five years before the mineral rights claimant attempted to attack the validity of his deed. Further, the court held that the individual's possession under his resale tax deed was possession of the entire property including the nonproducing minerals.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court was reversed with directions to enter judgment for the individual quieting his title to the involved real property.

Lockett v. Constr. Trades Union A. F. of L.


No. 35163


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 429; 207 Okla. 484; 250 P.2d 468; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 833; 31 L.R.R.M. 2178; 22 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P67,276



November 25, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Cleveland County; Tom P. Pace, Judge.

Action by plaintiff, Lloyd Lockett, against Construction Trades Union A.F. of L., and others, for an injunction, whereby plaintiff sought to enjoin defendants picketing a building site. From the judgment denying injunction relief, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In his action against defendant construction trade union and others for an injunction to prohibit the picketing of his building site, plaintiff building owner appealed a judgment of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma) denying injunction relief.


OVERVIEW: The building owner contended on appeal that the union's picketing was unlawful because the union was engaged in a secondary boycott, and the picketing was carried on for the purpose of coercing the building owner to breach his contract with third parties. The building owner further contended that Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 166 (1951) was unconstitutional and, even though constitutional, did not protect the union members in their unlawful activities.The court found that the evidence conclusively disclosed that the picketing was not carried on upon the building owner's premises and was accomplished without any physical force or violence whatsoever. The court held that the trial court's findings that a labor dispute existed between the building owner, contractor, and the union at the time the building was picketed, that no force or violence was employed in such picketing, and that no secondary boycott was established were amply supported by the record. The court concluded that the injunction was properly denied.

637 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


E. G. Nicholas Const. Co. v. State Indus. Comm'n


No. 35314


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 398; 207 Okla. 428; 250 P.2d 221; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 818



November 12, 1952, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Award vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action to review a death benefit award, petitioners, an employer and its insurance carrier, sought review of a decision from respondent State Industrial Commission of Oklahoma, which awarded the claimant for the death by heatstroke of her son. Petitioners argued that there was no evidence that the decedent's death resulted from an accidental injury arising out of the employment and that a certain Congressional bill was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: The employer, engaged in building a filling station, employed the decedent to shovel gravel and push it to a concrete mixer. The decedent complained several times to the foreman and fellow employees that he was feeling sick and hot and eventually wobbled and fell. The decedent was dead on arrival to the hospital and the doctor, who examined the decedent at the hospital, diagnosed the cause of death as a heatstroke. The claimant, as mother and sole dependent of decedent, filed for and was awarded death benefit compensation by the Commission. With respect to the contention that the injury did not result out of or in the course of employment, the court stated that there was no reliable evidence that the location of the decedent's work exposed him to danger of heatstroke in a greater degree than the general public was exposed from climatic conditions and that it was necessary that some connection between his employment and his injury be proved. The court rejected the contention that a certain Congressional bill was violative of the Due Process Clauses of the state and federal constitutions because there were no heirs or other persons who could be affected by the award.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the award of the Commission and remanded.

 

638 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bd. of County Comm'rs v. Stokes


No. 35001


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 270; 207 Okla. 37; 247 P.2d 526; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 704



July 29, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Eben L. Taylor, Judge.

Appeal from an action wherein a writ of mandamus was granted to compel allowance and payment of the salary of an elected county official.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant county commissioners sought review of the judgment of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), that granted a writ of mandamus to compel the allowance and payment of the salary of appellee elected county official.


OVERVIEW: The official was elected county clerk. His salary was based on the county population and valuation under the 1940 federal census. The official argued that after the 1950 census, his salary was payable under Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 180.42b (1947). The court found that the statute made no reference to any decennial federal census, but was applicable to all counties having a population in excess of 200,000; and provided that county clerks in all such counties should be paid $ 6,000 per year, payable monthly. The court held that the additional amount of work in offices in counties of such large population constituted a good reason and was a reasonable basis for creating larger salaries than was provided for counties of smaller population. When a comparison was made as to salaries paid in other counties coming within the lower population brackets, the court found nothing to indicate that such a classification was arbitrary or unjust; and, as a general law, it operated uniformly throughout the state and was not violative of the provisions of Okla. Const. art. 5, § 59. The writ directing the county to pay the increase was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment granted the writ of mandamus.

 

639 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Swanda v. Swanda


No. 35105


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 268; 207 Okla. 186; 248 P.2d 575; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 719



July 23, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 30, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Caddo County; L. A. Wood, Judge.

Action to recover community property. From an adverse judgment, defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant, decedent's son by a former marriage, appealed a judgment of the District Court, Caddo County (Oklahoma), which was rendered in favor of plaintiff widow in the widow's action to recover community property under the provisions of the Community Property Law of 1945, Okla. Stat. tit. 32, §§ 66-82 (1951).


OVERVIEW: Following her husband's death, the widow received the marital home but the remainder of the estate was given to the decedent's children from a former marriage. The widow filed a petition in which she alleged that the personal property in the estate was accumulated by her joint efforts with her husband during coverture and that she was the owner of an undivided half interest in the personal property and entitled to possession and control thereof. The trial court rendered judgment in favor of the widow. Decedent's son appealed, denied that there was any partnership or community property, and claimed that all of the property at issue was the separate property of the decedent. The court held that in the absence of a statute to the contrary, community property included all property acquired by either spouse during marriage and the fruits and profits of the separate property of either spouse. The court affirmed the judgment. The court found that the trial court carefully divided the property and declared only the property that was acquired by joint effort and industry of the widow and the decedent to be community property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Capitol Steel & Iron Co. v. Fuller


No. 35301


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 209; 206 Okla. 638; 245 P.2d 1134; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 663



May 20, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 8, 1952.



DISPOSITION: Award vacated.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and its surety, sought review of a judgment by the State Industrial Commission (Oklahoma), which entered an award of death benefits in favor of respondents, a widow and three descendants, following the death of the decedent as a result of a work-related injury.


OVERVIEW: While engaged in work for the employer, the decedent died as a result of two railway cars coming together. The commission found the decedent's widow, as well as three of the decedent's descendants, eligible for the death benefits under the Oklahoma Workers' Compensation Law. On review, the court vacated the award. The court found that, while death benefits were recoverable under 1951 Okla. Sess. Laws 312, the commission erred in awarding benefits to any person other than the decedent's widow. The court held that the evidence established that the decedent's widow was the only person named in the award who was actually a dependent of the decedent. Thus, the court held that the entire award was payable to the widow.


OUTCOME: The court vacated the award.

State ex rel. Whetsel v. Wood


No. 34934


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 175; 207 Okla. 193; 248 P.2d 612; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 730; 34 A.L.R.2d 1321



April 23, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 7, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Pittsburg County; W. A. Lackey, Judge.

Action by State of Oklahoma ex rel. Fred W. Whetsel, County Attorney of Pittsburg County, against Thomas S. Wood, Jr., for permanent injunction under the Watchmaking Act of 1945. Judgment for defendant, and plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county attorney challenged an order from the District Court, Pittsburg County (Oklahoma), which sustained defendant individual's demurrer to the county attorney's action for permanent injunction on the ground that the Watchmaking Act of 1945, Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 771-782 (1951), was unconstitutional and void.


OVERVIEW: A county attorney sought a permanent injunction restraining an individual from practicing watchmaking in Oklahoma without first having obtained a license or certificate of registration as a watchmaker from the Oklahoma Board of Examiners in Watchmaking under the Watchmaking Act of 1945 (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 771-782 (1951). The individual filed a demurrer to the petition on the basis that the attorney had no legal capacity to sue, and that the Act was unconstitutional. The trial court sustained the demurrer on the ground that the Act was unconstitutional and void. On appeal, the judgment was affirmed. The court held that the Act prohibited one who might be fully qualified by years of training and experience from following his chosen craft and forced him to seek some other work or trade, thus depriving him of the fruits of his own industry as guaranteed by Okla. Const. art. II, § 2. The court concluded that the Act vested in the Board powers to make rules and regulations that might deny some citizens their inherent right to earn their livelihood in a private field of work, and thus deprived them of a valuable property right without due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.
