City of Guthrie v. Pike & Long


No. 34871


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 158; 206 Okla. 307; 243 P.2d 697; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 587



April 15, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Logan County; Henry W. Hoel, Judge.

Action brought by Pike & Long, a copartnership, against the City of Guthrie to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance purporting to regulate the business of plaintiffs. The trial court granted a permanent injunction, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city appealed the judgment of the Logan County District Court (Oklahoma), which granted a permanent injunction in favor of plaintiff partnership in the partnership's action to enjoin the enforcement of an ordinance purporting to regulate their business.


OVERVIEW: The partnership operated a general merchandise store in which they sold merchandise acquired by them at receiver's sales or other such sales. The city passed an ordinance purporting to regulate their business but which, in effect, prohibited the further conducting of their business. A trial court rendered judgment for the partnership and enjoined the city from enforcing the ordinance against them. On appeal, the court affirmed and held that that the ordinance was passed solely for the purpose of forcing the partnership to close their place of business, by placing restrictions with which they could not possibly comply and by saddling them with large and unnecessary license payments. This was done solely for the benefit of their competitors. The ordinance was violative of the partnership's constitutional rights of plaintiffs, and was arbitrary and discriminatory, and the issuing of the injunction against its enforcement was fully sustained by the evidence. No defrauded customer was produced as a witness, nor was there any complaint by the taxing authorities, but the only persons who testified on behalf of the ordinance were competing retail merchants.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment in favor of the partnership.

 

643 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Parkes v. Natural Gas Pipe Line Co. of Am.


No. 34392


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 157; 207 Okla. 91; 249 P.2d 462; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 774; 1 Oil & Gas Rep. 1718



April 8, 1952, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Texas County; F. Hiner Dale, Judge.

Action to condemn lands in Texas county, Oklahoma, for natural gas pipe line purposes under Federal Natural Gas Act (Tit. 15 U.S.C.A. §§ 717-717w). Judgment for plaintiff, and defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant landowners appealed a decision from the District Court of Texas County (Oklahoma), which granted judgment to plaintiff natural gas company in its claims to condemn part of the landowners' real property for the construction of a natural gas pipeline under the authority of the Natural Gas Act, 15 U.S.C.S. §§ 717-717w.


OVERVIEW: The landowners opposed the company's condemnation proceeding on the grounds that the Natural Gas Act violated the Fifth Amendment and Okla. Const. art. II, § 23 and that the company had failed to comply with the state's eminent domain requirements, the Production and Transportation Act of 1913 (Transport Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 24 (1951). The trial court held that the Natural Gas Act was constitutional and that the company's permit from the Federal Powers Commission rendered compliance with the Transport Act unnecessary. On appeal, the court affirmed. The company was not a common carrier and had not tried to comply with the Transport Act by applying to the state agency. Congress's power to grant eminent domain powers to private corporations for public uses was well established. The court deferred to Congress's interpretation of "public use." The Natural Gas Act was constitutional. The Natural Gas Act did not require additional compliance measures, such as the Transport Act, from the company for each state affected by the pipeline. The company was not required to fulfil the state requirement of becoming a common carrier before it proceeded against the landowners' property.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the district court's order that permitted the company to condemn the landowners' property under the Act.

 

644 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Romang v. Cordell


No. 35395


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 139; 206 Okla. 369; 243 P.2d 677; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 584



April 1, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 23, 1952.



DISPOSITION: Writ denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner state representative sought a writ of mandamus directing respondent Secretary of the Election Board of the State of Oklahoma to refuse to accept and file certain notifications and declarations of candidacy for nomination and election as members of the Oklahoma House of Representatives due to the alleged invalidity and unconstitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 14 §§ 93-96 (1951) (Act), an apportionment act.


OVERVIEW: The purpose of the Act, among other things, was to provide for legislative apportionment, establish legislative districts and boundaries thereof, and designate the number of representatives for each county in the State. The representative argued that the Act violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 10 by depriving persons in certain counties of equal representation under the apportionment set forth in the Act. The court agreed but refused to grant the writ of mandamus on the grounds that it lacked authority to do so under the doctrine of separation of powers. The court reasoned that, although Okla. Const. art. V, § 10(j) granted to the court the power to review rules and regulations promulgated by the legislature in connection with apportionment actions, it did not permit the court to revise and change the districts as fixed by the legislature. The court further concluded that it would not exercise its authority to grant writs, under Okla. Const. art. VII, § 2, to command another branch of government to perform an action that could likely increase the inequality of the representation that was already in existence.


OUTCOME: The court denied the representative's application for a writ of mandamus ordering the Secretary to refuse to accept and file notifications and declarations of candidacy.

 

645 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Fortinberry Co. v. Blundell


No. 34503


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1952 OK 80; 206 Okla. 261; 242 P.2d 427; 1952 Okla. LEXIS 545



February 26, 1952, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 1, 1952.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, corporation and bank, filed a motion for a writ of mandamus requiring that defendants, State Budget Director, State Treasurer, State Auditor, and the Oklahoma Tax Commission, approve plaintiffs' claim to issue and deliver to the bank a warrant thereon, drawn upon the fund in the hands of the treasurer, which was collected by the commission, and requiring the treasurer to pay the warrant out of the fund.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiffs filed a motion for a writ of mandamus requiring that defendants approve plaintiffs' claim to issue and deliver to the bank a warrant thereon, drawn upon the fund in the hands of the treasurer, which was collected by the commission and requiring the treasurer to pay the warrant out of the fund. The court concluded that the corporation had a right to prosecute the action. Further, the court held that it was equally clear that the bank, as pledgee and assignee of the claim, with the agreement of the commission to pay to the bank any moneys due under the contract, could maintain the action in its own name without regard to the power of its co-plaintiff. Thus, the court held that the accrued right of plaintiffs could not be defeated by an attempt to repeal the law under which the claim arose, and which law made ample provision for its payment. It was also found that no reason was shown why the commission declined to accept and pay for the parts as issue according to its agreement. The court held that only the State failed to perform its lawful and valid agreement. Therefore, the court granted the writ of mandamus.


OUTCOME: The court ordered and decreed that a writ of mandamus issue commanding and requiring that the treasurer reinstate the "General Enforcement Fund", and that the commission deposit therein 10 per cent of its collections, requiring the director to approve the claim, requiring the auditor to issue a warrant thereon and deliver the same to the bank, and requiring the treasurer to pay the warrant out of the General Enforcement Fund.

Battles v. State ex rel. Okla. Comm'n ex rel. Crippled Children


No. 34996


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 313; 206 Okla. 444; 244 P.2d 320; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 762



November 20, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 13, 1952.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Muskogee County; E. G. Carroll, Judge.

Defendants have appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Muskogee County, Oklahoma, whereby, upon application of the State of Oklahoma ex rel. Oklahoma Commission for Crippled Children, as plaintiff, a writ of mandamus was ordered issued, directing the County Excise Board of Muskogee County, Oklahoma, and the members thereof, as defendants, to comply with the provisions of section 172.13 of Title 10 O.S. 1949 Supp.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded, with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant Muskogee County Excise Board (Oklahoma) challenged an order of the District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma), which issued a writ of mandamus requiring the Board to comply with the provisions of the Crippled Children's Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 172.1 through 172.16 (Supp. 1949), relative to the appropriation of revenue from ad valorem taxes to plaintiff Oklahoma Commission for Crippled Children.


OVERVIEW: The Board contended that the Crippled Children's Act was in conflict with the Oklahoma Constitution. While the Commission urged that the question of the constitutionality of the Act was not properly presented for determination, the court held that it was a public question in which confusion could occur in the making of levies for subsequent years. Therefore, it was appropriate for the court to express its view. The court opined that resolution of the issue depended upon the authority of the legislature to apportion funds of the Board to the specific purposes of the Act. The court found that the primary purpose of enacting Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 172.13 (Supp. 1941) was to require counties to provide a fund that the Commission could use for reimbursement of expenditures or for expense of a patient's care and treatment in a state institution until the county funds became exhausted. The court held that the legislature was precluded from imposing that burden by Okla. Const. art. XXI. Further, as a result of the obnoxious portion of the Act, the entire act was unconstitutional and void.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded the matter with directions for the trial court to enter judgment for the Board and to recall the writ in mandamus.

Spiers v. Magnolia Petro. Co.

Supreme Court of Oklahoma

DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner landowner appealed from the order of the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma, which granted the petition of respondents, two oil companies, over the landowner's protest. OVERVIEW: The oil companies requested that the Commission make the necessary findings and enter an order that created the sand unit, defined the unit area of said unit and prescribing the plan of unitization applicable thereto, upon such terms and conditions as were fair, reasonable, and equitable and which were necessary or proper to protect, safeguard, and adjust the respective rights and obligations of the several persons affected, including royalties, oil and gas payments, carried interests, mortgagors, lien claimants and others, as well as the lessees. The Commission's order created the unit, approved the area outlined by the oil companies' map, and approved their plan. Supreme Court of Oklahoma

October 23, 1951, Decided

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from an order of the Corporation Commission creating the Chit-Wood Cunningham Sand Unit and adopting a plan of unitization applicable thereto. Grounds of appeal are insufficiency of evidence to support the order and that the Unitization Act is unconstitutional.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff in error, an owner of land, filed a protest to challenge an order of the Corporation Commission of the State of Oklahoma that granted a petition filed by defendant in error petroleum company pursuant to the Oklahoma Unitization Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 286.1 - .17 (1941) for the creation of a unit area that included part of the owner's land and that adopted a compulsory plan of unitization for the unit area.


OVERVIEW: The petroleum company was the lessee of record for 99.02 percent of the total area of the common source of supply. Half of the owner's land was within the unit area and half was outside it. He contended that the proposed plan was unfair and unjust, that it violated the terms of his lease, that the petition did not reflect facts sufficient to justify unitization of his land, and that the Act was unconstitutional. The court refused to substitute its notion of expediency and fairness for that of the Commission. The court held that the arguments raised by the owner pertaining to the Act's constitutionality had been carefully considered in two other recent cases and that it found no reason to depart from its prior holdings that the Act was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order.

Starner v. Okla. City


No. 34497


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 253; 205 Okla. 170; 236 P.2d 479; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 611



October 9, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Clarence M. Mills, Judge.

Action by Roy W. Starner and Mollie Starner against the City Council of Oklahoma City and the City Engineer to enjoin the establishing and construction of a limited access highway and the inclusion of their property within the assessment district. The trial court sustained a demurrer to the plaintiff's petition, and plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs landowners sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which dismissed their action against defendants, the city and the city engineer, which sought to enjoin further proceedings in the establishment of a limited access facility in the city.


OVERVIEW: The landowners asserted that the city council had adopted a resolution purporting to establish a limited access facility and that the payment for the facility would be assessed against a district in which the landowners resided. The landowners questioned the need for the facility and whether it was a local improvement. The trial court sustained the demurrer and dismissed the action. The court agreed that the landowners' action was premature until a necessity resolution had been adopted, as required by Okla. Stat. tit. 69, § 11.9 (Supp. 1949). The court explained that after such a resolution was adopted, a stay of further action could be obtained by the residents of the area that could cause the city to abandon the project. The court stated that the landowners' objections could only become material in case no protest was filed when the resolution of necessity was published, or, if a protest was filed, that the same should be denied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that dismissed the landowners' suit.

Anderson-Prichard Oil Corp. v. Corp. Comm'n


No. 34283


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 234; 205 Okla. 672; 241 P.2d 363; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 752; 1 Oil & Gas Rep. 391



October 2, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 23, 1951. Application for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied November 6, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal by Anderson-Prichard Oil Corporation from an order of the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma fixing the western boundary line of the productive area of the Pooler zone in the Chickasha gas field so as to give Anderson-Prichard only 57 acres as an acreage factor in the allocation formula of gas in lieu of the 160 acres covered by Anderson-Prichard lease.



DISPOSITION: Order affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant oil company challenged the decision from appellee the Oklahoma Corporation Commission, which entered an order against the oil company in its application for an amendment of another order to use an acreage factor of 160 acres to determine the amount of gas production from a field. The Commission determined that the acreage factor was 67 acres.


OVERVIEW: Three zones were producing gas through one well. The Commission entered its original order to allocate gas production and prevent waste. The oil company's lease was for the entire 160-acre area. The Commission used 57 acres upon the reasoning that only productive acres could be considered in the acreage factor. The oil company also sought by its application for an amended order to extend its boundary to include the 160 acres. The appellate court affirmed. The Commission had the full authority to enter orders to only allow for limited production in order to avoid waste and protect all producers. The acreage factor was a reasonable means of determining production. The oil company's leasehold rights did not trump the statutory powers of the Commission. After determining the rights of the Commission, the court found that there was substantial evidence to use only 57 productive acres in determine the acreage factor based largely on oil and gas experts. Further, the oil company's due process rights were not violated. The police powers of the State allowed it, through the Commission, to regulate the oil and gas supply without violating due process.


OUTCOME: The order of the Commission was affirmed.

Williams v. Dickey


No. 34548


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 159; 204 Okla. 629; 232 P.2d 637; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 532



May 29, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 19, 1951.

Action by C. Roy Williams, plaintiff, for an injunction against Donald F. Dickey, Joe M. Beaver, and M. G. Young, in their capacities as members of the State Insurance Board of the State of Oklahoma, to restrain them from revoking his license to sell life insurance. Injunction denied, and plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff appealed the decision in the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) denying his petition for an injunction to restrain defendants, in their capacities as members of the state insurance board, from revoking his license to sell life insurance.


OVERVIEW: Defendants initially issued a license to sell insurance to plaintiff upon plaintiff's application through his employer, a company duly licensed to sell life insurance in the state. Some months later defendants issued a show cause order why plaintiff's license should not be revoked because of false answers on his application. After a hearing, defendants revoked plaintiff's license. Plaintiff gave false answers in his application for a license to sell insurance in regard to the particulars of his earlier experience as an agent, the refusal and suspension of his license in other states, and his conviction of four felonies. Plaintiff appealed defendants' revocation. The court held that the insurance board would have had the right to refuse the plaintiff a license to sell insurance at the time his application was submitted if it had been given the true facts. Because of plaintiff's fraud and misrepresentation disclosed in the record, the license was improperly issued, and the court affirmed the revocation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendants' decision to revoke the license because the state had the power to revoke licenses obtained by fraud and misrepresentation.

 

652 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Adams v. Fry


No. 35014


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 127; 204 Okla. 407; 230 P.2d 915; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 495



May 1, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff judges sought a writ of mandamus to require defendant court clerks to pay additional judicial salary from the court funds.


OVERVIEW: The additional payment to judges in larger counties and cities, Okla. Stat. tit. 74, § 251b (Supp. 1947) was amended to alter the size requirements. The statute provided that judges who were in judicial districts with a population in excess of 250,000 and a city with a population of more than 200,000 would receive an additional $ 4000 compensation. For districts with a population of more than 200,000 and less than 250,000 and cities with more than 100,000 but less than 200,000, a judge was to receive $ 3000. The judges served in a district with a population of more than 250,000 but a city of less than 200,000, so that the district did not fall within either classification as § 251v was written. The court held that § 250.3 was incomplete because it did not refer to the supplemental salary. The court held that this was a violation of Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57. The court determined that to read § 251b literally would destroy the intention of the legislature. The court held that the judges should be paid the supplemental amounts.


OUTCOME: The court granted the writ.

 

653 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sewer Improvement Dist. No. 1 v. Foster


No. 34897


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 107; 205 Okla. 201; 236 P.2d 678; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 622



April 10, 1951, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 10, 1951. Second Petition for Rehearing Denied September 25, 1951.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Horace D. Ballaine, Judge.

Action by Jack Foster and others against Sewer Improvement District No. 1, Tulsa County, Oklahoma, M. D. Ator and others as members of the board of directors. Judgment for plaintiffs, and defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant city challenged a judgment from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which found that Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 871 (Supp. 1949) was unconstitutional. Plaintiff landowners were not required to pay the assessment against their property.


OVERVIEW: The city annexed the landowners' property and, as a result, the annexed property became part of certain public improvement districts. The landowners did not sign the annexation petition, but their property was assessed. The landowners instituted suit against the city, arguing that they were denied due process of law because they did not have an opportunity to contest the assessments. The district court agreed and found § 871 unconstitutional. On appeal, the court affirmed. Under Okla. Stat. tit. 19, § 872.1 (Supp. 1949), an annexed territory for all purposes became a part of the original sewer improvement district and assumed its full proportion of all liabilities of the district. The annexation statute did not provide for notice and an opportunity to be heard. The court concluded that, to the extent of the burden imposed, the statute deprived a nonconsenting landowner of his property. Due process of law contemplated that such owner be given notice and opportunity to be heard on the question of whether the construction would benefit his land. The annexation statute was repugnant to due process, and the order of annexation made under authority of the statute was void.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

654 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Palmer Oil Corp. v. Phillips Petro. Co.


Nos. 33336, 33708


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 78; 204 Okla. 543; 231 P.2d 997; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 517



March 20, 1951 


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Petitions for Rehearing Denied May 22, 1951. Applications for Leave to File Second Petition for Rehearing Denied June 5, 1951.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, owners of interests in certain oilfields with a common source, appealed an order of respondent state corporation commission providing for the unitized management and operation of the oil fields pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 286.1-286.17 (1945). Petitioners filed an action against the commission seeking a writ of prohibition forbidding it from exercising further jurisdiction in connection with the unitization of the oil fields.


OVERVIEW: Petitioners claimed that the Unitization Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 52, §§ 286.1-286.17 (1945), was unconstitutional and that the commission's order providing for unitization of their oil fields was unlawful. They claimed that the act was unreasonable because it did not require as a condition to the establishment of a unit a finding by the commission that, for the purpose of conservation, the application of the act would be more effective than that of the existing laws. They also claimed that it was an unlawful delegation of legislative power. The court upheld the commission's order. The court ruled that (1) the challenge to the reasonableness of the act was in fact a challenge to the legislature's decision on a matter of policy and was outside the scope of judicial inquiry; (2) there was no delegation of legislative power to the commission; (3) the act did not violate the Equal Protection Clause in treating lessees and royalty owners differently; and (4) the commission's conclusions were not contrary to the weight of the evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the commission's order providing for unitized management of the oil fields and denied the application for a writ of prohibition.

Adwon v. Okla. Retail Grocers Ass'n


No. 34707


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 43; 204 Okla. 199; 228 P.2d 376; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 419



February 27, 1951, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Glen O. Morris, Judge.

Action by Oklahoma Retail Grocers Association against Earnest Adwon, d/b/a Earnest Adwon Grocery, to enjoin violations of the Unfair Sales Act. The trial court overruled the demurrer of defendant to plaintiff's petition, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant grocer appealed an order from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which overruled its demurrer to plaintiff association's petition. The association brought an action to enforce compliance by the grocer with the provisions of the Unfair Sales Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 598 (Supp. 1949). After overruling the demurrer, the trial court granted the association a temporary injunction.


OVERVIEW: The association represented the Oklahoma retail grocers. The association claimed that the grocer sold items of merchandise for less than cost. The association asserted that the grocer's acts were done with the intent and purpose of impairing and preventing fair competition. Affirming, the court held that the trial court properly overruled the demurrer, which alleged that the petition failed to state a claim because the act was unconstitutional. The court ruled that the act was enacted under the state's police power and that the legislature was primarily the judge of the necessity of the enactment. Further, the court ruled that every possible presumption was in favor of the act's validity, even if the court held views that were inconsistent with the act. Further, the court held that the act was considered constitutional unless it involved a palpable abuse of power and lack of reasonableness to accomplish the law. The court found that the grocer failed to prove that any portion of the act was unconstitutional. Therefore, the trial court correctly overruled the demurrer.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

656 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Nat'l Bank of Tulsa Bldg. v. Goldsmith


No. 33439


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1951 OK 5; 204 Okla. 45; 226 P.2d 916; 1951 Okla. LEXIS 389



January 16, 1951, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Sustained.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioners, an employer and an insurance carrier, sought review of a judgment of a trial court (Oklahoma) that found in favor of respondent employee in a personal injury action.


OVERVIEW: Respondent employee was injured on the job. Petitioner employer had obtained a policy of insurance covering liability of the employer under the Workmen's Compensation Law (Act). Respondent's employment was considered or used in determining amount of premiums paid and received under the policy. The policy was in effect in May 1947, when the legislature enacted Okla. Stat. tit. 85, §§ 65.1-65.4 (Supp. 1947). Petitioner contended the Act was unconstitutional and void in that it impaired its right and liberty to enter into lawful contracts of insurance and indemnity; it attempted to impose obligations on the basis of a classification that was unreasonable and arbitrary; and it violated rights guaranteed by the "equal protection and due process" clauses of the State and Federal Constitutions. The court affirmed the award, holding that the Act did not violate constitutional guarantees against impairment of contract, and did not create obligations that were unassumed. As to respondent insurance carrier, the court held it was within the power of the legislature to provide for enforcement of a contract voluntarily entered into and assumed by respondent as an insurance carrier.


OUTCOME: The judgment was sustained on the ground that it was within the power of the state in legislative enactment to provide for the enforcement of the contract and obligation voluntarily entered into and assumed by an insurance carrier. The Workmen's Compensation Law (Act) left to the injured employee the choice of whether to accept or reject the provisions of the Act, and there was no transgression of constitutional rights.

In re Okla. Tpk. Auth.


No. 34736


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 208; 203 Okla. 335; 221 P.2d 795; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 612



July 21, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied July 27, 1950.



DISPOSITION: Bonds approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Applicant Oklahoma Turnpike Authority sought to issue certain turnpike revenue bonds pursuant to its mandate under the Oklahoma Turnpike Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 69, § 659 (Supp. 1949), and numerous protestors, including a county board, city board of education, and others, objected to the issuance of the bonds.


OVERVIEW: The Authority decided to issue the bonds after holding hearings giving the protestors an opportunity to be heard. The protestors attacked numerous aspects of the validity of the bond issue and the underlying statutes authorizing the Authority and authorizing the bond issue. The court found that: (1) the Authority had been legally created with valid delegation of powers to carry out and perform its duties, including issuing the bonds for the toll road, and did not violate the state constitution; (2) the proposed bond issue was legally and properly authorized; (3) legal and valid notice of the application had been given and the parties had been fully heard on their grounds of protest; (4) the bonds would constitute valid obligations under their terms; and (5) the issuance of the bonds was proper.


OUTCOME: The court found in favor of the Authority and approved the bond issue.

 

658 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Town of Ames v. Wybrant


No. 34666


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 197; 203 Okla. 307; 220 P.2d 693; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 603



July 14, 1950, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Application Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowners filed an application with the court to assume original jurisdiction and award a writ of prohibition against defendants, the judge of the District Court of Major County, Oklahoma, and a city, enjoining further proceedings in four condemnation proceedings by the city against the landowners in the district court.


OVERVIEW: The judge declined to pass upon the merits of the landowners' motion to dismiss until his appointed commissioners had viewed and appraised the premises. The landowners argued that, under Okla. Stat. tit. 66, § 53 (1941), the city intended to take possession of the premises upon the report of the commissioners, thereby depriving them of their property without a day in court. The court held that: (1) § 53, which dealt with condemnation damages, could have no application where the power to condemn did not exist, or where it was sought to be exercised in excess of the power that obtained; (2) the establishment of the right to condemn was a prerequisite to any right of possession by the condemnor; (3) the landowners were entitled to challenge the right to condemn and have that question judicially determined prior to the final determination of the award for compensation and damages; and (4) such judicial determination was not proper until the matter of the condemnation was brought before the trial court by objection to the report of the commissioners because, until that point, the functions of the judge in the appointment of commissioners were ministerial and not judicial.


OUTCOME: The court denied the landowners' writ of prohibition on the ground that they were afforded adequate legal remedies for the protection of their rights in the district court's condemnation proceedings.

660 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Appeal of Fred Jones Co. v. Fred Jones Co.


No. 33516


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 126; 203 Okla. 321; 220 P.2d 245; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 504



May 9, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 20, 1950. Second Petition for Rehearing Denied July 18, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Horace D. Ballaine, Judge.

Application by Fred Jones to the Board of Adjustment of the City of Tulsa for a variance from a zoning ordinance requiring buildings to be set ten feet back of the property line on South Boston Avenue. The Board of Adjustment denied the application and on appeal the application was granted by the District Court.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant in error landowner filed an application with the board of adjustment of plaintiff in error city for a waiver of the setback restrictions so as to permit the erection of part of a building beyond the property's setback line on a major city street. The board denied the request; the landowner appealed. After a trial de novo, the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma) granted the landowner's application. The city appealed.


OVERVIEW: To erect a car showroom that persons going south on the avenue would see before they reached a point directly opposite the property, the landowner needed a waiver of the setback restriction. No other property owner objected. The trial court decided that because of the property's location, the angle made by the avenue where it changed direction, and the fact that the setback restriction began in the northern part of the landowner's property, the landowner was subjected to an unnecessary hardship in the strict application of the setback ordinance. The court agreed, finding the landowner would have suffered a deprivation of the benefits derived from having a showroom upon his property had the ordinance been strictly enforced. Further, under the proposed arrangement, the variance requested was in accord with the purpose or spirit of the ordinance. The trial court required that the landowner, at his expense, remove the building located upon the setback when necessary for the widening of the avenue. Thus, the city would be left in the same situation as if there had been strict compliance with the ordinance. The court concluded that the trial court did not err in granting the variance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Bd. of County Com'rs v. Mullins


No. 33669


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 95; 202 Okla. 628; 217 P.2d 835; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 439

PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; Eben L. Taylor, Judge.

Action by the Board of County Commissioners of Tulsa County against John C. Mullins and L. O. Mitchell, dba Arena Roller Rink, and Tulsa County Fair Board, intervener, to cancel a lease executed by the Tulsa County Fair Board. Judgment for defendant. Plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff Board of County Commissioners of Tulsa County sought review of a judgment from the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which ruled in favor of defendant lessees, two roller rink owners, and intervenor lessor, the Tulsa County Fair Board, in the Commissioners' action to cancel a lease executed by the lessor.


OVERVIEW: The Commissioners brought an action to cancel a five-year lease given by the lessor to the lessees covering the pavilion building located on the Tulsa County Fair grounds. The Commissioners claimed that the lessor lacked the authority to enter into the lease for the five-year time period. The trial court held in favor of the lessor and lessees, and the Commissioners sought review. On appeal, the court upheld the judgment. The court rejected the Commissioners' arguments that the lease was invalid for the reason that it excluded the public from county-owned property for a period of years and that § 13 of the Fair Board Act, tit. 2, ch. 2, 1943 Okla. Sess. Laws, was unconstitutional to the extent that it permitted such absolute and unrestricted conveyance. The court held that the Act did not prohibit the leasing of all county-owned property simply because it was owned by the county. The court found that the land leased was not a public park and was not open to free use by the public for such purposes at any time. The court further found that the legislature was authorized to create the Fair Board and to place the county-owned property in its custody, control, and management.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Jungels v. Town of Hennessey


No. 33693


SUPREME COURT OF OKLAHOMA


1950 OK 90; 202 Okla. 619; 217 P.2d 167; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 696



April 11, 1950, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Appeal from District Court, Kingfisher County; O. C. Wybrant, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Action by Frank Jungels and other property owners for injunction to prohibit Board of Trustees of Town of Hennessey from proceeding with street improvements. Injunction denied, and plaintiffs appeal. Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an action by plaintiffs, property owners and taxpayers, against defendants, a town, its board of trustees and others, seeking to enjoin defendants from proceeding to make street improvements in the town, plaintiffs appealed an order of the District Court of Kingfisher County (Oklahoma), which sustained defendants' motion for judgment and denied plaintiffs the requested injunctive relief.


OVERVIEW: The board adopted a resolution to create a street improvement district and published a notice that provided that unless owners of more than 50 percent of the area filed a written protest, the improvements would be made. After a protest was filed, the board rescinded its resolution and passed two more resolutions, which were also rescinded after protests were filed. The trial court sustained defendants' motion for judgment and denied plaintiffs the injunctive relief. The court affirmed. The court held that the 1947 amendment to Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 85 (1941), which stated that failure to mail notice to property owners of street improvements would not invalidate the proceedings, was not unconstitutional. The amendment did not violate Okla. Const. art. V, § 157 because the title of the bill of the amendment was pertinent to the subject of the statute, which dealt with street improvement. The court found that the board did not act improperly in rescinding the resolutions and that any fraud had to be proved by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court, which sustained defendants' motion for judgment and denied the injunctive relief sought by plaintiffs to enjoin the making of street improvements in the town.

Stuart v. King


No. 34352


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 88; 203 Okla. 23; 217 P.2d 540; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 431



April 4, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 2, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Payne County; Henry W. Hoel, Judge.

Appeal from the judgment of the district court vacating order of the Board of County Commissioners altering highway passing through the campus of the Agricultural and Mechanical College at Stillwater, Oklahoma. Reversed and remanded.

Appeal from the judgment of the district court prohibiting Board of Regents of Agricultural and Mechanical College at Stillwater, Oklahoma, from vacating highway where it passes through campus of said College.



DISPOSITION: Appeal dismissed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner residents sought review of a decision of the District Court of Payne County (Oklahoma), which found in favor of respondent five protesting residents and vacated a decision of the board of county commissioners that relocated a public highway from the college campus to another location.


OVERVIEW: Residents filed a petition before the board of county commissioners asking that a segment of a public highway within the college campus be vacated and another routing of the highway be substituted therefor. Other residents protested this petition. The board of county commissioners sustained the petition. Five of the protesting residents appealed. While the appeal was pending, the legislature enacted Okla. Stat. Laws tit. 19, ch. 10 (1949), prescribing the process for vacating a public highway. The college filed an action with the board of county commissioners under this law. The trial court vacated the decision of the board of county commissioners and declared the law unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that (1) the only requirement necessary to entitle the residents to invoke the action of the board was that they be freeholders residing in the vicinity; (2) on appeal from the board the trial court takes appellate jurisdiction only, and the extent of the jurisdiction was determined by the board's jurisdiction on the matter; and (3) the petition for alteration of the highway was fully sustained by the evidence and the trial court erred in not so holding.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the trial court and remanded the action with instruction to enter judgment not inconsistent with the court's decision.

Sess. Laws 186, Okla. Stat. Ann. tit. 19, § 896. Opponents brought a motion to dismiss the application, urging, inter alia, their right to present the issues in a local trial court.


OVERVIEW: In connection with the issuance of bonds, the district filed an application in the court for approval of the bond issue and for a judicial determination of the incontestable validity of the bonds and the revenues pledged to their payment. Several resident landowners of the sewer district filed protest and a motion to dismiss the application, arguing for their right to resolve the matter in a local forum, and referencing an action already filed in a local court challenging the bond issue. In addition, the protestants alleged that approval of the application would constitute a taking without due process. The court dismissed the application, holding that it had done so in the interest of the protection of the constitutional rights of the protestants who appeared and presented their rights to have a proper day in court in their local forum of general jurisdiction and to have complete adjudication there of their contentions without any question of lack of due process of law.


OUTCOME: The court granted the protestants' motion to dismiss the district's application for approval of a local bond issue and for a determination of the incontestable validity of the bonds and the revenues pledged to their payment.

In re State Bldg. Bonds Comm'n


No. 34512


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 45; 202 Okla. 454; 214 P.2d 934; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 380



February 15, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 28, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Original action for approval of State of Oklahoma Building Bonds and for approval of their purchase by the State Treasurer of the State of Oklahoma.



DISPOSITION: Bonds approved. Investment therein by State Treasurer approved.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner The State of Oklahoma Building Bonds Commission filed an action in which it sought approval to issue building bonds and for the purchase of those bonds, to which the protestant objected, by the State Treasurer of the State of Oklahoma under the authority of the provisions of Okla. Const. art. X, § 31.


OVERVIEW: The protestant alleged that the proposed purchase of the bonds was a misuse of state funds. The court granted the commission's request, concluding that the court lacked the authority to question the commission's findings and determined that the legislation that proposed that the bonds be issued and purchased by the treasurer did not violate Okla. Const. art. X, § 19. The court reasoned that the protestant did not attack the bonds' validity and that the record showed that the legislature carried out the public will by enacting a law that granted the treasurer the power to invest idle "public monies" in the bonds. The court also held that it lacked the jurisdiction to decide if authorizing the investment was wise, noting that the legislature had a broad power to declare fiscal policy and that buying the bonds did not divert the funds that were used to purchase them and the funds were merely invested for a time during which they would have otherwise idly remained in a bank. The court further determined that the treasurer was required to insure that the investment in the bonds was only made in a sum that did not threaten to impair the continuing solvency of any separate funds.


OUTCOME: The court granted the commission's request for permission to issue the bonds and to have the treasurer purchase them.

 

666 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cities Serv. Gas Co. v. Peerless Oil & Gas Co.


Nos. 32994, 33006


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1950 OK 4; 203 Okla. 35; 220 P.2d 279; 1950 Okla. LEXIS 512



January 17, 1950, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 21, 1950.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Order of Corporation Commission of Oklahoma fixing a minimum price consideration in the taking of natural gas from the Guymon-Hugoton Field in Oklahoma, and from order for ratable taking of gas made in favor of the Peerless Oil & Gas Company. The Cities Service Gas Company appeals. The Phillips Petroleum Company appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant, a gas company, sought review of a decision by the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma that fixed a minimum price consideration in the taking of natural gas from appellee, a gas supplier, and ordered the ratable taking of gas from the supplier's well.


OVERVIEW: During the pendency of the proceedings, the company entered into an agreement with the supplier for a ratable taking of gas from the wells, but left unsettled, the price to be paid for the gas. In hearing the matter, the commission acted pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 52, § 239 (1941), which authorized its regulation of natural gas. The company contended, inter alia, that the commission had no power to fix natural gas prices and that such powers were unconstitutional if they existed. The court upheld the fixed price. The court held that: (1) state regulation of natural resources was justified to prevent waste and to adjust private correlative rights; (2) the due process and equal protection clauses did not preclude the state in the exercise of its power to preserve the correlative rights of producers of natural gas from a common pool, from requiring one to take ratably from the other producers who had no outlets; (3) the commission's power to regulate the taking of natural gas to prevent waste, included the power to fix a minimum price by necessary implication; and (4) the fixed price was not arbitrary where it was based on evidence that the current price was resulting in waste.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order fixing a minimum price and ordering a ratable taking.

Bd. of Comm'rs of Tulsa County v. Okla. Tax Comm'n (City of Tulsa)


No. 34334


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 258; 202 Okla. 269; 212 P.2d 462; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 465



November 29, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 16, 1949.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original proceeding instituted in the court by the relator, a board of county commissioners for itself and all other counties similarly situated, the relator sought a writ of prohibition to enjoin the Oklahoma Tax Commission and a county treasurer from allocating and distributing moneys under the authority of certain house bills purporting to amend the Motor Vehicle License and Registration Act (Act), Okla. Stat., tit. 47, § 22.2 (1941).


OVERVIEW: Two acts, tit. 70, ch. 20, § 6, S. L. 1949 (hereinafter H.B. 120) and tit. 47, ch. 1a, § 1, S. L. 1949 (hereinafter H.B. 430), purportedly amending the Act, were challenged on constitutional grounds. The subject matter of the Act was the public school system. A certain percentage of funds allocated thereunder were to be used to support the county schools. However, a proviso under H.B. 120, to be incorporated in Okla. Stat. tit. 47, § 22.2(e), provided for allocation of funds to governmental agencies that were distinct from the constituted school authorities and committed funds to uses distinct from schools. The court issued the writ. Such proviso, purporting to amend the Act, violated Okla. Const. art. V, § 57 because it was not germane to the subject matter of the Act. One reading the Act, in view of its title referencing schools, would be surprised by the incorporation of such amendment thereto. Also, the purported amendment under H.B. 430, a proviso to another section of the Act, was ineffective to constitute an amendment thereof without re-enactment and re-publication of such section at length because the proviso did not contain all law upon the subject embraced in the section.


OUTCOME: The writ of prohibition issued.

One Chi. Coin's Play Boy Marble Bd. v. State ex rel. Adams

Supreme Court of Oklahoma

Proceeding by the State ex rel. Elmer W. Adams, County Attorney of Tulsa County, against One Chicago Coin's Play Boy Marble Board No. 19771 for confiscation as a slot machine. OVERVIEW: The State, on relation of a county attorney, brought the action to confiscate defendant's game, which was a coin-operated marble board. 669 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ex parte Haley


No. 33297


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 218; 202 Okla. 101; 210 P.2d 653; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 419; 12 A.L.R.2d 416



October 11, 1949, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Writ discharged.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an original petition for a writ of habeas corpus to challenge his confinement under arraignment on an information in the Court of Common Pleas of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that charged him with the operation of a bookmaking establishment for the purpose of receiving and reporting bets on horse racing contrary to the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 991 (1941).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that § 991 was not in force when he was charged because a 1914 referendum election adopting its predecessor act was invalid. He also contended that the trial court in which he was charged did not exist when he was charged because the population of the city in which it was located had grown beyond the bounds set out in its authorizing legislation. Assuming jurisdiction because of the challenge to the trial court's existence, the court discharged the writ. It accepted petitioner's claim that the referendum election was invalid, but it held that § 991 was effectively re-enacted when the legislature adopted the 1941 Oklahoma Code. The referendum did not deprive the legislature of power to re-enact § 991. The legislature retained that power under Okla. Const. art. V, § 7, which was to be construed together with Okla. Const. art. V, § 3. Okla. Stat. tit. 20, § 651 (1941), under which the trial court was established, did not provide that such courts would cease to exist when populations grew beyond the stated limits. In the absence of such a statement, the legislature was presumed to have intended the trial court to continue to exist.


OUTCOME: The writ was discharged and petitioner was remanded to the sheriff's custody.

 

670 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


City of Bethany v. Mason


No. 34001


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 190; 202 Okla. 66; 210 P.2d 353; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 411



September 28, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; A. P. Van Meter, Judge.

Civil action in the nature of quo warranto by the City of Bethany against Albert Mason et al. The District Court sustained demurrer to petition and dismissed the action, and City appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff City of Bethany appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) that sustained defendant city officers' demurrer to the City's petition in the City's action brought using Okla. Stat. tit. 12, §§ 1531 to 1538 (1941). The City sought, inter alia, that the officials be ousted for wrongfully and illegally usurping their offices. The trial court ruled that the City did not have authority to bring the action.


OVERVIEW: The City alleged that another city, which it had annexed with other land, was incorporated by the city officials but that such incorporation was unconstitutional because as excluded from the other land its population was greatly below the minimum required by statutes and the Oklahoma Constitution; the City also alleged that a proper petition was not signed by 35 percent of the qualified electors residing in certain territorial limits. The city officials argued that the petition in the case sub judice pleaded a cause in the nature of quo warranto and that the City was not a proper party to bring or maintain such an action. Where the municipality was at least a de facto corporation, the validity of its ordinances and corporate existence could be challenged only by the State in direct proceedings such as quo warranto brought through the instrumentality of the Attorney General or another officer or person authorized to pursue the remedy. Ergo, the court ruled that there was no error in sustaining the city officials' demurrer.


OUTCOME: Ruling in favor of the city officials, the court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

672 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


St. Louis-San Francisco Ry. Co. v. Tillman County Excise Bd.


No. 33519


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 174; 201 Okla. 624; 208 P.2d 576; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 384



July 19, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Tax Review; Clarence M. Mills, James T. Shipman, and J. Knox Byrum, Judges.

In the matter of the protest of St. Louis-San Francisco Railway Company against illegal and excessive tax levies for fiscal year beginning July 1, 1947, and ending June 30, 1948, by the County Excise Board of Tillman County. From an adverse judgment, protestant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Protestant railroad appealed from a decision of the Court of Tax Review (Oklahoma), which concluded that tax levies for a school district were not illegal and excessive as contended by the railroad.


OVERVIEW: The governing board of school district C-3 of Tillman County informed the excise board that had dispensed with its school for that fiscal year and that the county superintendent had transferred all of its pupils to other districts in the county. The district requested the excise board to make proper appropriations for the transportation and education of the transferred pupils to the other districts. After a mistake in the calculation of the transfer fees was made, a correction sheet was issued that authorized an increase in the transfer fees. The railroad contended that the increased transfer appropriation, or tax levy, was illegal because section 5(a) of H.B. No. 85, 1947 Legislative Session, was unconstitutional. The court rejected that contention. The court reaffirmed a prior holding that the act did not violate Okla. Const. art. V, §§ 57 and 59. Nor did the act violate Okla. Const. art. X, § 9, which forbid a levy of ad valorem taxes for a state purpose. The levy involved was not for a state purpose, but was levied for the purpose of discharging the obligation of School District C-3 to the receiving districts for the education and transportation of its pupils.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

 

673 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Stephens v. Borgman


No. 33774


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 166; 202 Okla. 41; 210 P.2d 176; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 406



July 12, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 28, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Tom R. Blaine, Judge.

Action by Hattie M. Stephens against W. R. Borgman et al., members of the State Board of Affairs of the State of Oklahoma, for injunction. From judgment for defendants, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff employee appealed the denial of her request for an injunction against defendant Chairman State Board of Public Affairs by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) by which she sought to compel the Board's compliance with Okla. Const. art. 23, § 1 and Okla. Stat. tit. 61, § 3 (1941) that required an eight hour work day for all state employees.


OVERVIEW: Working at the state hospital for 12 hours a day, 6 days a week, for $ 85 per month and room and board, the employee sought to enforce the eight hour work day limit for state employees under § 3. On appeal, the employee argued that the trial court erred in not granting the injunction. Contending otherwise, the State claimed that the judgment was supportable on the basis given but also because the employee's service was not within the purview of § 3. Affirming the trial court's holding for yet a third reason, the court held that no grounds existed for the granting of an injunction. In so holding, the court found that no statutory authority existed for the employee's action and that equity afforded no grounds for the private request of such an injunction. Moreover, the Labor Commissioner, who intervened prior to the appeal, was not authorized by the Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 1 (1941) definition of his office to prosecute the action. Finally, the court was unable to find a private, litigable right that was invaded by the violation of § 3 so as to entitle the employee to prosecute the action. Indeed, the court found the very existence of such right was negatived.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Englebrecht v. Day


No. 33869


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 154; 201 Okla. 585; 208 P.2d 538; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 376



July 5, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Muskogee County; E. G. Carroll, Judge.

Action in equity by Warren O. Englebrecht, doing business as Warren's Grocery, against Ernest Day and others for injunction restraining the alleged violation by defendants of the Unfair Sales Act. From judgment for the defendants, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Judgment affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the owner of a grocery store, filed an action in equity against defendants, the owners of a competing grocery store and its manager, seeking an injunction to restrain defendants from allegedly violating the Oklahoma Unfair Sales Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 15, §§ 591-597 (1941). The District Court of Muskogee County (Oklahoma) entered judgment in favor of defendants. Plaintiff appealed from that judgment.


OVERVIEW: Plaintiff alleged that defendants advertised and continued to advertise for sale, offered for sale, and sold at retail certain articles of merchandise at less than cost to the retailer in violation of the provisions of the Act. Plaintiff also alleged that the items referred to were sold at prices which could not be justified by prevailing market conditions within Oklahoma and that the items were sold to the general public as bait with the intent of inducing the purchase of other merchandise. Plaintiff charged that defendants were selling the items with the intent to impair and prevent fair competition and injure public welfare. The trial court sustained defendants' demurrer to plaintiff's action, holding that the Act was unconstitutional. The court held that Okla. Stat. tit. 15, § 593 violated federal and state constitutional due process by making sales by retailers at less than the cost contrary to public policy, and a violation thereof a crime, where such sales were made with the effect of inducing the purchase of other merchandise or unfairly diverting trade from a competitor or otherwise injuring a competitor even though there was no such intent on the part of the seller.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

675 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. Bd. of County Com'Rs


No. 34161


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 144; 201 Okla. 652; 208 P.2d 177; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 374



June 22, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: As Corrected July 16, 1949. Rehearing Denied and Concurring Opinion Filed July 19, 1949.



DISPOSITION: Writ granted.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff county assessor filed an original action seeking a mandamus to require defendants, board of county commissioners, to make a further and supplemental appropriation out of the unencumbered surplus revenue on hand to provide the county assessor with funds in order to enable him to perform his mandatory duties.


OVERVIEW: The county assessor filed an original action seeking a mandamus to require the board of county commissioners to make a second appropriation out of the unencumbered surplus revenue on hand to provide the county assessor with funds in order to enable him to perform his duties. The court held that under Okla. Stat. Ann. tit. 68, § 15.17 (1947), it was the clear legal duty of the board of county commissioners to provide adequate appropriations for supplies, deputy hire and traveling expenses for the performance of the duties imposed upon the county assessor. The court stated that the assessor complied with all legal duties in requesting the funds and that the board did not fail to grant the additional funds on the grounds that the claim was excessive or fraudulent. The court noted that upon admission of the board that adequate unencumbered funds were on hand, out of which the appropriation requested could be made, it was not only the clear legal duty of the board to provide the appropriation, but it was its mandatory duty, made so by the statute. The court concluded that mandamus was the appropriate vehicle for the assessor to obtain relief and granted the writ.


OUTCOME: The court granted the county assessor's writ of mandamus.

St. Louis & S.F. R.R. Co. v. Ottawa County Excise Bd.


No. 33979


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 134; 201 Okla. 478; 207 P.2d 275; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 338



June 14, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from Court of Tax Review; Clarence Mills, James T. Shipman, and Knox Byrum, Judges.

Protest of St. Louis-San Francisco Railway Company, a corporation, against certain tax levies made by the Excise Board of Ottawa County. Protest denied, and protestant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant taxpayer sought review of a decision of the Court of Tax Review (Oklahoma), which denied its protest against alleged excessive and unlawful tax levies made by appellee county for the benefit of the general fund of the city of Picher.


OVERVIEW: The county recovered several judgments against the city on warrants held by it as an investment in its sinking fund. An annual tax levy was made for five years to raise the funds to retire the judgments. The tax levies raised an amount in excess of that needed to retire the judgments. The surplus was transferred to the general fund with the approval of the county under the authority of Okla. Stat. tit. 62, § 445 (1943 Supp.). The county then authorized an appropriation for general fund purposes and levied a tax of three mills on the assessed value of the city. The taxpayer alleged that the surplus transferred to the general fund was an unconstitutional diversion of the fund and that it should have been refunded to the taxpayers by reducing the three mill tax levy. The lower court denied the taxpayer's protest. The court affirmed, finding that a surplus cash fund arising incidentally from receipts in excess of appropriations and expenditures was subject to the disposal of the Legislature for any lawful state purpose in accordance with the legislative will. The court held the statute therefore did not violate Okla. Const. art. X, § 9.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the lower court denying the taxpayer's protest against the tax levies made by the county for the benefit of the general fund of the city was affirmed.

Shanks v. Blaine's Heirs


No. 33307


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 94; 201 Okla. 350; 206 P.2d 978; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 320



May 3, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Creek County; C. O. Beaver, Judge.

Action by L. E. Shanks against the heirs of C. Blaine, deceased, and others. From the part of the judgment in favor of the named defendants, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff asserted title and right to possession of two lots and rested his claim upon a resale tax deed issued after a tax sale. The lots were sold for delinquent assessments. Defendants in possession of the lots received a deed one-year prior to the tax sale from the then recorded owner and asserted title in themselves. The District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma) rendered judgment in favor of defendants, and plaintiff appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendants asserted that the county treasurer was without statutory authority to resell the property for delinquent taxes because the sale of the property was barred under the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 242 (1941) and the failure of the bondholders to commence an action to enforce collection of the assessment liens or accept refunding bonds absolved the property from the liens and the sale of the property was null and void. Plaintiff asserted that defendants were precluded from raising the question of the legality of the resale because of a federal court decision. The court affirmed an noted that the federal action concerned a bondholder's right to maintain an action for foreclosure of tax liens within the purview of the general statute of limitations, but did not address the issue of the provision of § 242 that limited the time of enforcement of the lien of any bond by foreclosure. The court held that defendants were not barred by that action from trying the issues presented in the instant case. The court held that because the limitation period under § 242 had expired, the treasurer was without authority to order the resale of the lots.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

State Dry Cleaners' Bd. v. Compton


No. 33503


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 78; 201 Okla. 284; 205 P.2d 286; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 563



April 19, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Canadian County; Baker H. Melone, Judge.

Suit by V. M. Compton against State Dry Cleaners' Board and others to enjoin the defendants from enforcing minimum prices fixed under act empowering the State Dry Cleaning Board to fix minimum prices, on ground that the act is unconstitutional. From judgment for plaintiff, defendants appeal.



DISPOSITION: Judgment reversed, with directions to vacate injunction and dismiss the cause.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff individual initiated an action against defendants, the Oklahoma State Dry Cleaners' Board and others, and sought to enjoin the board from enforcing minimum prices under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 744, 757, and 758 (1947). The District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma) declared the specified provisions unconstitutional and granted injunctive relief in favor of the individual. The board and others appealed.


OVERVIEW: The individual sought to enjoin the board from enforcing minimum prices under Okla. Stat. tit. 59, §§ 744, 757, and 758 (1947), on the ground that the statutory provisions lacked constitutional validity. The trial court agreed with the individual's position, declared the provisions unconstitutional, and granted injunctive relief. On review, the court reversed the trial court's judgment and remanded the case with directions. The court held that price control in an industry affecting the public health, safety, and general welfare, like any form of regulation, was constitutional unless arbitrary, discriminatory, unreasonable, or demonstrably irrelevant. The court concluded that the price-fixing authority of the board under the statutory provisions was constitutional. Furthermore, the court concluded that the record lacked evidence that the prices were unreasonable, arbitrary, or otherwise unjust.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and directed the trial court to vacate the injunction and to dismiss the cause of action.

Reinhart & Donovan Co. v. Guar. Abstract Co.


No. 32912


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 40; 201 Okla. 334; 205 P.2d 881; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 296



March 8, 1949, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied May 3, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Lucius Babcock, Judge.

Action by the Reinhart & Donovan Company against the Guaranty Abstract Company et al. Judgment for defendants, and plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff landowner brought an action in the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) against defendants, a title abstract company and its surety, for damages due to a claimed cloud on the title to the landowner's property. In their answers defendants, among other defenses, asserted the doctrines of res judicata and estoppel by judgment. A bench trial was held and a judgment was rendered for defendants. The landowner appealed.


OVERVIEW: The landowner's petition alleged the abstract company's preparation of an abstract covering the property purchased by the landowner was erroneous in that it did not reflect the true state of the records of the county treasurer relating to property taxes for three years. The landowner contended that the trial court erred in holding that the judgment in a federal court case operated as an estoppel by judgment so as to preclude its right to recover in the instant case. The abstract company made two certificates, the earlier one to the landowner and the last one to the insurance company. It was readily apparent that the issue as to the liability of the abstract company was the same in each case, in that neither certificate showed the proceedings whereby the taxes on the property were reduced by the county commissioners. A decision in litigation against the board of county commissioners, which held that such reductions were void, had not been handed down at the time either certificates were made. The evidence sufficiently established that the case in the federal court, while brought in the name of the insurance company, was brought, supervised, and controlled by the landowner.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

 

680 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. City of Durant


No. 33132


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1949 OK 11; 201 Okla. 113; 202 P.2d 418; 1949 Okla. LEXIS 518



January 25, 1949, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Bryan County; Roy Paul, Judge.

Action by W. E. Williams against the City of Durant and others. From the judgment, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff owner appealed a decision of the District Court, Bryan County (Oklahoma), which, in an action against defendants, officials and bank, seeking to quiet title to certain real property, denied the relief sought by the owner as to paving taxes assessed against the owner's real property and paving bonds that were payable out of such assessments.


OVERVIEW: The owner acquired title from parties who purchased the property at tax resale for ad valorem taxes only. The tax sale did not include any paving taxes assessed against the property. The bank owned the paving bonds. The bonds matured and five months later the bank, pursuant to the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 11, §§ 242 and 242a (1941), filed with the city clerk its agreement to accept street improvement refunding bonds. The refunding bonds were never issued. The trial court denied the owner relief. The court affirmed, finding that the foreclosure statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 107, did not apply to bonds issued prior to 1923. Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 95(2) barred only the right to bring an action to foreclose the lien of bonds that had matured more than three years prior to the bringing of the action, and did not cancel or nullify the lien of the bonds on the property or prevent the bondholder from availing itself of other remedies provided by law for the enforcement of its lien. The court found that Okla. Stat. tit. 11, § 242a did not extinguish the lien of the bonds or limit the duty of the county treasurer in reference to enforcement of the liens for delinquent assessments.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the trial court denying the relief sought by the owner was affirmed.

 

681 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Murphy v. Eldridge


No. 33134


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 247; 201 Okla. 501; 207 P.2d 260; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 423



November 16, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 14, 1949.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; Lucius Babcock, Judge.

Action by Juanita Eldridge and others against W. A. Pat Murphy, Labor Commissioner, of the State of Oklahoma. Case revived as against Jim Hughes, present Commissioner. Judgment for plaintiffs, and defendant appeals.



DISPOSITION: Reversed with directions.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant labor commission appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), finding that the maximum rate to be charged under Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 43 (1941) against plaintiff employers was confiscatory. The court granted an injunction.


OVERVIEW: The employers filed suit, seeking an injunction alleging that imposing their maximum fee rate under § 43 would result in their going out of business. The labor commission conceded that, if the rates were to be applied, the employers could not maintain their current services. The district court entered judgment in the employers' favor. On appeal, the court reversed and remanded for a new trial. The court held that the guaranty of due process demanded only that the law should not be unreasonable, arbitrary, or capricious and that the means selected should have a real and substantial relation to the object sought to be attained. The court held that no evidence was presented in the district court regarding whether the employers could reduce the services rendered without decreasing efficiency or loss of benefits to their clients. The mere fact that the employers could not maintain the same services did not automatically result in the rate being confiscatory.


OUTCOME: The court reversed and remanded for a new trial.

Armstrong v. Sewer Improvement Dist. No. 1


No. 33764


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 198; 201 Okla. 531; 199 P.2d 1012; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 410



October 5, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 16, 1948. Second Petition for Rehearing Denied December 7, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Tulsa County; John Ladner, Judge.

Action by Arche Donald Armstrong and wife against Sewer Improvement District No. 1, Tulsa County, et al. to enjoin issuance of bonds and construction of sewer. From the judgment, plaintiffs appeal.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on rehearing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff citizens appealed a decision of the District Court, Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which denied the citizens' request that the court enjoin the issuance of bonds and the construction of a sewer under the provisions of a legislative act providing for the organization and functioning of sewer improvement districts. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of the act and the formation of the sewer district.


OVERVIEW: The citizens asked the court to enjoin the issuance of bonds for the construction of a sewer. The trial court upheld the constitutionality of Okla. Stat. tit. 19, ch. 20 (Supp. 1947), and denied the injunction. On appeal the citizens contended that the law violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 26, in that it authorized the district to incur a debt in excess of five percent of the value of the taxable property therein. The court held that the sewer district was not a political subdivision and therefore did not fall within the class affected by § 26. The citizens also argued that, in permitting the assessment of the lands at a greater valuation for sewer purposes than for general purposes, the law also violated Okla. Const. art. X, § 5. The court held that the assessments were special assessments levied upon the theory that all of the assessed property would be equally benefited by the construction of the sewer. The court held that the act was constitutional. However, the court reversed the judgment and directed the trial court to issue the injunction because it found that proper procedure was not followed in the publishing of the petition.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court and remanded with directions to issue the injunction sought by the citizens.
