City of Ardmore v. Excise Bd.


No. 33450


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 158; 200 Okla. 516; 197 P.2d 961; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 351



June 29, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied September 28, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Carter County; W. J. Monroe, Judge.

Action by plaintiff, City of Ardmore, for writ of mandamus to compel defendants, members of County Excise Board, to apportion to plaintiff some part of 15 mills legal limit of tax levy. Judgment for defendants, and plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff, the City of Ardmore, Oklahoma, sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Oklahoma) in favor of defendants, members of the Carter County, Oklahoma, Excise Board, in the City's action for a writ of mandamus to compel the board to apportion to the City a part of the annual ad valorem tax levy.


OVERVIEW: The Board initially allocated one mill to the City; it later attempted to rescind the former order and made a new allocation providing no mills to the City. The City contended that the Board was without authority to make the latter allocation; that Okla. Const. art. 10, § 9 required the Board to apportion some part of the annual levy to the City; and that by reason of Okla. Stat. tit. 8, § 44a (Supp. 1943), the Board was bound to allocate to the City one-half mill for cemetery purposes. The court affirmed the judgment. It held that the initial apportionment made by the Board was not final and irrevocable, and that it was acting within its authority when it changed the allocation prior to certification of the levies and appropriations. The court held that the constitution did not require the Board to apportion some part of the levy to each of the three subdivisions of government, regardless of the relative needs thereof. The court also held that because the only interpretation which could be given to § 44a was that it undertook to raise the legal limit of ad valorem taxation in cities coming within its purview from 15 mills to 15 1/2 mills, the statute was unconstitutional.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

State ex rel. Robinett v. Jarrett

DISPOSITION:  Writ granted.

OVERVIEW: Relator and another party both filed as candidates for county superintendent of public instruction. Thereafter, the other party filed a protest with the county election board against the recognition of relator's candidacy, based upon her lack of qualifications. The board overruled the protest. The other party then sought to enjoin the board from putting relator's name on the ballot. A temporary injunction was awarded ex parte. Because the right sought to be protected was purely political, the court held that the trial court was without jurisdiction to enjoin. As such, the court granted the writ.


OUTCOME: The application for writ of prohibition was granted.

 

686 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sanders v. Okla. Empl. Sec. Comm'n


No. 32643


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 116; 200 Okla. 366; 195 P.2d 272; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 505



May 11, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 8, 1948. Second Petition for Rehearing Denied July 13, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, Oklahoma County; A. P. Van Meter, Judge.

Action by Leo Sanders by injunction against the Oklahoma Employment Security Commission. From judgment sustaining motion to dismiss appeal, plaintiff appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff taxpayer appealed a decision from the District Court, Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) sustaining defendant employment security commission's motion to dismiss the taxpayer's action by injunction for lack of jurisdiction. The taxpayer commenced this action against the commission to enjoin the commission from enforcing certain tax liens for delinquent contributions assessed under the Oklahoma Employment Security Act.


OVERVIEW: Where an administrative remedy was provided by statute, relief must be sought from the administrative body; that remedy must be exhausted before the courts would act; exhaustion of administrative remedy was a jurisdictional prerequisite for resort to the courts. The Oklahoma Employment Security Act provided a full, complete and comprehensive administrative remedy with respect to any controversy over the amount of any contribution required by the law. It gave the plaintiff the right to apply for the adjustment of any alleged overpayments and authorized the commission to allow a refund as to any just claim of overpayments. The taxpayer did not claim that he ever pursued the remedy provided by law before the commission and the appeal to the trial court. The taxpayer apparently sought a reversal of the order of dismissal of his claim, seeking a declaratory judgment as to the constitutionality of a statute. Such proceeding was prohibited by Okla. Stat. tit. 40, § 224, subdiv.(b), subsec.(3) (1941). The question could properly be determined in a proceeding before the commission, and judicially determined on appeal. The court affirmed dismissal of the action for lack of jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed, holding that the trial court's decision sustaining the commission's motion to dismiss for lack of jurisdiction was proper.

Fenimore v. State ex rel. Comm'rs of the Land Office


No. 33178


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 93; 200 Okla. 400; 194 P.2d 852; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 492



April 20, 1948, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied June 15, 1948.


PRIOR HISTORY: Appeal from District Court, McCurtain County; Howard Phillips, Judge.

Motion by G. O. Fenimore to suppress an execution issued against him in a mortgage foreclosure action to recover a deficiency due on the judgment and to enjoin the issuance of any other execution. From an order overruling the motion, Fenimore appeals.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant individual sought review of an order of the District Court of McCurtain County (Oklahoma), which overruled the individual's motion to suppress an execution issued against him in a mortgage foreclosure action to recover a deficiency due on a judgment and to enjoin the issuance of any other execution.


OVERVIEW: In 1937, the State obtained a default judgment in its suit to recover from an individual a personal judgment on notes and for foreclosure of a mortgage securing the notes. In 1941, an execution was issued and the sale of the realty realized less than the judgment amount, but no proceedings were taken to determine the deficiency. In 1947, an execution was issued against the individual, who then filed a motion to suppress said execution, arguing the State's failure to comply with Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 686 (1941), which required a judgment creditor, within 90 days after the sale of mortgaged premises, to determine the difference between the mortgaged debt and the market value of the mortgaged property, and the entry of a deficiency judgment for the difference. When the motion was denied, the individual appealed, contending that this statute applied to the State. The court disagreed, noting a proviso therein exempting the State from the statute, namely, that nothing would reduce a deficiency judgment in favor of the State. Finally, that the law was inapplicable to the State did not make it an unconstitutional special law, as the State was alone in the class to which the law applied.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court order overruling the individual's motion to suppress an execution issued against him to recover a deficiency due on a judgment.

 

688 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bond v. Phelps


No. 33240


Supreme Court of Oklahoma


1948 OK 76; 200 Okla. 70; 191 P.2d 938; 1948 Okla. LEXIS 327



March 30, 1948, Decided



DISPOSITION:  Writ issued.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an original action plaintiffs, commissioners of the Corporation Commission of Oklahoma, sought an order in the nature of mandamus that directed defendant state officials to pay their claims for services performed by the Commissioners in compliance with Okla. St. Ann. tit. 52, §§ 451-453 (1947) (the Act).


OVERVIEW: The Act provided, as an elective duty of commissioners, the preparation of a compilation of the oil and gas laws of Oklahoma and the rules and regulations adopted pursuant thereto for additional compensation. The Attorney General contended that the Act was void as it applied to the commissioners then in office, by reason of Okla. Const. art. 23, § 10, which prohibited changes to the salary of a public official after his election. The court followed the nongermane rule, which allowed remuneration for additional duties imposed beyond the scope of previous duties. The law did not impose any additional power upon the commission. Rather, it offered employment to the commissioners, to be performed so as not to interfere with their constitutional and statutory duties. The court held that these duties were nongermane to the previous powers and duties of the members of the Corporation Commission. The court also held that the Act embraced one subject. Regardless of whether the duties imposed upon the commissioners were germane or nongermane to their official duties, the subject remained the same. Embracing but one subject, the Act did not violate Okla. Const. art. 5, § 57.


OUTCOME: The Act was constitutional and the Commissioners were allowed to receive compensation as it provided.

Fairchild v. State


Case No. F-96-121


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 49; 998 P.2d 611; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 84



December 7, 1999, Filed

PRIOR HISTORY: Previously Reported at: 992 P.2d 350 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.

AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE MAJOR WILSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.

Original Opinion of August 20, 1998, Reported at: 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 45.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of his conviction in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for first-degree murder of a child.


OVERVIEW: Appellant severely beat a child resulting in death and was convicted of first-degree murder of a child. Appellant was sentenced to the death penalty. Appellant contended that the court should have given an instruction on voluntary intoxication, that expert testimony and autopsy evidence regarding the victim's injuries had prejudiced the jury, and that the death penalty would be cruel and unusual punishment. The appellate court affirmed, holding that the defense of voluntary intoxication was inapplicable, that the expert testimony and autopsy evidence were relevant and not excessive, and that the death penalty in such a case was constitutional.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed because the defense of voluntary intoxication was unavailable, expert testimony and autopsy evidence were properly admitted, and the death penalty in such a case was not cruel and unusual punishment.

Martinez v. State


Case No. PC-98-739


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 47; 992 P.2d 426; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 76; 70 O.B.A.J. 3557



November 24, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  Martinez v. State, 1995 OK CR 52, 904 P.2d 138, 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 58 (Okla. Crim. App., 1995)
 Martinez v. State, 1999 OK CR 33, 984 P.2d 813, 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63 (Okla. Crim. App., 1999)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Motion for Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, criminal defendant, filed his Application for Post-Conviction Relief in the Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma in accordance with Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (1999) and Motion for Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery, following denial of his direct appeal of murder convictions.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was sentenced to death, following his conviction on two counts of murder. Petitioner appealed his conviction to the instant court, which sustained the conviction. Petitioner then filed his Application for Post-Conviction Relief in the instant court in accordance with Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (1999) and a Motion for Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery. Petitioner's primary complaint was that of ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel for their failure to present facts regarding petitioner's life in Cuba, to support mitigating circumstances. The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief and his motion for evidentiary hearing, holding that there existed no controverted, previously unresolved factual issues material to the legality of petitioner's confinement; petitioner could have previously raised collaterally asserted grounds for review; and grounds for review which were properly presented had no merit or were barred by res judicata. Furthermore, petitioner failed to show why additional discovery was necessary and failed to overcome the presumption of regularity.


OUTCOME: Petitioner's application for post-conviction relief and motion for evidentiary hearing and discovery were denied; no controverted, previously unresolved factual issues material to the legality of petitioner's confinement existed. Furthermore, petitioner failed to show why additional discovery was necessary and failed to overcome the presumption of regularity.

 

691 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Woodward v. Morrissey


No. M-99-170


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 43; 991 P.2d 1042; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 73; 70 O.B.A.J. 3461; 70 O.B.A.J. 3555



November 19, 1999, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] The Name of this Case and Opinion Text has been Corrected by the Court November 30, 1999.



DISPOSITION: Petitioner's request for a writ of mandamus DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus and/or prohibitation, challenging the constitutionality of the Oklahoma Drug Court Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 471-471.11 (Supp. 1998) because he was denied entry into the program.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner sought a writ of mandamus and/or prohibition pursuant to the Rules of the Oklahoma Court of Criminal Appeals Rule 10.6, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, ch. 18, App. (1998), alleging that the Oklahoma Drug Court Act (Act), Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 471-471.11 (Supp. 1998), was unconstitutional. Petitioner had been denied entry into the Drug Court program by the District Attorney, and challenged the Act's lack of a provision for judicial review. The court found that the Act simply provided for a plea bargain arrangement. Under separation of powers principles, the court could not interfere with prosecutorial discretion in deciding to prosecute petitioner in the absence of a discriminatory ground. Petitioner's argument that he was being denied access to the courts in violation of Okla. Const. art. II, § 6 was without merit. The request for extraordinary relief was therefore denied.


OUTCOME: Requests for writ of mandamus and/or prohibition denied on the grounds that petitioner did not establish that he had a clear legal right to the relief. Petitioner did not provide authority supporting position that statute's lack of judicial review was unconstitutional.

Bernay v. State


Case No. F-97-461


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 37; 989 P.2d 998; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 68; 70 O.B.A.J. 2963



October 12, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied December 7, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 77.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged his conviction of first degree malice murder and death sentence imposed by District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: The trial court did not abuse its discretion by not inquiring further after receiving unequivocal answers from prospective jurors because it made the proper inquiry to determine whether prospective jurors could consider the death penalty. Permitting a witness's preliminary hearing testimony to be read into evidence and admitting photographs at the first and second stages of the trial was not an abuse of discretion. When viewed in light most favorable to the state, the evidence was sufficient for the jury to find appellant shot the decedent with premeditated design to effect death. The court also rejected appellant's constitutional claims of error relating to his guilt, claims that the trial court erred in the sentencing, claims of prosecutorial misconduct, and claims of ineffective assistance of counsel. Under the mandatory sentence review of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13(C) (1991), the court found that the sentence of death was appropriate.


OUTCOME: Judgment and sentence affirmed because no error warranted reversal or modification, sentence of death was appropriate and not imposed under influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.

Mooney v. State


No. F-95-1140


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 34; 990 P.2d 875; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64; 70 O.B.A.J. 2414



August 31, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Habeas corpus proceeding at, Magistrate's recommendation at Mooney v. Workman, 2002 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 28328 (W.D. Okla., July 5, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF WASHITA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD DARBY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED and MODIFIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Washita County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree malice aforethought murder and sentenced him to death based on a jury verdict.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged his conviction for first degree malice aforethought murder and death sentence imposed pursuant to a jury verdict. The court rejected appellant's claims that his previous robbery conviction violated double jeopardy rights, that a 16 year old must be given individual consideration as to his maturity before the death penalty was imposed, and that jury instructions on lesser-included offenses should have been given. Error did occur as a result of appellee prosecution's failure to make a timely and voluntary disclosure of a witness' letters to defense counsel which may have shown bias. This error did not affect the first stage of trial, but was not harmless error in the sentencing stage. The bailiff's unauthorized communication with the jury in violation of 22 Okla. Stat. § 857 (1991) improperly coerced the death sentence. The conviction was therefore affirmed, but the sentence of death was modified to life imprisonment without parole.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed, and sentenced modified to life without parole because two errors, the prosecution's delay in providing a witness' letters which may have shown bias and the bailiff's unauthorized communication with the jury, were not harmless error with respect to the sentencing stage of appellant's trial.

 

695 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Wilkins v. State


Case No. F-98-487


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 27; 985 P.2d 184; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 58; 70 O.B.A.J. 2026; 70 O.B.A.J. 2182



June 18, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Counsel Amended July 1, 1999. Rehearing Denied July 26, 1999. Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 283.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PITTSBURG COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JERRY L. COLCLAZIER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Pittsburg County (Oklahoma) convicting him and sentencing him following a non-jury trial of two counts of child stealing in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 891.


OVERVIEW: Defendant sought relief from his conviction for child stealing. The court affirmed the conviction and sentence. The statute was not overbroad, as any defect could be cured on a case-by-case analysis. Common sense indicated that the statute only applied to malicious, forcible, or fraudulent taking of a child with the intent to detain and conceal from the other parent. The statute could only be analyzed for vagueness as applied to defendant. The statute applied to any person without exception, defendant had fair notice of its application. The statute was not preempted by the federal kidnapping statute, which had a different purpose and was not so pervasive to preclude enforcement of state laws on the taking of children by their parents. Defendant's taking of the children without their mother's knowledge or consent, planned for some time, clearly fit within Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 891, and the evidence supported the verdict.


OUTCOME: Defendant's conviction and sentence imposed for child stealing was affirmed, because the statute was not vague or overbroad, it was not preempted by the federal kidnapping statute, and defendant's actions fit the description of the prohibited activity.

 

696 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


No. F-97-72


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 16; 980 P.2d 1111; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 35



April 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 26, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF KAY COUNTY THE HONORABLE LESLIE D. PAGE PRESIDING.

This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of April 12, 1999, Previously Reported at: 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13.



DISPOSITION: Judgment against Appellant is AFFIRMED, but his sentence is REVERSED and REMANDED to the District Court for RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment and sentence from the District Court of Kay County (Oklahoma), which convicted appellant, based upon a jury verdict, of first degree murder, and sentenced him to death based on the jury's finding of the existence of two aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Appellant approached an officer and admitted to killing his aunt. In total, he made four confessions. He was subsequently charged and convicted of first degree murder. Based on the jury's finding of two aggravating circumstances, appellant was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court found that because appellant objected to the admission of his two videotaped custodial interrogations, he was entitled to an in camera hearing as to the voluntariness of those confessions. Without a hearing, the tapes should not have been admitted into evidence. It then determined the error was harmless at the trial stage because the jury had already heard two of appellant's confessions. However, the court held it was difficult to find beyond a reasonable doubt that the jury's decision regarding punishment was not influenced by having watched appellant's demeanor on the tapes. Additionally, a hearing would have permitted a more informed decision on whether appellant waived his right to remain silent at the first interrogation. Finding the remaining contentions to be meritless, the court affirmed the conviction, but reversed the sentence and remanded the matter for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction for first degree murder was affirmed, but the death sentence was reversed and the matter was remanded for resentencing because the failure to conduct an in camera hearing as to the voluntariness of appellant's two custodial interrogations while harmless at trial, constituted error at the sentencing phase.

Lambert v. State

Post-conviction proceeding at, Remanded by Lambert v. State, 2003 OK CR 11, 71 P.3d 30, 2003 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11 (Okla. Crim. App., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Lambert v. Workman, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56629 (N.D. Okla., July 2, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CREEK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DONALD D. THOMPSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Lambert v. State, 1991 OK CR 22, 808 P.2d 72, 1991 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Okla. Crim. App., 1991)



DISPOSITION: The Judgments and Sentences on both counts of First Degree Murder are AFFIRMED. The Judgments and Sentences for two counts of Robbery with a Dangerous Weapon are VACATED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his death sentence and his convictions on two counts of first-degree murder entered by the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: On retrial, defendant again was found guilty of first degree murder on an amended information charging him with first degree malice murder or first degree felony murder. Because defendant was charged in the alternative, the court affirmed his convictions as felony murder convictions and affirmed his death penalty. To avoid multiple punishment, the court vacated robbery convictions that earlier were affirmed but had become the felonies underlying the second murder convictions. Defendant's eight year old mental age was not a per se bar to admissibility of his confession. Testimony of prison employees about his competence was admissible as lay opinion testimony since the witnesses did not specifically state he was competent to stand trial. Failure of his counsel to move for a change of venue was not ineffective assistance because jurors who had heard of the case affirmed they could be objective. Reference by a state witness to defendant's arson while in jail and attempted sexual assault while a young adolescent was impermissible but harmless error. Execution of a mentally retarded person such as defendant would not violate Oklahoma or federal constitutions.


OUTCOME: The death penalty for defendant upon his first-degree murder convictions was affirmed. Mental retardation was not a per se bar to admission of his confession, and execution of a mentally retarded person would not violate Oklahoma or federal constitutions.

Short v. State


No. F-97-540


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 15; 980 P.2d 1081; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 47; 70 O.B.A.J. 1223



April 14, 1999, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 21, 1999. Certiorari Denied January 10, 2000, Reported at: 2000 U.S. LEXIS 268.
Writ of certiorari denied Short v. Oklahoma, 528 U.S. 1085, 120 S. Ct. 811, 145 L. Ed. 2d 683, 2000 U.S. LEXIS 268 (2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Short v. Sirmons, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 31758 (10th Cir. Okla., Dec. 26, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: JUDGMENTS and SENTENCES AFFIRMED and the APPLICATION FOR EVIDENTIARY HEARING ON SIXTH AMENDMENT CLAIMS IS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed imposition of the death penalty and his conviction before the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) for first-degree murder and on five counts of attempting to kill after former conviction of two or more felonies.


OVERVIEW: Defendant allegedly threw a firebomb into an apartment. An apartment on the next floor collapsed into the fire, and the resident of that apartment died. Defendant's murder conviction and death penalty were affirmed. Although defendant was declared competent to stand trial under an unconstitutional standard, evidence supported a finding that defendant was competent even under the constitutional preponderance of the evidence standard. Exclusion of a witness who would contradict testimony of defendant's cellmate describing defendant's confession was permissible because the potential witness was listed on a handwritten note to the prosecutor rather than in defendant's discovery response. The confession was admissible because its trustworthiness was supported by testimony of two occupants of the apartment. Failure to instruct the jury on the need for corroboration was not prejudicial. Argument that it was unjust to allow defendant to live while the victim's mother grieved was improper but did not affect the jury's imposition of the death sentence. The court would not question defense counsel's abandonment of the defense that the fire occurred in a home laboratory for illegal drugs.


OUTCOME: Defendant's first-degree murder conviction and death penalty were affirmed. Evidence supported defendant's jail house confession, a defense witness to contradict the confession not properly listed in a discovery response was permissibly excluded, and trial court and defense counsel errors were not prejudicial.

 

699 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Young


No. S-98-212, No. S-98-344


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 14; 989 P.2d 949; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 12; 70 O.B.A.J. 1076



April 5, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant prosecution sought review of two judgments of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which affirmed the ruling of the magistrate sustaining criminal appellee one and twos' demurrers to their indictments of five counts of false claims against the state in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 358 (1991). Criminal appellee one filed a motion to dismiss the appeal.


OVERVIEW: Criminal appellee one and two were charged with five counts of false claims against the state in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 358 (1991). The magistrate sustained their demurrer to the indictment. The trial court affirmed the magistrate's rulings, including the finding that the funds of the Oklahoma State Insurance Fund were not public funds pursuant to § 358. Appellant sought review and criminal appellee one filed a motion to dismiss the appeal. While the court found that appellant had the right to appeal the magistrate's adverse ruling, it found that the state appealed under the wrong statute. Thus, appellant failed to follow the correct procedures to appeal the decision as set forth in Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1053 (1991) and its appeal was not timely filed. Thus, the motion to dismiss was granted. As to criminal appellee two, the court affirmed the district court's judgment. Reviewing relevant case law and legislative history, the court held that the funds of the Oklahoma State Insurance Fund were not public funds insofar as they were not available for public use or purposes. Thus, they were not public funds as defined in § 358 and the demurrer was properly sustained.


OUTCOME: Criminal appellee one's motion to dismiss appellant prosecution's appeal was granted because appellant failed to file its appeal under the proper statute, which resulted in the appeal being untimely filed. Judgment affirming the sustaining of criminal appellee two's demurrer was affirmed because the funds of the Oklahoma State Insurance Fund were not public funds as required for a violation of the false claims against the state statute.

White v. State


No. F-89-566


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 10; 990 P.2d 253; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 9; 70 O.B.A.J. 870



March 10, 1999, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKMULGEE COUNTY THE HONORABLE JOHN MALEY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED as to guilt but REMANDED for RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of an Okmulgee County District Court (Oklahoma) decision that, after a jury trial, convicted appellant of first degree murder and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant challenged a trial court decision that convicted him of first degree murder after a jury trial and sentenced him to death. The appellate court affirmed appellant's conviction but remanded for resentencing. The trial court committed reversible error by refusing to give jury instructions on all sentencing options provided by law, including the alternative life imprisonment without parole option. Appellant was properly found competent to stand trial after a retrospective post-examination competency hearing. Appellant's retrospective competency hearing did not violate appellant's due process rights as finding appellant competent to participate in criminal proceedings was based on substantial evidence. Appellant's rights were not interfered with and he was not prejudiced by his erroneous non-presence at the final day of this competency hearing. Appellant also failed to establish that the prosecution committed discrimination against Native Americans by striking the only minority members of the jury panel as the prosecution provided a sufficient race-neutral explanation for striking the minority jury panel members.


OUTCOME: The appellate court affirmed a trial court decision that convicted appellant of first degree murder but reversed the imposed death sentence after finding that the trial court failed to instruct the jury of all sentencing options. Appellant's competency to take part in criminal proceedings was established by substantial evidence and the prosecution offered sufficient race-neutral reasons for striking the only minority jury panelists.

Stewart v. State


Case No. H 98-1013


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 9; 989 P.2d 940; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8; 70 O.B.A.J. 795



March 9, 1999, Decided  
March 9, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Writ of Habeas Corpus GRANTED. Petitioner's Judgment and Sentences in CF 97-1817 VACATED and matter REMANDED to District Court of Oklahoma County for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order from the Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma), denying his petition for a writ of habeas corpus. Defendant pled guilty to drug possession, driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor, and driving under revocation. Defendant claimed the sentence was void where the trial court exceeded its statutory authority by sentencing him to prison following his failure to complete a night-time incarceration sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to drug possession, driving under the influence of intoxicating liquor, and driving under revocation. The trial court imposed a night-time incarceration sentence under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 991a-2. Defendant did not complete the sentence, and the trial court sentenced defendant to prison. Defendant petitioned for a writ of habeas corpus, which was denied. Defendant appealed, claiming the sentence was void where the night-time sentence imposed was a form of suspended sentence for which defendant was ineligible. Defendant claimed that the most the trial court could do was compel defendant's completion of the night-time sentence. The court vacated the sentences and remanded, holding that where the statute did not provide consequences for noncompliance, imposition of a prison sentence was improper. Because defendant was not eligible for night-time sentencing due to his prior felony convictions, remand was ordered to allow defendant to withdraw his pleas and to be sentenced accordingly.


OUTCOME: The court granted defendant's habeas corpus petition, vacating the trial court's judgment and sentences against defendant. Because night-time incarceration was a form of suspended sentencing for which defendant was ineligible, the trial court improperly sentenced defendant to prison following his failure to complete night-time incarceration. Remand was granted to allow withdrawal of defendant's pleas and for appropriate sentencing.

 

702 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Huskey v. State


Case No. F-97-1541, Case No. F-97-1548


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 3; 989 P.2d 1; 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1; 70 O.B.A.J. 242



January 8, 1999, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants sought review of their convictions and sentences from the District Court of Bryan County (Oklahoma) for child abuse in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 7115 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: Appellants were jointly accused of child abuse. The information specified that the particular form of abuse charged was mental injury through exposure to explicit adult sexual conduct and acts, and by failure to prevent the same. In their trial, over appellants' objection, a jury instruction did not include "force or require" in the elements of lewd or indecent acts, the third overall element of sexual abuse. Appellants' convictions and sentences under Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 7115 (Supp. 1995) were affirmed. The legislature specifically intended the § 7115 crime of child abuse, when accomplished through lewd or indecent acts, to include "allowed or permitted," rather than include the "force or require" element. The jury was correctly instructed on the crimes of sexual exploitation and sexual abuse, which were specifically included in § 7115. There could be no credible claim that appellant had no notice of the charges against them.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions because the trial court correctly instructed the jury on the crime of child abuse through sexual abuse by exposure to lewd and indecent acts, as well as sexual exploitation.

 

703 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


C.R.B. v. State


No. J 98-0701


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1999 OK CR 1; 973 P.2d 339; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 73; 70 O.B.A.J. 234



December 31, 1998, Decided


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of the judgment of the trial court (Oklahoma), denying her motion for certification as a youthful offender under the Youthful Offender Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 7306-2.1 (Supp. 1997), after being charged as an adult with murder in the first degree.


OVERVIEW: Appellant, who was 17 years old, was charged as an adult with murder in the first degree. The trial court denied her motion for certification as a youthful offender pursuant to the Youthful Offender Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 7306-2.1 (Supp. 1997), and appellant sought review. The court remanded, finding that there was an insufficient record to review whether the trial court properly considered the statutory guidelines set out in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, § 7306-2.5(D) (Supp. 1997), in denying certification. Accordingly, the court held that it would require detailed findings of fact and conclusions of law as to each of the certification guidelines, as referred to in Okla. Stat. tit. 10, §§ 7306-2.8(C), 7306-2.9(A)(1), as well as the trial court's statement that it had considered each of the guidelines in reaching its decision.


OUTCOME: The court remanded to the trial court for a full adversarial hearing for determination whether appellant should be treated as a youthful offender, and ordered the trial court to issue an order with detailed findings of fact as to each of the guidelines and conclusions of law.

 

704 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Patton v. State


No. F-96-1460


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 66; 973 P.2d 270; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64; 69 O.B.A.J. 4283



December 9, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 17, 1999.
Rehearing denied by, 03/17/1999
Post-conviction relief denied at Patton v. State, 1999 OK CR 25, 989 P.2d 983, 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 55 (Okla. Crim. App., 1999)
Writ of certiorari denied Patton v. Oklahoma, 528 U.S. 939, 145 L. Ed. 2d 271, 120 S. Ct. 347, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6736 (1999)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Patton v. Mullin, 2005 U.S. App. LEXIS 20276 (10th Cir. Okla., Sept. 21, 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LEAMON FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: FINDING NO ERROR WARRANTING REVERSAL OR MODIFICATION, JUDGMENT AND SENTENCES FOR FIRST DEGREE MURDER AND FIRST DEGREE BURGLARY ARE AFFIRMED AND APPLICATION FOR EVIDENTIARY HEARING ON SIXTH AMENDMENT CLAIMS IS DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After a jury trial in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), appellant was convicted of first-degree murder and of first-degree burglary after former conviction of two or more felonies. Appellant, whose death sentence entitled him to mandatory sentence review under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13 (1991), challenged the judgment and sentence on numerous grounds.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was sentenced to death after being convicted of first-degree murder and first-degree burglary after former conviction of two or more felonies. The court affirmed his conviction and sentence, also conducting a mandatory sentence review under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.13 (1991). It rejected his claims that the trial court erred in restricting the scope of voir dire, in removing jurors and prospective jurors and failing to remove others, in limiting his cross-examination, and in admitting certain photographs. It found that the evidence supported his convictions and the jury's findings regarding aggravating factors, that the jury instructions were proper, that he was not denied a fair trial, that his counsel was not ineffective and that his allegations of ineffective assistance did not warrant an evidentiary hearing, and that the cumulative effect of any errors did not require reversal. Concluding that the death sentence was factually substantiated and appropriate, it also held that the trial court's report filed for mandatory sentence review purposes, when combined with the rest of the record, contained sufficient information on which the court to base its review.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's convictions for first-degree murder and first-degree burglary, rejecting appellant's numerous charges of error by the trial court and finding that his claims of ineffective assistance did not warrant an evidentiary hearing. Conducting a mandatory sentence review, it concluded that appellant's death sentence was factually substantiated and appropriate.

Slaughter v. State

DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of various counts of first degree murder and perjury in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), and the jury recommended the punishment of death. The appellate court affirmed the judgments and sentences. Petitioner filed an original application for post-conviction relief in the appellate court.


OVERVIEW: The appellate court determined that there existed no controverted, previously unresolved factual issues material to the legality of petitioner's confinement. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(D)(4)(a)(1), (2), (3) (Supp. 1995). Most of petitioner's claims could have been raised on direct appeal, and those that were raised were barred by res judicata.


OUTCOME: The application was denied.

Cummings v. State


No. PC-98-134


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 60; 970 P.2d 188; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 59; 69 O.B.A.J. 3979



November 10, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Cummings v. State, 1998 OK CR 45, 968 P.2d 821, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 43 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief DENIED. Petitioner's request to keep the record open DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant's conviction in the District Court of Coal County (Oklahoma) of first degree malice murder and first degree felony murder was affirmed. He filed an application with the appellate court for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's claim of factual innocence was not based on evidence not discoverable on direct appeal, nor did it contain specific facts supporting such innocence. Defendant's ineffective assistance of trial counsel claim did not turn on facts unavailable on appeal. Appellate counsel's failure to litigate defendant's ineffectiveness of trial counsel claim as fully as defendant felt he should did not render counsel's assistance unreasonable. Prosecutorial misconduct was either raised on appeal or could have been. Defendant's ineffective assistance and prosecutorial misconduct claims as to sentencing were already determined. The constitutionality of the aggravating circumstance not overruled on appeal was already addressed. Jury instructions at sentencing could have been raised on appeal. Acts or omissions denying defendant a fair trial and sentencing were or could have been raised on appeal. Seating an unqualified juror could have been raised on appeal. The Oklahoma Post-Conviction Procedure Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1088 et seq., was constitutional. Defendant's claim that Oklahoma's clemency scheme was unconstitutional was not cognizable on post-conviction review.


OUTCOME: Defendant's application for post-conviction relief was denied.

 

707 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Young v. State


Case No. F-95-1142


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 62; 992 P.2d 332; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 57; 69 O.B.A.J. 3903



November 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Young v. Oklahoma, 528 U.S. 837, 120 S. Ct. 100, 145 L. Ed. 2d 84, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 5289 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Young v. Sirmons, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 57071 (N.D. Okla., Aug. 2, 2007)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder and one count of first degree burglary by the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma). He appealed his conviction charging numerous errors.


OVERVIEW: Following the second stage of trial, the jury found three aggravating circumstances and set punishment at death for each of the murders committed by defendant and fifty years imprisonment for the burglary. Defendant claimed that he was denied due process by the trial court's error in denying challenges to veniremen for cause necessitating the use of peremptory challenges. He also claimed that the search warrant executed at the home of his mother where he was residing, which produced blood stained clothing, was invalid. The appellate court held that there was no denial of due process because defendant never explained why the veniremen he claims he was unable to remove due to a lack of peremptory challenges were unacceptable and therefore failed to demonstrate any prejudice from the alleged error. The court further determined that, under the totality of the circumstances, the magistrate's decision to issue the search warrant was supported by probable cause to believe evidence of wrongdoing would be found at the home of appellant's mother, including a broken door chain seen by the victim's relative, which connected defendant to the crime, and the fact he changed clothes there.


OUTCOME: The judgment of conviction and sentence were affirmed.

McCarty v. State


Case No. F-96-503


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 61; 977 P.2d 1116; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 56; 69 O.B.A.J. 3886



November 6, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 26, 1999, Reported at: 1999 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 45. Certiorari Denied November 15, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 7615.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE, DANIEL L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The sentence of death AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County, Oklahoma, which entered a death penalty sentence against defendant. The twenty something year old defendant argued that the trial court erred in allowing the uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice witness concerning the murder of a seven year old girl and a prior guilty plea to statutory rape concerning the issue of continuing threat to society aggravator.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, a twenty something year old, was convicted of raping and murdering an 18 year old girl. Defendant had always claimed that another unknown accomplice had actually knifed and strangled the girl. The case had been reversed for a new punishment trial. At the new trial, the trial court allowed an accomplice witness who had been convicted of murdering a seven-year-old girl to testify that defendant had actually committed the murder. Defendant had agreed with the state to testify against that accomplice witness in exchange for immunity. The trial court had never confirmed that agreement. The court affirmed defendant's death penalty sentence. The court held that at the punishment phase, the trial court could allow the uncorroborated testimony of the accomplice witness and defendant did not have immunity because the trial court had never confirmed the immunity agreement. The court also stated that another girl with whom the defendant had sexual intercourse was allowed to testify that defendant had threatened her, although he never pled guilty to an aggravated charge. The court concluded that defendant could not argue that he didn't do it at the punishment phase.


OUTCOME: The court confirmed defendant's death penalty sentence. The court held that the jury was justified in sentencing defendant, a twenty something year old, to death because of the uncorroborated testimony of an accomplice witness stating that defendant actually murdered a seven year old girl, a teen aged girl's testimony that defendant threatened her when they had sexual intercourse, and the circumstances of the eighteen year old girl's murder.

Miller v. State


Case No. F 96-1380


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 59; 977 P.2d 1099; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 58; 69 O.B.A.J. 3876



November 5, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6177. Rehearing Denied & Denied February 19, 1999.
Rehearing granted by, 02/19/1999
Writ of certiorari denied Miller v. Oklahoma, 528 U.S. 897, 145 L. Ed. 2d 192, 120 S. Ct. 228, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6177 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Miller v. Mullin, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 873 (10th Cir. Okla., Jan. 21, 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Oklahoma County District Court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree murder, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.10 (1991), and sentenced him to death after it found aggravating circumstances. At issue was whether the factors were supported by the evidence and whether the sentence was influenced by passion, prejudice, or an arbitrary factor.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murder in the district court and sentenced to death. He was before the court on original appeal from the judgment and sentence, which were affirmed. The jury found aggravating circumstances: 1) at the time of the crime defendant was previously convicted of a felony involving the use or threat of violence to the person; 2) the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel; 3) the murder was committed for the purpose of avoiding or preventing a lawful arrest or prosecution; and 4) there exists a probability that defendant would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society. The court found the aggravating factors were supported by the evidence. The only error which possibly injected prejudice into the trial was the testimony of the victim's mother in which she recounted two dreams in which her dead son appeared to her. However, in the emotionally wrenching but fair context of the parents' testimony regarding their anguish caused by the murder, the testimony could not have had any improper influence on the jury. Therefore, the sentence of death was not influenced by passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The judgment and sentence were affirmed. The court found the aggravating factors were supported by the evidence, and the sentence of death was not influenced by passion, prejudice, or any arbitrary factor. In an emotionally wrenching but fair context, the parents' testimony regarding their anguish caused by their son's murder and the mother's recounting of two dreams in which her dead son appeared to her had not improperly influenced the jury.

Welch v. State


No. PC-97-1486


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 58; 972 P.2d 26; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 54; 69 O.B.A.J. 3806



October 23, 1998, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] FOR PUBLICATION.
Writ of habeas corpus denied Welch v. Sirmons, 2007 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 21634 (N.D. Okla., Mar. 26, 2007)


PRIOR HISTORY: This Opinion Substituted by the Court for Withdrawn Opinion of October 7, 1998, Previously Reported at: 1998 OK CR 55, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 53.
Welch v. State, 1998 OK CR 55, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 53 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)
Conover v. State, 1997 OK CR 6, 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 22, 68 Okla. B.J. 1296 (Okla. Crim. App., 1997)



DISPOSITION: DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant had appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Ottawa County, Oklahoma, that convicted him on a jury verdict of first degree murder and sentenced him to death. After his direct appeal was denied, he filed an application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: The instant court rejected all of defendant's post-conviction claims. The Post-Conviction Procedure Act did not unconstitutionally limit defendant's access to the courts, or deny him due process and equal protection. Issues of ineffective assistance of trial counsel, omission of a jury instruction, and defendant's right to post-arrest silence, were raised and rejected on direct appeal. Further consideration of them was thus barred by res judicata. The issue of the admission of other crimes evidence, while not raised on direct appeal, could have been, and was thus waived. As to the issue of the ineffectiveness of appellate counsel, that this counsel was not successful in the appeal was not proof of his ineffectiveness. Appellate counsel's failure to raise certain non-frivolous claims was not unreasonable under prevailing professional norms. Defendant was not entitled to an evidentiary hearing on the issue of whether trial counsel failed to present evidence about defendant's abusive background, as this was an issue that could have been raised on direct appeal.


OUTCOME: The petition was denied.

Cummings v. State


No. F-96-657


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 45; 968 P.2d 821; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 43; 69 O.B.A.J. 2901



August 4, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied November 3, 1998. Certiorari Denied June 7, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3891.
Post-conviction relief denied at Cummings v. State, 1998 OK CR 60, 970 P.2d 188, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 59 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Cummings v. Oklahoma, 526 U.S. 1162, 119 S. Ct. 2054, 144 L. Ed. 2d 220, 1999 U.S. LEXIS 3891 (1999)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cummings v. Gibson, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 56793 (E.D. Okla., Aug. 10, 2006)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Count I is REVERSED with instructions to DISMISS. Count II is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Coal County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first degree malice aforethought murder for killing his sister and first degree felony murder (kidnapping) for killing his niece and sentencing him to death. Defendant was also charged with child abuse for raping the niece before the murder, but this count was dismissed at trial.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with two counts of first degree malice murder for killing his sister and niece. A magistrate dismissed without prejudice the malice murder count for the niece's murder for lack of venue, which was upheld on appeal. An amended information was filed charging defendant with malice murder and felony murder (kidnapping) for the niece's murder. At a jury trial, defendant was convicted and was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court reversed the conviction on the malice murder count because it was based upon the uncorroborated accomplice testimony of defendant's wives. However, the court affirmed the conviction and sentence on the felony murder count. The court held that because one of the wives was not an accomplice to the niece's murder, her testimony was sufficient to corroborate the accomplice testimony of the other wife on the felony murder count. The court held that the evidence was sufficient to prove the predicate felony of kidnapping. The court ruled that the seizure of notebooks and handcuffs from defendant's home did not violate his Fourth Amendment rights because police had reason to believe that one of the wives had authority to consent to a search.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of first degree malice aforethought murder and sentencing him to death for that count, but it affirmed the judgment convicting him of first degree felony murder and sentencing him to death for that count. The court remanded the case with instructions to dismiss the malice murder count.

Allen v. City of Oklahoma City


Case No. C-97-1678


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 42; 965 P.2d 387; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 37; 69 O.B.A.J. 2520



July 6, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED and REMANDED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order from the Oklahoma City Municipal Court Case (Oklahoma), which denied his request to withdraw his guilty plea to a charge of offering to engage in an act of lewdness. Defendant alleged that Oklahoma City, Okla., Rev. Ordinances art. VII, §§ 30-151 and 152 (1993), were unconstitutionally overbroad and impaired constitutionally protected free speech.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pleaded no contest to offering to engage in an act of lewdness in violation of the Ordinance. The trial judge sentenced defendant to jail and imposed a fine. Defendant subsequently filed an application to withdraw his guilty plea and the trial court denied the request. On appeal, the court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion to withdraw the plea but remanded the cause to the trial court for a consideration of all of its sentencing options. The court held that because the trial judge stated on the record that he did not believe he had the discretion to suspend or defer defendant's sentence, the cause had to be remanded for resentencing. In doing so, the court stressed that it did not find error in the trial court's failure to suspend or defer defendant's sentence, but rather in the trial court's failure to consider those options. The court further held that it was irrelevant that no evidentiary hearing was held on defendant's motion to withdraw his plea because defendant was not challenging the voluntariness of his plea or in any way contending that it was entered.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the order denying defendant's motion to withdraw his plea to a charge of offering to engage in an act of lewdness but remanded the cause for resentencing.

DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence for First Degree Murder AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), in which he was found guilty of two counts of first degree murder with malice aforethought, in violation of 21 Okla. Stat. § 701.7(A), and one count of first degree burglary, in violation of 21 Okla. Stat. § 1431. Stat. § 701.7(A), and one count of first degree burglary, in violation of 21 Okla. Stat. § 1431. He raised a laundry list of errors including his competency to stand trial, errors during jury selection, due process violations, and evidence error. The court found that the evidence did not support the conclusion that defendant constituted a continuing threat to society because defendant had never been convicted of a crime and the prosecution's showing that he was a gang member was insufficient. Nevertheless, the court affirmed the death sentence imposed on defendant after finding that the remaining aggravating circumstance, that defendant caused the death of more than one person, outweighed the mitigating evidence produced by defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions and the death sentence imposed on him by the trial court, although it found that one of the aggravating circumstances relied on by the trial court was not supported by the evidence. The evidence was insufficient to show that defendant represented a continuing threat to society, but the court determined that the remaining aggravating circumstance still outweighed the mitigating circumstances.

Post-conviction relief denied at Torres v. State, 2002 OK CR 35, 58 P.3d 214, 2002 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 40 (Okla. Crim. App., 2002)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Torres v. Mullin, 317 F.3d 1145, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 1069 (10th Cir. Okla., 2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Torres v. State, 2005 OK CR 17, 120 P.3d 1184, 2005 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 12 (Okla. Crim. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Ochoa v. State, 1998 OK CR 41, 963 P.2d 583, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 39 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him on a jury verdict of two counts of first-degree murder with malice aforethought in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 and one count of first-degree burglary in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1431. The defendant was sentenced to death for both murders and to 20 years imprisonment for the burglary.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued, inter alia, that the Designation of Record included the transcript of his earlier mistrial, that his warrantless arrest was invalid, that color photographs were improperly admitted, and that his counsel was ineffective. The court held that the appellate record referred only to the second trial because defendant's appellate counsel failed to file a timely supplemental designation of record. There was probable cause to arrest defendant because the arresting officer heard the description of defendants over the radio prior to arresting them and he found defendants a short distance from the murder scene, perspiring and with blood on their clothes. The trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting color photographs because they were probative of the nature and extent of the wounds on the victims, they corroborated the medical examiner's testimony, depicted the crime scene, and established corpus delicti. Defendant's trial counsel was not ineffective in failing to suppress identification testimony because there was ample evidence that the witness had accurately identified defendant and her identification had been unwavering.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the conviction of defendant for first-degree murder and for first-degree burglary and the imposition of the death sentence.

Cannon v. State


No. F-96-369

1998 OK CR 28; 961 P.2d 838; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 26; 69 O.B.A.J. 1803

Habeas corpus proceeding at, Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by, in part Cannon v. Mullin, 383 F.3d 1152, 2004 U.S. App. LEXIS 19224 (10th Cir. Okla., 2004)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CLIFFORD E. HOPPER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first degree murder under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1991) for the stabbing death of his girlfriend and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree murder for the stabbing death of his girlfriend. At a jury trial, defendant was convicted and sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the judgment and sentence. The court ruled that defendant was not denied the right to life-qualify prospective jurors on voir dire. The court held that opinion testimony from a detective was admissible because the jury was not told what conclusion to reach. The court held that the trial court's deviation from the uniform instruction on heat of passion manslaughter was harmless error because the jury instructions as a whole fairly and accurately stated the applicable law. The court ruled that the State's notice of its victim impact evidence was deficient but that it did not prevent defendant from effectively using his peremptory challenges. The court also held that the sentence was not arbitrarily imposed, that the evidence supported the finding of the aggravating circumstances and that they outweighed the mitigating factors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court convicting defendant of first degree murder and sentencing him to death.
