Hain v. State


No. PC-97-611


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 27; 962 P.2d 649; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 29; 69 O.B.A.J. 1698



May 1, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed his original application for post-conviction Relief with the court under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (Supp. 1995).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree murder, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981), kidnapping, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21 § 741 (1981), robbery with a firearm, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21 § 801 (1981), third degree arson, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1403 (1981), and larceny of an automobile, under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1720 (1981). The court denied the post-conviction relief and held that the information forming the basis of the claims was either available to direct appeal counsel, or could have been obtained by counsel for purposes of raising the issues on appeal. Because the basis for the claim did not require factfinding outside the scope of information available to counsel at the time of the direct appeal, defendant's claims of ineffective assistance of trial counsel were waived because they could have been raised on direct appeal but were not. The court could not find appellate counsel's failure to raise the claims at issue here rendered his performance unreasonable under prevailing professional norms.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's request for post-conviction relief from his conviction for murder, kidnapping, robbery with a firearm, arson, and larceny of an automobile.

 

717 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Lewis v. State


No. F-96-85


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 24; 970 P.2d 1158; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24; 69 O.B.A.J. 1501



April 15, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied October 4, 1999, Reported at: 1999 U.S. LEXIS 6106. Rehearing Denied February 9, 1999. As Corrected February 3, 1999.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD W. FREEMAN PRESIDING.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of first degree murder and child abuse for killing his girlfriend and severely injuring her six year old daughter by throwing gasoline on them and setting them on fire. Defendant also appealed from the trial court's judgment sentencing him to death on the murder count and to life imprisonment on the child abuse count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first-degree murder and child abuse for killing his girlfriend and injuring her daughter by throwing gasoline on them and setting them on fire. After his arrest, defendant confessed to police. At a jury trial, defendant was convicted and sentenced to death for the murder count. On appeal, the court affirmed the convictions and sentences. The court ruled that one prospective juror was properly removed for cause as he indicated that he could not impose the death penalty. The court held that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in refusing to conduct a sequestered voir dire due to pretrial publicity. The court held that an expert witness improperly relied upon threatening phone calls in forming his opinion regarding defendant's sanity as there was no evidence that defendant made the calls. However, the admission of this testimony was harmless error because it did not substantially influence the outcome of the trial. The court ruled that defendant's confession was admissible because he made a knowing and intelligent waiver of his Miranda rights before confessing. The court also held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment convicting defendant of first degree murder and child abuse and sentencing him to death for the murder conviction and to life imprisonment for the child abuse conviction.

 

718 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Smith v. State


No. PC-97-982


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 20; 955 P.2d 734; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 20; 69 O.B.A.J. 1217



March 24, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied, in part, Writ of habeas corpus dismissed, in part Smith v. Gibson, 2002 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 27527 (W.D. Okla., Jan. 10, 2002)


PRIOR HISTORY: Smith v. Oklahoma, 521 U.S. 1124, 138 L. Ed. 2d 1023, 117 S. Ct. 2522, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4148 (1997)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Application for Post-Conviction Relief, Request for Evidentiary Hearing and Request for Discovery are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought post-conviction relief from his convictions on five counts of first degree murder and a death sentence resulting from those convictions. Petitioner previously appealed the judgment and sentence, which were affirmed by the court. Petitioner's arguments in his post-conviction relief petition included denial of a fair trial, deprivation of his right to due process, and ineffective assistance of counsel at trial and on appeal.


OVERVIEW: After petitioner challenged his convictions and sentencing on five counts of first-degree murder on direct appeal, he sought post-conviction relief, requesting an evidentiary hearing and discovery. The court denied the petition and the requests for an evidentiary hearing and discovery. The court held that petitioner failed to raise several issues which formed the basis of his post-conviction relief petition on direct appeal, when such issues could have been raised in that forum; therefore, the issues were waived and barred from post-conviction review. In addition, the court held petitioner had not demonstrated that appellate counsel's failure to raise certain issues on direct appeal rendered her performance unreasonable under prevailing norms. Finally, the court held that it had not erred in refusing to permit an evidentiary hearing during petitioner's direct appeal regarding the issue of petitioner's competency to stand trial upon a finding that the trial court had unconstitutionally required petitioner to prove his competence by clear and convincing evidence.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief, request for evidentiary hearing and request for discovery.

 

719 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Darks v. State


Case No. PC-97-1077


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 21; 954 P.2d 169; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 16; 69 O.B.A.J. 1214



March 19, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of habeas corpus denied Darks v. Mullin, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 6977 (10th Cir. Okla., Apr. 11, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY: Darks v. State, 1998 OK CR 15, 954 P.2d 152, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for post-conviction relief together with a request for an evidentiary hearing and a request for discovery. Petitioner was convicted of first degree murder with malice aforethought and was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that he was denied effective assistance of both appellate and trial counsel. Upon review, the court found that while he established that the conduct supporting his allegations of appellate counsel's ineffectiveness occurred, he failed to present facts that showed that his counsel was unreasonable under the circumstances, that his conduct did not fall within range of professional assistance, or that counsel breached a duty to him. Because his claims of the ineffective assistance of trial counsel were raised and addressed on direct appeal, the claims were barred by res judicata. Even though petitioner's arguments were different than those presented on direct appeal, the court could not address them because they did not turn on facts or information unavailable at the time of his direct appeal. The court found no material facts that would have warranted an evidentiary hearing to resolve factual issues petitioner claimed were in dispute. The court found that it did not have the authority to grant his discovery requests because they were not related to an issue, which could have been raised within the scope of Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (1995).


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief, his request for an evidentiary hearing, and his request for discovery.

 

720 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Wood v. State


Case No. F-95-759


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 19; 959 P.2d 1; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18; 69 O.B.A.J. 1030



March 11, 1998, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied April 20, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GREER COUNTY THE HONORABLE CHARLES GOODWIN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant was tried in the District Court of Greer County (Oklahoma) and convicted by jury of the crime of murder in the first degree, malice aforethought. In his sentencing hearing the jury found four aggravating circumstances, set punishment at death by lethal injection, and the trial judge sentenced appellant accordingly. Appellant sought review of his judgment and sentence.


OVERVIEW: Appellant stabbed a fellow inmate to death in the state reformatory. The evidence at trial was based on eyewitness accounts of the stabbing, appellant's alleged confession to another inmate and forensic evidence of the victim's blood on a shirt found under appellant's bunk. On appeal, appellant contended that the trial judge committed reversible error during voir dire, erred in admitting appellant's confession, and erred in admitting hearsay and DNA evidence. He also argued the violation of his constitutional rights, insufficient evidence, ineffective assistance of counsel, and sentencing errors. The court found that there were no trial court errors that warranted reversal. The court also held that, upon carefully considering and reviewing the evidence which supported the aggravating circumstances, as well as the evidence which may be considered mitigating, the sentence of death was factually substantiated and appropriate. The sentence of death was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed appellant's conviction for first-degree murder and the imposition of the death sentence.

 

721 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert v. State


No. PC-97-1158


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 17; 955 P.2d 727; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 15; 69 O.B.A.J. 940



March 10, 1998 


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma) of first-degree malice aforethought murder, kidnapping, and robbery with firearms. He was sentenced to death on the murder charge and to life imprisonment on the other charges. Defendant sought post-conviction relief, arguing primarily ineffective assistance of counsel. Defendant also applied for an evidentiary hearing and for discovery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree malice aforethought murder, kidnapping, and robbery with firearms. The jury found two aggravating circumstances in the murder charge and sentenced defendant to death. Defendant sought post-conviction review, first alleging ineffective assistance of counsel. The court found that counsel raised all relevant issues for consideration and was not under an obligation to raise all available issues. The court concluded that defendant could not show that counsel's performance was deficient. Defendant also claimed that the aggravator finding him a continuing threat was unconstitutional. The court rejected this argument, holding that the Tenth Circuit had upheld the constitutional validity of the aggravator. The court found that certain of defendant's claims were already raised on direct appeal and thus were barred by the doctrine of res judicata. The court denied defendant's application for an evidentiary hearing and discovery because defendant could not show that the materials to be introduced had or were likely to have support in law and fact to be relevant to an allegation raised in the application for post-conviction relief.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's applications for post-conviction relief and for an evidentiary hearing and discovery.

 

722 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Douglas v. State


No. PC-97-659


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 12; 953 P.2d 349; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6; 69 O.B.A.J. 510



January 23, 1998, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY: Douglas v. State, 1997 OK CR 79, 951 P.2d 651, 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 79 (Okla. Crim. App., Dec. 17, 1997)



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for post-conviction relief together with requests for discovery and an evidentiary hearing. Petitioner was convicted of murder in the first degree and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that he was denied his right to effective assistance of trial and appellate counsels. Petitioner appealed his conviction, and it was affirmed on appeal. Upon review, the court found that while some of the facts in support of the claim were not in the direct appeal record, there was no evidence that those facts were not available on direct appeal. Petitioner failed to meet the pre-conditions for review of his claim on the merits. Petitioner claimed that appellate counsel failed to ensure a compete record was filed on appeal and failed to properly raise and preserve meritorious issues. Petitioner established that appellate counsel committed conduct that gave rise to the allegations, but he failed to assert facts and law, which would have enabled the court to assess counsel's allegedly deficient performance. He offered no facts, which showed that she breached a duty to him or that her judgment was unreasonable under the circumstances. The court found that because controverted previously unresolved factual issues material to the legality of petitioner's confinement existed, there was no need to order discovery or an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief and his requests for discovery and an evidentiary hearing.

 

723 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Battenfield v. State


No. PC-97-732


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 8; 953 P.2d 1123; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5; 69 O.B.A.J. 513



January 21, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted of first degree malice aforethought murder by the District Court of Wagoner County (Oklahoma) and sentenced to death. Defendant's conviction and sentence were upheld on appeal, and the United States Supreme Court denied a petition for writ of certiorari. The lower court denied defendant's petition for post-conviction relief. Defendant appealed, claiming he was denied effective assistance of trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree malice aforethought murder, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701, and was sentenced to death. Defendant sought post-conviction relief, primarily claiming that trial and appellate counsel were ineffective. The lower court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief, and he sought review. On review, the court rejected defendant's claims that the performances of counsel were substandard and that defendant was prejudiced by counsels' errors. For example, defendant claimed that trial counsel was ineffective for failing to present mitigating evidence on his behalf. The record showed that defendant refused to testify on his own behalf and refused to allow counsel to call certain witnesses on his behalf. The court also found that appellate counsel's failure to challenge trial counsel was sound strategy. Appellate counsel was focusing on areas that he felt were the most meritorious in overturning defendant's conviction. The court concluded that appellate counsel's failure to raise every possible issue on appeal was not an indication of ineffective representation.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's denial of post-conviction relief to defendant.

 

724 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Charm v. State


Case No. PC-97-838


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 2; 953 P.2d 47; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1; 69 O.B.A.J. 150



January 6, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for post-conviction relief, a request for an evidentiary hearing, and a request for discovery. Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder with malice aforethought, first-degree rape, and kidnapping. He was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that the evidence was insufficient to support his convictions and that his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective. Upon review, the court found that petitioner's claims that his confession was not reliable, that his confession was not corroborated, and that the state failed to prove the corpus delicti of rape and kidnapping were issues that could have been raised on direct appeal. Thus, the claims were waived and barred from review under Okla. Stat. § 1089(C). Petitioner's claims that the evidence was insufficient to support the aggravating circumstances for the death sentence were raised on direct appeal and res judicata barred further litigation of those claims. Appellate counsel did fail to raise the issue of insufficient evidence on direct appeal. However, nothing in the record indicated that she was less than a diligent, able advocate for petitioner or that she breached her professional duties. Petitioner's allegations of the ineffectiveness of trial counsel did not require factfinding outside the scope of information available to his attorney at the time of his direct appeal. Thus, they were not properly raised under § 1089(D)(4).


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief, his request for an evidentiary hearing, and his request for discovery.

Hung Thanh Le v. State


Case No. PC-97-722


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1998 OK CR 1; 953 P.2d 52; 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2; 69 O.B.A.J. 147



January 6, 1998, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Application for an Evidentiary Hearing are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) of first degree malice aforethought murder, robbery with a dangerous weapon, assault and battery with intent to kill, larceny of a motor vehicle, and grand larceny. His death sentence on the murder conviction and sentence to prison terms on the non-capital crimes were affirmed on appeal. Defendant now applied for post-conviction relief and for an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree malice aforethought murder, robbery with a dangerous weapon, assault and battery with intent to kill, larceny of a motor vehicle, and grand larceny. Defendant was sentenced to death on the murder conviction and to prison terms for the non-capital crimes. The court affirmed defendant's convictions and sentences on appeal, and he sought post-conviction review. In his application for post-conviction review, defendant claimed ineffective assistance of counsel. He also claimed that the revised three-pronged standard for determining ineffective assistance of counsel was unconstitutionally vague. The court rejected defendant's claims, holding that the legislature did not usurp the court's authority to address post-conviction claims. The court considered defendant's claims that counsel was ineffective because he did not request an evaluation of defendant by a mental health professional experienced in dealing with Asian refugees and because counsel failed to object to sentencing instructions. The court rejected these claims because defendant could not show that this was deficient performance or how this performance might have prejudiced him.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief and for an evidentiary hearing.

Slaughter v. State


Case No. F-94-1312


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 78; 950 P.2d 839; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 80; 69 O.B.A.J. 87



December 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 3, 1998.
Writ of certiorari denied Slaughter v. Oklahoma, 525 U.S. 886, 142 L. Ed. 2d 163, 119 S. Ct. 199, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5838 (1998)
Post-conviction relief denied at Slaughter v. State, 1998 OK CR 63, 969 P.2d 990, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 60 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Slaughter v. Mullin, 68 Fed. Appx. 141, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 11381 (2003)
Post-conviction relief denied at Slaughter v. State, 2005 OK CR 2, 105 P.3d 832, 2005 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1 (Okla. Crim. App., 2005)
Post-conviction relief denied at Slaughter v. State, 2005 OK CR 6, 2005 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5 (Okla. Crim. App., 2005)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS C. SMITH, Jr., DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of two counts of first degree murder pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A), and sentenced him to death. Defendant claimed numerous errors, including improper trial conduct by the state.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of two counts of first degree murder, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1991), and was sentenced to death on both counts. Defendant then appealed. The court found that (1) it was error to permit the state to present irrelevant evidence concerning the debts of defendant's ex-wife, (2) the prosecution was guilty of misconduct insofar as it had improperly accused the main defense witness of committing perjury and had made other inappropriate comments, (3) the prosecution had also committed misconduct during sentencing when it commented on the look on defendant's face during trial, (4) defendant's remaining contentions of error were either meritless or moot, (5) particularly in light of flaws in defendant's alibi and strong circumstantial evidence, none of the errors were actually reversible because they would not cumulatively have changed the outcome of the trial, and (6) pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 01.13(C) (1991) the jury correctly found sufficient aggravating circumstances to outweigh defendant's mitigating evidence and justify the imposition of the sentence of death.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the lower court's judgment.

Douglas v. State


No. F-95-834


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 79; 951 P.2d 651; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 79; 69 O.B.A.J. 68



December 17, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 16, 1998.
Post-conviction relief denied at, Request denied by Douglas v. State, 1998 OK CR 12, 953 P.2d 349, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6 (Okla. Crim. App., Jan. 23, 1998)
Writ of certiorari denied Douglas v. Oklahoma, 525 U.S. 884, 119 S. Ct. 195, 142 L. Ed. 2d 159, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 5810 (Oct. 5, 1998)
Decision reached on appeal by Powell v. State, 2000 OK CR 5, 995 P.2d 510, 2000 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5 (Okla. Crim. App., Feb. 2, 2000)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Douglas v. Mullin, 2006 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 5686 (W.D. Okla., Jan. 31, 2006)
Related proceeding at Douglas v. Miller, 2012 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 43806 (W.D. Okla., Mar. 29, 2012)
Related proceeding at State ex rel. Okla. Bar Ass'n v. Miller, 2013 OK 49, 309 P.3d 108, 2013 Okla. LEXIS 56 (Okla., June 25, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL C. BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced defendant to death after defendant allegedly killed a person during a drive by shooting. In seeking review, defendant raised jury selection issues, guilt/innocence issues, ineffective assistance of counsel issues, and issues relating to the punishment.


OVERVIEW: Following a fatal drive by shooting, defendant was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. Upon review, the court rejected the claim that potential jurors had been improperly excused because the proper inquiry had been made to determine who could consider the death penalty. The court also held that individual voir dire had not been required because there had been no danger of exposing jurors to damaging information. Moreover, the court held that it had not been erroneous to impeach defendant with prior bad acts because the defense had volunteered defendant's non-violent character. Likewise, the court held it had not been erroneous to impeach defendant with conduct precipitating prior arrests and juvenile convictions. Although it had been erroneous to admit extrinsic evidence in proving witness bias and to consider a hypothetical bystander in determining the "great risk of death to more than one person" aggravator, the court held that the outcome had not been materially affected by the errors. Finally, the court held that defendant's unadjudicated bad acts had been admissible to prove the "continuing threat" aggravator and that counsel's representation had not been deficient.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of first degree murder and sentenced defendant to death.

 

728 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Gilbert v. State


No. F-96-31


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 71; 951 P.2d 98; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 73; 68 O.B.A.J. 3891



November 20, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 3, 1998.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CLEVELAND COUNTY. THE HONORABLE TOM A. LUCAS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the District Court of Cleveland County (Oklahoma), which convicted him on a charge of first degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), kidnapping in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 741 (1991), and robbery with firearms in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801 (1991).


OVERVIEW: At defendant's trial, evidence of his crime spree through three other states was admitted into evidence. Defendant contended that the trial court erred by refusing to order a competency evaluation and by denying his for cause challenges, that the Allen charge was per se coercive, that certain evidence was improperly admitted, and that his death sentence was improper. On appeal, the court affirmed, holding that the trial court did not err in not ordering the competency evaluation. The trial court did not err in refusing to grant defendant's for cause challenges because the jurors clearly indicated they could set aside any personal beliefs, would be fair and impartial, and would disregard anything they had previously heard about defendant. Defendant made a knowing and voluntary waiver of his Miranda rights, and his confession was properly admitted because proof of an express waiver was not required. The Allen charge was not per se coercive. The evidence of defendant's crime spree was properly admitted to support the aggravator of continuing threat. The evidence was sufficient to support defendant's conviction. The court denied the remainder of defendant's claimed errors.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the district court.

 

729 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Grady v. State


Case No. F-96-23


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 67; 947 P.2d 1069; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 70; 68 O.B.A.J. 3655



October 28, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication October 28, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF JACKSON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD DARBY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was convicted by a jury in the District Court of Jackson County (Oklahoma) of first-degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(C) (1991). On appeal, he argued that a jury instruction was improper, that the evidence did not sustain his conviction, and that his trial counsel was ineffective.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of killing a nine-month-old infant in his home day care center. A medical examiner testified that the infant's injuries were consistent with shaken baby syndrome and blunt force trauma. The court first held that although the trial court's definition of "willful" was confusing, the jury had been properly instructed on the elements of the crime of child abuse murder, including the requirement of intent to injure. Next, the court held that the circumstantial evidence presented at trial tended to exclude every reasonable hypothesis other than guilt. Finally, the court rejected defendant's claim that his counsel was ineffective for failing to call a physician who told police that she thought the injuries to the child occurred before the infant went to the day care center. The court stated that the physician saw the infant before the extent of her injuries was known and that the decision not to call her as a witness may have been reasonable trial strategy. Moreover, the court stated, in light of the other medical testimony, defendant could not show that he was prejudiced by his counsel's decision not to call the witness.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's decision.

Hooper v. State


Case No. F-95-835


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 64; 947 P.2d 1090; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 67; 68 O.B.A.J. 3623



October 21, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 24, 1997. Certiorari Denied June 22, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4128.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CANADIAN COUNTY. THE HONORABLE EDWARD C. CUNNINGHAM, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of three counts of murder in the first degree, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1991), and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of three counts of murder in the first degree, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1991), and sentenced to death. The court held that other crimes evidence was admissible to prove motive, opportunity, intent, preparation, plan, knowledge, identity, or absence of mistake or accident, pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2404(B) (1991), and that the trial court had not abused its discretion in admitting such evidence. The court held that, in accordance with Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2803(3), a victim's hearsay statements describing threats and beatings were admissible to show her state of mind and indicate fear of defendant. The court held that victim impact evidence was both relevant and admissible. The court held that the jury was not required to unanimously find mitigating circumstances. The court held that, although a jury was allowed to impose a life sentence even though it found more aggravating circumstances than mitigating ones, the trial court was not required to give an instruction to that effect. The court affirmed a judgment and sentence of the trial court.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed a judgment of the trial court, which convicted defendant of three counts of murder in the first degree. The court held that the victim's hearsay statements were admissible to show her state of mind. The court held that, although the jury was allowed to impose a life sentence even though it found more aggravating circumstances than mitigating ones, the trial court was not required to give an instruction to that effect.

 

731 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Willingham v. State


Case No. F-95-995


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 62; 947 P.2d 1074; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 68; 68 O.B.A.J. 3542



October 15, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 26, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE ALLEN McCALL, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment, after a jury trial in the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), convicting him of first-degree malice murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), and sentencing him to death. He claimed error in the trial court's refusal to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of second-degree depraved mind murder, and in insufficient evidence of aggravation to support the sentence.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree malice murder under § 701.7, and was sentenced to death. He appealed, asserting that the trial court erred in refusing to instruct the jury on the lesser-included offense of second-degree depraved mind murder, and that insufficient evidence of an aggravating circumstance supported the sentence. The court disagreed and affirmed. It explained that the evidence showed that defendant had beaten and kicked the victim in a restroom and left her bleeding on the floor, where she aspirated her blood and died. The court revisited the elements of second-degree depraved mind murder in Okla. Unif. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 4-92 (2d ed.) and amended the fifth element to read that "the conduct is not done with the intention of taking the life of any particular individual." It concluded that second-degree "depraved mind" murder was not a lesser-included offense of first-degree malice murder. Although victim impact evidence had been improper, defendant failed to show that the jury would not have found aggravation, but for that evidence. Thus, the court found that the sentence had been factually substantiated and appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

 

732 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Selsor v. Turnbull


No. P 97-911


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 61; 947 P.2d 579; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61



October 14, 1997, Decided  
October 14, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition for writ of prohibition and/or mandamus is DENIED. The stay of proceedings in Case No. CF 75-2181 previously imposed by this Court is DISSOLVED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application to assume original jurisdiction and a petition for writ of prohibition and/or mandamus asking the court to strike a bill of particulars and prohibit the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) from conducting a jury trial that exposed petitioner to the death penalty, or to life without parole. The Attorney General for the State of Oklahoma filed a response on behalf of respondent judge of the lower court.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner's conviction for murder and his modified sentence were ultimately overturned, and his case was remanded to the state district court for a new trial. In re-trial proceedings, petitioner was again charged for the offense of murder in the first degree. The State filed a bill of particulars again seeking the death penalty against petitioner. Petitioner relied on prior case law to argue that the State's filing of the bill of particulars on re-trial, under current death penalty statutes, violated the prohibition against ex post facto laws. He contended that life imprisonment was the only sentence that could be imposed for a 1975 first degree murder charge, and that retrial proceedings had to be limited to such punishment. The court overturned the ex post facto analysis and the holdings relied on by petitioner. The court held that the change in law by judicial decision that the prior case law should be overturned did not violate the Due Process Clause or ex post facto principles. It did not change the crime for which petitioner was charged, increase the punishment prescribed, or increase the quantity or degree of proof necessary to establish his guilt.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's writ of prohibition and/or mandamus. The court dissolved the stay of proceedings.

 

733 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Humphreys v. State


No. F-95-402


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 59; 947 P.2d 565; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64; 68 O.B.A.J. 3534



October 10, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 17, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKMULGEE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE FRANKLIN D. RAHAL, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Okmulgee County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree and, on remand from the court, sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of stabbing to death his common law wife. He was sentenced to death. On appeal, the court affirmed the conviction but remanded for resentencing. The trial court returned again sentenced him to death and defendant appealed. On appeal, the court held that the death-qualifying questions posed to the jurors did not diminish their sense of responsibility in determining the appropriate penalty. The question whether they could recommend the death penalty as opposed to imposing the death penalty was a proper statement of the law. Because the evidence showed that defendant was serving his sentence under house arrest at the time of the murder, the state proved beyond a reasonable doubt that he committed the murder while serving a sentence of imprisonment on conviction of a felony. Evidence of defendant's criminal conduct was sufficient to show that he would likely continue in the future. Defendant failed to prove his ineffective assistance of counsel claims. In performing its mandatory sentence review the court found that there was sufficient evidence to support the aggravating circumstances alleged by the state.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

 

734 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Sallahdin v. State


Case No. PC-96-1570


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 58; 947 P.2d 559; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63; 68 O.B.A.J. 3646



October 8, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Application for an Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(D)(1) (Supp. 1995), a petitioner under sentence of death filed an application for post-conviction relief together with requests for discovery and an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: A petitioner claimed that multiple constitutional errors occurred at his trial, that his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective, and that the Oklahoma capital post-conviction regime was unconstitutional. Contending that unresolved factual issues existed, he sought discovery and an evidentiary hearing. The court refused to consider those claims that were raised on direct appeal and were barred by res judicata, or that could have been raised then and had been waived. The court reaffirmed its holding that the Post-Conviction Procedure Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089, was constitutional, and found that the facts related to the ineffective assistance of trial counsel claims were available to be raised on direct review. Conclusory allegations that appellate counsel failed to raise meritorious claims were insufficient to prove that counsel was deficient. The court held that the petitioner was not entitled to relief on the basis of cumulative error where his claims were without merit or were procedurally barred. The request for discovery and a hearing was denied when the court determined that there were no unresolved factual issues material to the legality of the conviction.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief together with the application for discovery and an evidentiary hearing.

 

735 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hung Thanh Le v. State


Case No. F-95-1303


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 55; 947 P.2d 535; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 59; 68 O.B.A.J. 3218



October 2, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied November 17, 1997. As Corrected December 9, 1997.
Certiorari Denied June 15, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 3965.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE NANCY L. COATS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part and DISMISSED in part.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of various crimes including malice murder in the first degree and, upon the jury's recommendation, sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: After stealing the stereo equipment of the victim, who was defendant's friend, defendant attacked the victim and eventually killed him. The jury returned a verdict of conviction and recommended the death sentence. In affirming, the court held (1) that since defendant, who was an immigrant, objectively appeared to understand questions asked of him during his interrogation and freely gave a valid waiver, the police were not required to ask defendant about cultural differences; (2) that the trial court did not err in failing to conduct a post-examination competency hearing because Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1175.4(A) (1991) did not require a mandatory hearing and defendant never requested such a hearing; (3) that defendant's sentence was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor and evidence supported the jury's finding of aggravating circumstances; (4) that victim impact testimony describing the emotional, psychological, and financial effects of the crime was not unduly prejudicial; and (5) that while the prosecutors' comments revealed some error, the improper argument did not contribute to the verdict.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment with respect to defendant's convictions for all but two of the crimes. The court dismissed defendant's convictions on those two counts not affecting defendant's murder conviction or death sentence.

Fields v. State


No. PC-97-536


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 53; 946 P.2d 266; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 57; 68 O.B.A.J. 3131



September 26, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Application for an Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition seeking post-conviction relief after he entered a blind plea to first degree felony murder in the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), and the trial court sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a blind plea to first degree felony murder. The trial court sentenced defendant to death. His motion to withdraw plea was denied by the trial court. Defendant filed a petition for writ of certiorari, which was denied. Defendant then filed an application for post-conviction relief asserting ineffective assistance of counsel. The court held that after evaluating appellate counsel's performance, in light of the strong presumption that counsel's conduct fell within the wide range of reasonable professional assistance and recognizing that there were countless ways to provide effective assistance, defendant failed to support his claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court held that because defendant failed to show that appellate counsel's conduct on direct appeal was ineffective, his substantive claim remained barred and was not entitled to consideration on the merits.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief and application for an evidentiary hearing and discovery.

 

737 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


O.W.M. v. State


No. J-96-1494


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 49; 946 P.2d 257; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 53; 68 O.B.A.J. 3122



September 18, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 10, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CARLOS CHAPPELLE, SPECIAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant juvenile appealed the decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) that determined him to be a delinquent child as to the charge of first degree manslaughter, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 711 (1991), that was lodged against him for the killing of his 21 year old cousin while the cousin was attacking the 14 year old juvenile's 15 year old brother.


OVERVIEW: While the juvenile, his brother, and the 300 lb. victim were living with their grandmother, the victim began arguing with the brother, resulting in a physical fight. The 120-lb. brother escaped, ran into his bedroom to retrieve and hide a gun, and was assaulted and choked by the victim. The juvenile, who also weighed about 120 lbs., attempted to push the victim off his brother and when pushed aside shot the victim three times in the back. Finding that the brother did not fit within the statutory list of persons in whose defense a homicide was justified under Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 733 (1991), the trial court convicted him. In reversing the conviction, the court held that it was error for the trial court to have failed to consider the provisions of Okla. Stat. tit. 22, §§ 31 and 33 (1991), irrespective of the juvenile's failure to raise any arguments thereunder. While § 733 only allowed one to employ deadly force in defense of one's spouse, parent, child, employer, or employee, the court concluded that the trial court was obligated to independently consider the provisions of §§ 31 and 33, particularly in light of its finding that the juvenile acted in defense of his brother.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the judgment of the district court and remanded the cause to the district court for a new trial.

 

738 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


McCracken v. State


No. PC-96-934


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 50; 946 P.2d 672; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 54; 68 O.B.A.J. 3128



September 18, 1997, Filed



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Application for Post-Conviction Relief, Motions for Discovery, and Request for Evidentiary Hearing are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of four counts of first degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981) and possession of a firearm after former conviction of a felony. He was sentenced to death for each murder conviction and ten years for the firearm conviction. The court affirmed his judgments and sentences. He then filed an application for post-conviction relief, motions for discovery, and a request for evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Among other claims, petitioner raised the issue of the effectiveness of his trial and appellate counsel. The same attorney represented petitioner both at trial and on appeal and an ineffective assistance of trial counsel claim was therefore not raised on direct appeal. The court denied petitioner's requests for relief. The court found that certain claims were barred by res judicata and others were waived by not having been raised in petitioner's direct appeal. Specifically, the court noted that while petitioner established that the conduct supporting his allegations of ineffectiveness actually occurred, he failed to present facts showing that appellate counsel was unreasonable under the circumstances, that his conduct did not fail within the wide range of professional assistance, or that counsel breached any duty owed to him. The court decided that petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of trial counsel was waived because it could have been raised on direct appeal, but was not. Noting that the court had never allowed unfettered discovery in post-conviction proceedings, it denied petitioner's request for discovery.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief, motions for discovery, and request for evidentiary hearing.

 

739 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Toles v. State


No. F-94-1145


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 45; 947 P.2d 180; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 50; 68 O.B.A.J. 2779



August 22, 1997, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied December 1, 1997. Certiorari Denied June 26, 1998, Reported at: 1998 U.S. LEXIS 4370.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE MARK R. SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court Of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree, conspiracy to commit robbery after former conviction of a felony, and possession of a weapon after former conviction of a felony. The judgment further sentenced defendant to death and to terms of imprisonment.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged the legal sufficiency of the information, jury selection, admission of his confession, denial of funds to secure an expert witness, victim impact evidence, sufficiency of evidence supporting and the constitutionality of aggravating factors, prosecutorial misconduct, and the jury charge. The court affirmed. No confusion as to the crime charged existed in the information. One juror was properly discharged based on his strong aversion to the death penalty. The fact that defendant had to use a peremptory challenge to remove an unsatisfactory juror did not taint the verdict. As to the confession, defendant validly waived his right to counsel and it was not coerced. The decision that an expert witness would not be helpful was based on a valid trial strategy. The victim impact evidence was properly presented to the jury and was subject to all appropriate rules of evidence and criminal trial procedure. Although a necessary instruction for victim impact evidence was omitted, there was no reversible error because the evidence was otherwise sufficient to support each of the findings of aggravating circumstances. Defendant's remaining contentions lacked merit.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

 

740 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Scott v. State


No. PC-96-1270


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 40; 942 P.2d 755; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 44; 68 O.B.A.J. 2567



July 11, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Scott's Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Application for Evidentiary Hearing and Discovery DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner inmate brought an application for post-conviction relief together with requests for discovery and an evidentiary hearing. The inmate was previously convicted of Murder in the first degree and sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: After the inmate was denied relief on direct appeal, he sought post-conviction relief. The court later rejected the inmate's applications for both post-conviction relief and a hearing. The court held that under the revised post-conviction procedure act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (C)(1), (2) (Supp. 1995), the inmate had to show that his claims of newly discovered evidence were not and could not have been raised on direct appeal and that it supported a conclusion either that the outcome of the trial would have been different but for the errors or that he was factually innocent. The court was unable to conclude that the inmate's claim would have changed the outcome of the trial or that it supported the conclusion that he was factually innocent. The court rejected the inmate's argument that he was denied his right to the effective assistance of trial counsel because his trial attorney was deficient. The court ruled that because the inmate's ineffective assistance of trial counsel claim did not turn on facts unavailable at the time of his direct appeal, he had failed to meet the pre-conditions for review of his claim on the merits and therefore review of the claim was barred.


OUTCOME: The court denied the inmate's applications for post-conviction relief and for discovery and an evidentiary hearing.

 

741 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Ellis v. State


No. PC-95-786


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 36; 941 P.2d 527; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 41; 68 O.B.A.J. 2346



June 25, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE KARL GRAY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and Sentence of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed an order of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his petition for post-conviction relief from his convictions and sentences for the murders of three persons and the four counts of shooting with intent to kill.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of and sentenced for three murders and four counts of shooting with intent to kill. The conviction and sentence were affirmed on appeal. Defendant's petition for rehearing was denied. Defendant applied for post-conviction relief, claiming that the trial court's insanity instruction was fundamentally defective and that he was denied effective assistance of trial and appellate counsel. Defendant appealed the denial of his application. The court held that the trial court acted properly in declining to address the insanity instruction issue on rehearing because no objection was made to the instruction at the trial, nor was the issue raised on direct appeal. Thus, it could not have been raised for the first time in a petition for rehearing. Defendant's counsel's assistance was reasonable considering all the circumstances and defendant received a fair trial. Trial counsel properly acquiesced in the administering of the then appropriate uniform insanity instruction. Even though appellate counsel failed to raise the instruction issue on direct appeal, defendant did not establish that such omission, without more, constituted deficient performance.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order.

 

742 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Fields v. Driesel


No. P 96-817


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 33; 941 P.2d 1000; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 35; 68 O.B.A.J. 2009



June 3, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Stay of proceedings LIFTED. Writ of Prohibition GRANTED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner director of the state department of corrections appealed the order of respondent district judge, who ordered petitioner to show cause was he should not be held in contempt of court for failing to comply with a convicted criminal's judgment of sentence. Petitioner applied for a writ of prohibition.


OVERVIEW: Following the criminal conviction of the inmate, the department of corrections received him, as mandated by Okla. Stat. art. 57, § 95 (1991). Over a month later, the inmate was assigned to the electronic monitoring program (EMP) and released from prison. The district judge ordered petitioner to take the inmate into immediate custody or to personally appear and show cause why petitioner should not be held in contempt of court for refusing to comply with the district court's judgment of sentence. The court held that the department of correction had the power to operate the prisons and to administer alternative incarceration programs such as the EMP. The district court had only limited jurisdiction over petitioner to the extent that petitioner was required to receive inmates into custody. The district court did not have jurisdiction to hold petitioner in indirect contempt in a criminal proceeding. The court held that petitioner's power to assign inmates to the EMP did not violate the separation of powers doctrine. The instant situation was not one in which an inmate was discharged from a lawful sentence or pardoned or paroled.


OUTCOME: The court lifted the stay of proceedings over petitioner and granted petitioner's application for a writ of prohibition.

 

743 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Walker v. State


No. PC-89-305


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 31; 940 P.2d 509; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 32; 68 O.B.A.J. 2000



May 23, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition for post-conviction relief is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner criminal defendant filed in the court a second petition for post conviction relief from his conviction in the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) for first degree murder and his sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner had previously appealed from his conviction and the denial of post-conviction relief. He then applied for post-conviction relief a second time, claiming that a recent U.S. Supreme Court decision had held that the burden of proof as to his incompetency was unconstitutional. Petitioner claimed that, at the time of his post-examination competency hearing, Oklahoma law required him to prove his incompetence by clear and convincing evidence. The court disagreed, holding that the issue of his burden of proof as to incompetence was available for review on his appeal and, therefore, was waived for purposes of post-conviction relief. The U.S. Supreme Court had found that years of case law supported the conclusion that the clear and convincing standard of proof was unconstitutional; therefore, the issue was available to petitioner on his appeal. The court noted that, because the instant application was not petitioner's original application for post-conviction relief, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(D)(8) imposed an additional procedural bar to relief.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's second petition for post-conviction relief.

 

744 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Smallwood v. State


Case No. PC-96-1513


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 25; 937 P.2d 111; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24



April 15, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Under Okla. Stat. tit 22, § 1089(D)(1) (Supp. 1995) of the Uniform Post-Conviction Procedure Act, petitioner filed his original application for post-conviction relief. He had been convicted in a district court of first-degree malice murder with a death sentence and third-degree arson with a 15 year sentence and a fine. The Court of Criminal Appeals of Oklahoma affirmed, and the U.S. Supreme Court denied his petition for a writ of certiorari.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner claimed that the jury used extraneous and inaccurate information in determining the death sentence. In denying the petition under the Act, Okla. Stat. tit. § 1080 et seq. (Supp. 1995), the court found that, despite a claim that information was "newly discovered," the information could have been discovered on direct appeal. Petitioner claimed ineffective assistance in that trial counsel failed to object to the refusal to answer a jury question, but the court found that the facts underlying this claim were available on direct appeal. Finally, petitioner argued that it was error for appellate counsel not to raise the issue on direct appeal. However, the court found that appellate counsel did raise the issue that trial counsel failed to object. Therefore, petitioner did not meet the burden of proving that the alleged omission took place. On some of petitioner's other claims, the court held that (1) information was available earlier that there was an unqualified juror who was not a county resident; (2) there were no material issues of fact that would warrant an evidentiary hearing; (3) petitioner was not entitled to an extension of time.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief, request for extension of time, application for discovery, and request for an evidentiary hearing.

Robinson v. State


Case No. PC-96-1224


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 24; 937 P.2d 101; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 23



April 14, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petitioner's Application for Post-Conviction Relief, Request for Extension of Time, Application for Discovery and Request for an Evidentiary Hearing DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner sought post conviction review, pursuant to the Uniform Post-Conviction Procedure Act, of an order of the Oklahoma County trial court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree malice murder and sentenced him to death. His conviction was affirmed on direct appeal. He contended, in part, that appellate counsel was ineffective when she did not present a claim related to the introduction of evidence about his gang involvement.


OVERVIEW: Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(C)(1) and (2) (Supp. 1995), the court considered only those capital post-conviction claims that were not and could not have been raised on direct appeal and that supported a finding that either the trial's outcome would have been different but for the errors or that petitioner was factually innocent. The court rejected claims that the Act was unconstitutional, the jurors were not qualified, and he was factually innocent based on newly discovered evidence. The court rejected claims that he did not receive effective assistance at trial because each of his claims could have been raised on direct appeal. The court rejected his claims of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. Although he proved that the alleged conduct occurred, he failed to make any showing that the conduct, the failure to raise meritorious issues of ineffective assistance of trial counsel or to raise a claim regarding admissibility of gang affiliation evidence, was either unreasonable under the circumstances or did not fall within the wide range of professional assistance. The court denied his requests for an extension of time, discovery, and an evidentiary hearing.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief from his conviction for murder and sentence of death.

 

746 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Carter v. State


No. PC-96-48


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 22; 936 P.2d 342; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 21; 68 O.B.A.J. 1191



March 26, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed petitioner's conviction and sentence on appeal. Petitioner filed an application for post-conviction relief under the Uniform Post-Conviction Procedure Act. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) issued an order denying the petition. Petitioner appealed the district court's order.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner raised numerous challenges to his conviction in his application for post-conviction relief. On appeal, the court affirmed the district court's order denying petitioner's application. The court declined to consider petitioner's arguments that were raised in his direct appeal on the grounds that such arguments were res judicata. The court held that petitioner had waived several arguments that could have raised in his direct appeal but were not, and that such arguments were therefore procedurally barred under the Uniform Post-Conviction Procedure Act. The court rejected petitioner's ineffective assistance of appellate counsel claims. The court held that there was no inherent conflict of interest where appellate attorneys in the Oklahoma Public Defender's office alleged ineffective assistance of trial counsel who also worked in the public defender's office. The court held that appellate counsel's failure to raise every conceivable error on direct appeal did not constitute ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court held that the trial judge was not biased, and that the trial court's order met the requirements of Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1084 (1991).


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying petitioner's application for post-conviction relief.

 

747 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Wallace v. State


Case No. PC-95-1246


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 18; 935 P.2d 366; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18; 68 O.B.A.J. 1175



March 18, 1997, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN ORIGINAL PROCEEDING ON AN APPLICATION FOR POST-CONVICTION RELIEF.



DISPOSITION: DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: This matter was before the court on petitioner's application for post conviction relief and request for discovery and an evidentiary hearing.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner pleaded guilty to murder and waived his right to direct appeal. On a mandatory sentence review, the court affirmed the judgments and sentences, and certiorari was denied. Petitioner then instituted a proceeding for post-conviction relief and the court denied the relief requested. It found that the only issues that could be raised in an application for post-conviction relief were those that: 1) were not and could have been raised in a direct appeal and 2) those that support a conclusion that the outcome of the trial would have been different but for the errors or that the defendant is factually innocent. Both requirements had to be met before the court could review a claim. The court then held that petitioner waived many of the issues raised in his application by declining to pursue a direct appeal. As to petitioner's claim that the crimes actually occurred in Arkansas and, therefore, the trial court lacked jurisdiction, the court found that issue could be raised in a post-conviction proceeding, but that his proposition was without merit because there was competent evidence from which the jury could conclude that the offense charged was consummated in Oklahoma.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's request for post-conviction relief.

 

748 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Valdez v. State


PC-96-788


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 12; 933 P.2d 931; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11; 68 O.B.A.J. 831



February 28, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Valdez's Original Application for Post-Conviction Relief is DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an original application for post-conviction relief with the court following his murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner filed an original application for post-conviction relief with the court following his murder conviction and death sentence in accordance with the recent amendments to the Uniform Post-Conviction Procedure Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(D)(1) (Supp. 1995). The court denied the application. The court noted that it had recently considered and rejected petitioner's constitutional attack upon Oklahoma's current capital post-conviction procedure. The court also considered and rejected petitioner's claim of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel. The court found that while petitioner's counsel's failure to make a claim under caselaw could have supported his ineffective assistance claim, petitioner presented no facts specifically supporting his allegation that his direct appeal attorney was ineffective for omitting the issue, but instead reasons that an attorney who fails to raise a potentially meritorious appellate argument was always ineffective. The court held that a conclusory allegation, standing alone, could never support a finding that an attorney's performance was deficient.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief.

 

749 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hamilton v. State


No. F-93-1366


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 14; 937 P.2d 1001; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13; 68 O.B.A.J. 801



February 28, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 10, 1997.
Writ of certiorari denied Hamilton v. Oklahoma, 522 U.S. 1059, 118 S. Ct. 716, 139 L. Ed. 2d 657, 1998 U.S. LEXIS 229 (1998)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Hamilton v. Mullin, 2006 U.S. App. LEXIS 1675 (10th Cir. Okla., Jan. 24, 2006)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAY D. DALTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgments and Sentences are AFFIRMED, EXCEPT that the judgment and sentence for Robbery with a Firearm is REVERSED and REMANDED to the District Court with instructions to DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of robbery with a firearm and four counts of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to 500 years imprisonment and death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the State's failure to give notice of a critical witness, in violation of Okla. Const. art. II, § 20, denied him the opportunity to investigate the witness and to revise his trial strategy. The court found that defendant had adequate time to prepare for the witness' testimony and that the trial court did not abuse its discretion in denying defendant's motion for a continuance. The court determined that the trial court did not err in submitting a flight instruction to the jury. The court determined that since the jury's conviction of defendant was possibly based on the theory of felony murder, he could not have also been convicted of the underlying felony of robbery with a firearm. The court further found that the prosecutor did not engage in prosecutorial misconduct. After carefully considering and reviewing the evidence that supported the aggravating circumstances, as well as mitigating evidence, the court found that the sentence of death was factually substantiated and appropriate. The court also found that the sentence of death was not imposed under the influence of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions for four counts of murder in the first degree. The court also affirmed his sentence of death, but reversed and dismissed his conviction and sentence for robbery with a firearm.

Lafevers v. State


No. PC-96-768


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 8; 934 P.2d 356; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6



February 25, 1997, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Application for Post-Conviction Relief and Application for an Evidentiary Hearing DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was convicted in the District Court of Oklahoma City (Oklahoma) of first-degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Ok. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.1 (1991) and third-degree arson in violation of Ok. Stat. tit. 21, § 1403(A) (1981), filed an application with the court for post-conviction relief. Because the jury found that the murder was especially heinous and cruel, defendant was sentenced to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had previously appealed his conviction and sentence to the court, which affirmed both. The court then denied defendant's petition for a rehearing, and the United States Supreme Court denied his petition for certiorari. Defendant then filed his application for post-conviction relief with the court. Under the post-conviction statutes, the only issues that could be raised in post-conviction were those that were not or could not have been raised in a direct appeal; and that support a conclusion that the outcome of the trial would have been different but for the error. The court found that defendant raised the issue of ineffective assistance of counsel, and the court found that the claim was proper only if it required fact-finding outside the direct appeal record. The court denied defendant's claim of ineffective assistance of his trial counsel because some of the material was available to the court, and that some of it was discussed in the opinion on direct appeal. The court found that defendant failed to establish that the remainder of his claim required fact-finding outside the direct appeal record. There was no evidence that defendant's appellate counsel was deficient.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief.

McGregor v. State


No. PC-96-1006


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 10; 935 P.2d 332; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 9



February 25, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 23, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 3941.



DISPOSITION: Post-Conviction Relief and Motion for Discovery are DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought post-conviction relief from both the judgment from the trial court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first degree murder and sentenced him to death and from the court, which affirmed the conviction. Defendant claimed ineffective assistance of both trial and appellate counsel in connection with an alleged error committed by the trial court in admitting evidence for which the proper chain of custody had not been established.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's first conviction was overturned because his constitutional rights were violated when he was denied state funds for a psychiatrist to assist in his defense. He relied on an insanity defense and was convicted again in a 1988 retrial. The court affirmed the conviction and the U.S. Supreme Court denied his petition for certiorari. In 1996, he filed an application for post-conviction relief, claiming he was denied effective assistance of counsel at his 1988 trial and subsequent appeal. As required by Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(D)(4)(b)(1), defendant submitted affidavits to support his arguments that his claim could be reviewed because it required fact-finding outside the direct appeal record. The court held that his claim that the trial court erred in admitting evidence taken from his truck without the establishment of the proper chain of custody required no fact-finding outside the direct appeal record. The court stated that the category of items requiring fact finding outside the direct appeal record did not include items that trial counsel could discover. In the context of ineffective assistance of appellate counsel the court found no error.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's motion for post-conviction relief from his first-degree murder conviction.

Conover v. State


No. F-95-780


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 6; 933 P.2d 904; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 8



February 21, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Order Denying Rehearing and Directing Issuance of Mandate of April 3, 1997, Reported at: 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 22.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OTTAWA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE SAM C. FULLERTON, DISTRICT, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of guilt of First Degree Murder is AFFIRMED, the sentence of death is VACATED and the case is REMANDED for RESENTENCING.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence to death in the District Court of Ottawa County (Oklahoma) on a charge of first-degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21 § 701.7 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant punched and held a victim down, while a co-defendant stabbed the victim. After defendant and the co-defendant fled in car, the victim identified the co-defendant and bled to death. After a separate jury trial, defendant was convicted on a first-degree murder charge and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction, vacated the death sentence, and remanded the action to the trial court for resentencing. The court held that (1) the information alleged all of the elements of murder, including malice aforethought, which was equivalent to "premeditated design"; (2) viewing the evidence in the light most favorable to the State, a rational trier of fact could have found defendant guilty on the first-degree murder charge because defendant intended that a killing take place, or he aided and abetted the co-defendant, knowing of the co-defendant's intent to kill the victim; (3) the trial court did not abuse its discretion in admitting gruesome photos into evidence; and (4) the trial court erred by admitting victim impact evidence that was so unduly prejudicial that it rendered the trial fundamentally unfair and by excluding evidence of the victim's illegal drug activity.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction on a charge of first-degree murder. The court vacated defendant's sentence to death and remanded the action to the trial court for resentencing.

Ledbetter v. State


Case No. F-94-640


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 5; 933 P.2d 880; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 4



February 21, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied March 25, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAY DALTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED in part and REVERSED IN PART.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma) convicting him of murder in the first-degree and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant accepted a ride from an individual, who was in town for a Christian convention. The individual drove appellant to the home of his wife, whom he stabbed with a butcher knife and drove an ice pick through her eye. As a result of his actions, appellant was convicted of murder in the first-degree and sentenced to death. At the sentencing, a victim impact statement was read by a police officer on behalf of the victim's minor children. The jury found that appellant was convicted of a crime that was especially heinous, but did not find that appellant was likely a repeat offender. Appellant challenged the conviction and the sentence. The court affirmed the findings of guilt on the ground that each of the errors raised by appellant was without merit. However, the court found that the sentence was improper because the victim impact statement contained improper opinion testimony, was improperly prepared in that it relied on outside sources beyond the parties affected, and the prosecutor failed to give appellant proper notice of what was contained in the victim impact statement. Therefore, the matter was remanded for resentencing.


OUTCOME: Appellant's guilt of the crime of first-degree murder was affirmed, but the sentence of death was reversed and remanded for further consideration.
