Walker v. State


Case No. PC-96-1003


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1997 OK CR 3; 933 P.2d 327; 1997 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2; 68 O.B.A.J. 316



January 23, 1997, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Certiorari Denied June 27, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4161 



DISPOSITION: DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the Tulsa County District Court (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first degree malice aforethought murder, assault and battery with a dangerous weapon, and assault with a dangerous weapon. Defendant was sentenced to death on the first degree murder charge. Defendant filed a motion for post-conviction relief and an application for an evidentiary hearing and discovery.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's primary contention on appeal was that he was denied ineffective counsel at the trial and appellate levels of his case. Defendant also attacked the constitutionality of Oklahoma's amended capital post-conviction review statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(C)(1) (1995), on the grounds that both on its face and as applied, he was denied due process, equal and adequate access to the courts, and that the ex post-facto clause was violated. Section 1089(C)(1) provided limited grounds for defendants to attack their "final" judgments. The court disagreed and denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief and application for an evidentiary hearing and post-conviction discovery. The court held that defendant failed to satisfy all the criteria necessary to establish either of his ineffective assistance of counsel claims as appropriate for post-conviction relief. The court found that defendant raised no controverted, previously unresolved factual issues material to the legality of his confinement, and that defendant could have previously raised his collaterally asserted grounds for review.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief and application for an evidentiary hearing and discovery.

 

755 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Bannister v. State


Case No. F-95-973


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 60; 930 P.2d 1176; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61; 68 O.B.A.J. 32



December 26, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] The Judgment and Sentence of the trial court is REVERSED and this cause is REMANDED for a NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Payne County District Court (Oklahoma), which convicted him of first-degree child abuse murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(C) (1991), contending that the jury instruction establishing the elements of the offense were contradictory and confusing.


OVERVIEW: Defendant appealed his conviction for first-degree child abuse murder in violation of § 701.7(C), which prohibited the willful or malicious injuring, torturing, maiming, or using of unreasonable force upon a child. Defendant claimed that the jury instruction establishing the elements of the offense was contradictory and confusing. The court reversed the conviction and remanded the cause for a new trial, finding that the challenged instruction improperly permitted the jury to convict defendant whether he did or did not intend to injure, torture, maim or use unreasonable force on the child victim. The trial court's instruction indicated that "willful," as defined in Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 92 (1991), did not require any intent to violate the law or to injure another or to acquire any advantage. The court held that the definition of "willful," as provided both by § 92 (1991) and Okla. Unif. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 424, was at odds with the plain meaning of that term as used in the statutes defining the crime of first-degree child abuse murder. Accordingly, that definition of "willful" should not have been included in the jury instructions for first-degree child abuse murder.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's conviction for first-degree child abuse murder and remanded the cause for a new trial.

 

756 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Medlock v. State


No. PC-96-1081


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 58; 927 P.2d 1069; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 58; 67 O.B.A.J. 3570



November 15, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] DENIED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner filed an application for post-conviction relief and a request for an evidentiary hearing with the court. Petitioner was convicted, upon his guilty plea, of first degree murder. He was sentenced to death. The district court denied his application to withdraw his plea. The court affirmed the district court's denial of his application and affirmed his death sentence. The U.S. Supreme Court denied petitioner's certiorari petition.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner argued that the rulings of the trial court and the court deprived him of his right to a full and fair hearing on the merits of his claim that trial counsel had a conflict of interest rendering him ineffective during the hearing on his application to withdraw his plea. The court noted that petitioner had raised this issue in his direct appeal. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089(C)(1)(2) (Supp. 1995) of Oklahoma's Post-Conviction Procedure Act, only issues that were not and could not have been raised on direct appeal could be raised in an application for post-conviction relief. Further, res judicata barred the court from considering those issues raised on direct appeal. Petitioner also argued that his execution violated the Eighth Amendment of the U.S. Constitution and Oklahoma law because he suffered from Multiple Personality Disorder. He claimed that appellate counsel was ineffective for failing to raise this issue in his direct appeal. The court disagreed. The Eighth Amendment and Oklahoma law barred the execution of insane persons. Petitioner had failed to make any showing that he was now insane or that he would be insane at the time of his execution.


OUTCOME: The court denied petitioner's application for post-conviction relief and request for an evidentiary hearing.

Lozoya v. State


Case No. C-95-861


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 55; 932 P.2d 22; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 56; 67 O.B.A.J. 3437



November 5, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied January 13, 1997.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE VIRGIL C. BLACK, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Convictions affirmed. Case REMANDED to reconsider the sentencing options.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which entered petitioner's guilty pleas to trafficking in illegal drugs, Okla. Stat. tit. 63 § 2-415 (1991), maintaining a vehicle where a controlled dangerous substance is kept, Okla. Stat. tit. 63 § 2-404 (1991), and possession of a controlled dangerous substance without a tax stamp, Okla. Stat. tit. 68 § 450.3 (1991).


OVERVIEW: After marijuana was found in petitioner defendant's van, he pleaded guilty to trafficking in illegal drugs, maintaining a vehicle where a controlled dangerous substance is kept, and possession of a controlled dangerous substance without a tax stamp. Petitioner applied to withdraw his pleas. The court affirmed the convictions, holding that the trial court did not err by refusing to deny petitioner's motion to withdraw his pleas because he did not show they were not intelligently and voluntarily given and petitioner sought to withdraw his pleas because he did not like his sentence. The civil forfeiture provisions in Okla. Stat. tit. 63 § 2-503, used against petitioner's vehicle and his monies in a prior, separate proceeding, did not constitute "punishment" for purposes of the Double Jeopardy Clause of U.S. Const. amend. V. The court remanded the case to allow the trial court to consider the sentencing options available under the Delayed Sentencing Program for Young Adults, specifically Okla. Stat. tit. 22 § 996.3 (1991), which was not impliedly repealed by the Trafficking in Illegal Drugs Act, specifically Okla. Stat. tit. 63 § 2-414 (1991), and applied to petitioner.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court denying petitioner defendant's motion to withdraw his guilty pleas because he failed to show his pleas were not intelligently and voluntarily given. The court remanded the case to allow the court to consider the sentencing options available under the Delayed Sentencing Program for Young Adults, which applied to petitioner and was not impliedly repealed by the Trafficking in Illegal Drugs Act.

Smith v. State


No. F-94-1199


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 50; 932 P.2d 521; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 51; 67 O.B.A.J. 2958



October 1, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted December 6, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63.
Rehearing granted by State v. Smith, 1996 OK CR 50, 932 P.2d 521, 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 63 (Okla. Crim. App., 1996)
Writ of certiorari denied Smith v. Oklahoma, 521 U.S. 1124, 117 S. Ct. 2522, 138 L. Ed. 2d 1023, 1997 U.S. LEXIS 4148 (1997)
Subsequent appeal at, Decision reached on appeal by Smith v. State, 2013 OK CR 14, 306 P.3d 557, 2013 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 13 (Okla. Crim. App., 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD W. FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which had convicted him of five counts of first degree murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 707.7 (1991), and imposed the death penalty upon a finding that five aggravating circumstances had been alleged and proved to exist.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of murdering his wife and her four children and was sentenced to death. Defendant appealed the conviction and sentencing on numerous grounds, but primarily focused on the imposition of the death penalty and the question regarding the admissibility of his confession and pictures of the crime scene. OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment and sentence convicting defendant of five counts of first degree murder and imposing the death penalty.

Charm v. State


F-94-1069


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA

SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied September 30, 1996. Certiorari Denied April 28, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2732.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF COMANCHE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE ROY D. MOORE, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Comanche County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), first degree rape in violation of § 1114(A)(3), and kidnapping in violation of § 741. Defendant was sentenced, in part, to death for the murder and claimed numerous pretrial, trial, and sentencing errors committed by the trial court.


OVERVIEW: Defendant kidnapped, raped, and murdered a 14 year old girl, was convicted, and sentenced to death for the murder. Defendant appealed and claimed, in part, that the trial court committed numerous errors in the sentencing stage of his trial. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and the sentence. The court held that the State's evidence of continuing threat and avoidance of arrest or prosecution aggravators was sufficient and that the aggravators were not unconstitutionally vague. The heinous, atrocious or cruel aggravator was proven beyond a reasonable doubt based on the evidence of a conscious physical suffering of the victim prior to death that showed that the murder was preceded by torture or serious physical abuse. The court rejected defendant's claim that a prosecutor's statement about defendant not being deterred by the killing from eating fried chicken and playing basketball was a racial slur because the evidence showed that defendant ate chicken and played basketball after the murder.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence.

Hatch v. State


No. PC-96-718


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 37; 924 P.2d 284; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 38; 67 O.B.A.J. 2628



August 6, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected November 26, 1996.



DISPOSITION: The Application for Post-Conviction Relief, Request for Stay of Execution, and Request for Discovery and Evidentiary Hearing DENIED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In an application for post-conviction relief, request for stay of execution, and request for discovery and evidentiary hearing, petitioner challenge a conviction for first-degree murder and a death sentence, which was entered by the District Court of Canadian County (Oklahoma).


OVERVIEW: Petitioner exhausted all state and federal appeals, and an execution date was set. Petitioner raised several grounds for relief, including the absence trial court's subject matter jurisdiction under the Uniform post-conviction Procedure Act. Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1089 (1991), and ineffective assistance of counsel. On appeal, the court refused the relief sought, holding that petitioner failed to raise the issues in accordance with §1089. Further, he failed to show an Equal Protection violation because post conviction petitioners were not a suspect classification. He also fell short in proving that there was no rational basis for the provisions of § 1089, which merely tightened procedures already in place. Regarding the ineffective assistance of counsel issue, the court held that petitioner was receiving exactly that which he was due under state law -- competent counsel and an opportunity to present claims on appeal. Finally, any failure to allege facts constituting an offense did not affect the trial court's jurisdiction.


OUTCOME: The court denied the application for post-conviction relief, request for stay of execution, and request for discovery and evidentiary hearing.

Fields v. State


No. C-94-414


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 35; 923 P.2d 624; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 36; 67 O.B.A.J. 2618



July 31, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied October 8, 1996. Certiorari Denied May 12, 1996, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 2947.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE JAMES L. GULLETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction and death sentence for first degree felony murder following his blind plea from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma). He appealed the trial court's denial of his motion to withdraw his plea.


OVERVIEW: Defendant entered a blind plea to felony murder and he was sentenced to death. On appeal of the trial court's denial of his motion to withdraw his plea, the court affirmed the trial court's decision. The information was sufficient because, while lacking specificity, it gave defendant sufficient notice of the charges against him. An examination of the record did not support defendant's claim that he was not fully apprised of the ramifications of entering a plea to felony murder. He knowingly and voluntarily entered his plea. There was no requirement that the trial court advise defendant that he waived the right to jury sentencing by entering a guilty plea. Defendant raised no legitimate ineffective assistance of counsel claim. The trial court properly weighed the aggravating factors against the mitigating factors in imposing the death sentence and there was nothing in the record to indicate that the sentence imposed was the result of passion, prejudice, or any other arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.

Cooper v. State


Case No. F-92-533


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 32; 924 P.2d 749; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 32; 67 O.B.A.J. 2505



July 25, 1996, Decided  
July 25, 1996, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The case was remanded to the court by the United States Supreme Court, which reversed defendant's conviction and ordered the court to conduct further proceedings consistent with its opinion. The U.S. Supreme Court found that a Due Process violation occurred when defendant was required to prove that he was not competent to stand trial by clear and convincing evidence.


OVERVIEW: The State filed a response to the mandate of the U.S. Supreme Court, and the court gave defendant an opportunity to reply. Due to a clerical error, defendant's request for a continuance was filed on the last day on which he could file a reply. The court had filed an order to remand the case, but it held that order until it read defendant's reply. Upon reviewing defendant's reply, the court vacated its order holding the remand order. The court remanded the matter to the trial court to determine the feasibility of holding a retrospective post-examination competency hearing and to hold the hearing if feasible. The court found that the hearing was not prohibited and noted that the fact that the procedure could be difficult did not render it impossible. The court rejected defendant's argument that the U.S. Supreme Court had made a factual determination that he was incompetent at the time of trial because the U.S. Supreme Court normally did not review findings of fact. The court also noted that an incorrect burden of proof concerning competency to stand trial, in defendant's case, did not directly impact on his Sixth Amendment right to a trial by jury.


OUTCOME: The court remanded the matter to the trial court to determine the feasibility of holding a retrospective post-examination competency hearing. If the hearing was determined to be feasible, the court ordered the trial court to conduct the hearing.

Mayes v. State


Case No. PC-95-1218


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 28; 921 P.2d 367; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 29; 67 O.B.A.J. 2343



July 10, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF JEFFERSON COUNTY. THE HONORABLE GEORGE W. LINDLEY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner challenged an order of the District Court of Jefferson County, which denied his request for post-conviction relief. Petitioner was convicted of murder in the first degree and conspiracy to commit murder. After finding the presence of an aggravating circumstances, the jury recommended punishment of death for murder, and 10 years' and a $ 5,000 fine for conspiracy. The court affirmed the convictions on direct appeal.


OVERVIEW: On appeal from the denial of post-conviction relief, petitioner claimed that his trial and appellate counsel were ineffective. Petitioner claimed trial counsel was ineffective because he did not present evidence of petitioner's mental disorders. The court rejected that argument, finding that a psychologist, who submitted an affidavit on petitioner's behalf, admitted that petitioner appeared outwardly normal; thus, there was nothing to indicate that petitioner exhibited any mental impairment. Therefore, petitioner failed to demonstrate that trial counsel's representation was unreasonable under prevailing professional norms. Further, petitioner failed to show prejudice. He failed to present evidence to the court showing that by the time he reached adulthood, he had not learned that killing was wrong. Petitioner claimed that his appellate counsel was ineffective because she failed to present a cumulative error argument. However, the court held that petitioner did not show that, even if his counsel's performance fell below that which was expected, he was prejudiced by that failure. Under a plain error review, the court found the cumulative error argument lacking.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Miles v. State


No. F-95-475


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 24; 922 P.2d 629; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 35; 67 O.B.A.J. 2590



June 3, 1996, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] Petition for Rehearing Denied.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant filed a petition for rehearing of his appeal of his first-degree murder conviction under Okla. Stat. tit. 21 § 701.7 (1971). Defendant contended that he was denied due process by application of an ex post facto law and that the court's decision conflicted with principles of constitutional law that could not have been called to the court's attention during the pendency of his appeal.


OVERVIEW: Defendant filed his petition under Okla. R. Ct. Crim. App. 3.14, alleging that, because the information did not allege all the elements of the underlying felony, robbery with firearms, his due process rights were violated and that the use of data not included in the information to supply notice was unconstitutional. On appeal, the court held that it was no longer a pleading requirement that each felony murder information must allege facts to support every element of the underlying felony. Because the information stated the charge, date, time, place, weapon, victim's name, and the fact that a death had occurred, defendant was placed on notice of what he would have to defend against. The fact that the defense of an inadequate information based on lack of facts to support the underlying felony charge was no longer available to defendant due to a narrowing judicial interpretation of the law did not amount to passage of an ex post facto law. No additional behavior was criminalized, no greater punishment was inflicted, and no legal rules of evidence were changed. The court rejected defendant's contention that he was denied due process.


OUTCOME: The court denied defendant's petition for a rehearing.

 

766 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Williams v. State


No. F-94-741


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 16; 915 P.2d 371; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 17



April 16, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied May 13, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANIEL OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgments and Sentences for First Degree Murder are REVERSED and the case is REMANDED for NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court for Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him upon the jury verdict on two counts for murder in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (1991), sentenced him to death on one of the counts, and sentenced him to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole on the other count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and killed two individuals. Thereafter, defendant was convicted upon the jury verdict on two counts for murder in the first degree, in violation of § 701.7(A). The jury found defendant was previously convicted of a felony involving the use or threat of violence, knowingly created a great risk of death to more than one person, and probably would commit criminal acts of violence that would constitute a continuing threat to society. In accordance with the jury's recommendation, the trial court sentenced defendant to death on one of the counts and to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole on the other count. The court reversed the judgments and sentences and remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial. The court held that the trial court violated defendant's privilege against self-incrimination under the Fifth Amendment and his right to the assistance of counsel under the Sixth Amendment when it ruled that he had to take the stand before presenting evidence of self-defense. One accused of committing a crime was allowed to raise self-defense sufficiently to justify an instruction through circumstantial evidence alone.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and sentences. The court also remanded the case to the trial court for a new trial.

 

767 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Davis v. State


Case No. F-94-1232


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 15; 916 P.2d 251; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 18



April 12, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE RICHARD W. FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: Judgment and sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant challenged the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) which convicted him of five counts of operating a computer bulletin board where he trafficked obscene pictures.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was found guilty of five counts of operating a computerized bulletin board where he trafficked obscene pictures. The jury fixed punishment at five years of imprisonment and a fine on each of the first three counts. In addition, the jury set punishment at five years imprisonment and a fine for count four and five years of imprisonment and a fine for count five. Appellant argued that CD-ROM discs containing obscene material were not prohibited in Oklahoma and that he was deprived of his constitutional right to due process on all five counts on the grounds the statutes did not provide fair warning of the conduct for which he was prosecuted and convicted. The court stated that appellant distributed obscene pictures by distributing the discs which could then be used to display obscene visual images. The key in the present case was the necessary computer software and hardware to access the obscene pictures made available by the disc. Accordingly, the court held that appellant's sales to a police sergeant of the CD-ROM discs were distributions of obscene pictures in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1021(A)(3). Therefore, the judgment and the sentence was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the trial court which convicted appellant of operation of a computerized bulletin board where he trafficked in obscene pictures. The court reasoned that obscene material stored in electronic media was subject to the obscenity statutes.

Paxton v. State


No. PC-95-473


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 4; 910 P.2d 1059; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 5; 67 O.B.A.J. 221



January 12, 1996, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE MAJOR WILSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.
Paxton v. State, 1993 OK CR 59, 867 P.2d 1309, 1993 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64 (Okla. Crim. App., Dec. 30, 1993)



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner appealed the decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied his application for post-conviction relief after the court affirmed his first degree murder conviction and death sentence.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of first degree murder and sentenced to death. The court affirmed the conviction, and petitioner then filed an application for post-conviction relief in the district court. The district court denied him relief, and he appealed. The court affirmed the denial of post-conviction relief. The court first held that only three of petitioner's claims were properly raised by the Post-Conviction Procedure Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1080 (1991) because only the issues which could not have been raised on direct appeal were reviewable. As to those claims, the court held that (1) petitioner's appellate counsel was not ineffective because his counsel submitted a well-researched brief, and was not required to raise every issue now raised; (2) the claim that counsel could not meet with petitioner under constitutional conditions was unsubstantiated; and (3) the trial court did not err in failing to hold an evidentiary hearing on his request for post-conviction relief because the issues raised die not require the taking of evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's denial of petitioner's request for post-conviction relief.

Knighton v. State


No. F-90-1326


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 2; 912 P.2d 878; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 2; 67 O.B.A.J. 131



January 8, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 28, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF NOBLE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE NEAL BEEKMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Noble County (Oklahoma) convicting him on two counts of murder in the first degree and sentencing him to death.


OVERVIEW: Appellant was the mastermind behind a crime spree that stretched from Kansas to Texas and left several people dead, including the victims in Oklahoma. As a result of his actions, the trial court found appellant guilty on two counts of murder in the first degree, and the sentence was rendered as death. Appellant challenged the conviction and the sentence raising numerous points of error. Appellant's most strenuous objection regarded the composition of the jury in that certain veniremen should have been excluded because of their views on capital punishment. The court noted that in a death penalty case, a venireman was properly excused for cause if he expressed consideration for the death penalty as the only appropriate sentence, and thus was unwilling to consider other alternatives. The court noted that while two members of the jury were strongly in favor of the death penalty, they did not express an unwillingness to consider sentencing alternatives. The members were properly allowed. Appellant's remaining contentions were equally without merit, thus the conviction and the sentence was proper.


OUTCOME: Appellant's conviction and sentence was affirmed.

 

770 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Trim v. State


Case No. F-89-1207


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1996 OK CR 1; 909 P.2d 841; 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 1; 67 O.B.A.J. 142



January 5, 1996, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 6, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE JAMES L. GULLETT, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Count I is AFFIRMED, Count II and Count III are REVERSED with instructions to DISMISS.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which following a jury trial convicted him of three counts of selling obscene magazines.


OVERVIEW: Defendant, an adult bookstore clerk, sold three obscene magazines to undercover officers. The three counts of selling obscene magazines arose from the same transaction. On appeal, the court reversed two of the three counts of defendant's conviction. The court held that the federal constitutional right guaranteeing freedom from double jeopardy barred conviction for multiple counts of one offense arising out of one transaction. The court ruled that nothing in the defining language of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1021(A)(3) (Supp. 1984), which was the statute that defendant was convicted pursuant to, suggested a different result. Accordingly, judgment and sentence for two of the three counts were reversed and remanded with instructions to dismiss. Further, the court ruled that obscene material was outside the protection of the First Amendment, and therefore no fundamental right was involved. The court found that bookstore clerks were not a suspect class and a distinction between them and movie theatre employees did not violate the Equal Protection Clause. The court ruled that the protection against prosecution afforded to the movie theatre clerks did not apply to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed Count I but reversed Counts II and III and remanded with instructions to dismiss.

Cargle v. State


Case No. F-94-763


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 77; 909 P.2d 806; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 88; 66 O.B.A.J. 50



December 22, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied February 8, 1996.
Writ of certiorari denied Cargle v. Oklahoma, 519 U.S. 831, 117 S. Ct. 100, 136 L. Ed. 2d 54, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 4957 (1996)
Writ of habeas corpus granted Cargle v. Mullin, 317 F.3d 1196, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 1298 (10th Cir. Okla., 2003)
Writ of habeas corpus denied Cargle v. Sirmons, 2008 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 24154 (W.D. Okla., Mar. 26, 2008)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE CHARLES L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged an order from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree and for being a felon in possession of a firearm. The jury found aggravating circumstances and recommended a sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant alleged numerous errors, including a claim that the accumulation of errors at his trial dictated reversal. His main contention was that the admission of victim impact evidence prejudiced the jury in its decision to sentence him to death. On appeal, the court held that the Eighth Amendment did not bar the admission of victim impact evidence or prosecutorial argument on that evidence; however, that evidence had to restricted to those unique characteristics that defined the individual who died. The court held that it was permissible to give the jury a "glimpse of the life" that was lost, and the court established a jury instruction for all future capital murder cases in which victim impact evidence was presented. In this case, the court found that the trial court committed error in admitting portions of the victim impact evidence, but the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt given the aggravating circumstances. The lack of a transcript, refusal to order a competency examination, admission of victims' photographs, and prosecution argument did not establish an accumulation of errors requiring reversal.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgments and sentences of the trial court on all convictions.

 

772 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Priddy v. State


No. M-95-0299


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 76; 908 P.2d 808; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 82; 66 O.B.A.J. 70



December 21, 1995, Decided  
December 21, 1995, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was issued a traffic citation for failing to carry a security verification form. The Rogers County District Court (Oklahoma) found him guilty of that violation. Defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Okla. Const. art. 2, § 17 set forth the formal requirements that the state mandated to initiate a criminal proceeding in the courts of the state. The constitution provided that no person could be prosecuted criminally in courts of record for felony or misdemeanor otherwise than by presentment or indictment or by information. On appeal, the defendant argued that the trial court lacked subject matter jurisdiction to convict him because he was given a ticket and the officer did not properly verify that ticket as required by law. At trial, the trooper admitted that he signed the ticket but that he did not actually subscribe or verify the information on the ticket in the presence of an attesting officer. The court affirmed the conviction. The court held that: (1) Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 1114.3 provided that a traffic ticket, i.e., a Uniform Violations Complaint, constituted an Information if properly endorsed and certified; (2)Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 303B (1992) provided that if the officer signed the ticket or citation stating that the statements therein were true, the ticket was properly verified; and (3) it became an Information when the district attorney filed it.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

Romano v. State


No. F-93-75


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 74; 909 P.2d 92; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 81; 66 O.B.A.J. 4015



December 19, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 24, 1996.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DANIEL L. OWENS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The judgment and sentence of the trial court is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his jury conviction for murder in the first degree, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1981), and the death sentence imposed by the District Court for the District of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) on the jury's recommendation and finding of two aggravating circumstances.


OVERVIEW: Defendant and codefendant planned to rob decedent. They conned their way into decedent's apartment, turned up the stereo volume to mask the sounds of their attack and murdered decedent. Defendant's first trial resulted in a conviction and death sentence. The judgment and sentence was reversed for failure to sever defendant's trial from codefendant's. Defendant alleged that the trial court erred in allowing a detective to testify to certain non-verbal reactions during questioning. The court held that the testimony was proper. Defendant's actions in trembling and dropping his head were too vague and ambiguous to be assertions. Thus, these movements were not adoptive admissions. However, the detective could properly testify to his direct observations of defendant's conduct in reaction to the questioning. The court held that defendant's head nod in reaction to an assertion that he was guilty was admissible as an adoptive admission. The court found that defendant heard the accusation and appreciated the context in which it was made. By waiving his right to remain silent and participating in the interview defendant could have either denied the accusation or become silent.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence.

Cheney v. State


No. F-94-220


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 72; 909 P.2d 74; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 80; 66 O.B.A.J. 3916



December 8, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE B.R. BEASLEY.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment of the district court is AFFIRMED and the Sentence of death is MODIFIED TO LIFE IMPRISONMENT WITHOUT THE POSSIBILITY OF PAROLE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of an order of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted him on a charge of first-degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged after he shot and killed his wife after he purchased a gun. Several witnesses testified that they observed defendant and his wife fighting, observed the wife spray defendant with mace, and then heard a gunshot, which was followed by several more. On appeal, the court affirmed defendant's conviction and modified his sentence to life imprisonment without parole, holding that although the evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction, the evidence was legally insufficient to support the imposition of the death penalty. The facts surrounding the victim's death did not support a finding of serious physical abuse or torture sufficient to show that the murder was committed in an especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel manner. The pretrial publicity of the crime and the trial court's refusal to conduct individual voir dire did not deprive defendant of a fair trial. The evidence was sufficient to sustain defendant's conviction. The State could disprove defendant's insanity through the testimony of lay witnesses. Evidence of the protective order was properly admitted to show intent and motive. The court overruled the remainder of defendant's claims.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's murder conviction, but modified defendant's death sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole.

Sawatzky v. City of Okla. City


No. M-94-1309


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 69; 906 P.2d 785; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 76; 66 O.B.A.J. 3722



November 21, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE MUNICIPAL COURT OF OKLAHOMA CITY. THE HONORABLE EMILY KAYE LONIAN, MUNICIPAL JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Sawatzky's Judgment and Sentence for Offering to Engage in an Act of Lewdness is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the Municipal Court of Oklahoma City (Oklahoma), which found him guilty of offering to engage in an act of lewdness in violation of Okla. City Municipal Code ch. 30, § 30-152 (1993).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted for soliciting in a public place an act of sodomy from a police officer of the same gender. On appeal, the court affirmed. The court declines to consider whether Okla. City Municipal Code ch. 30, §§ 30-151, 30-152 (1993) violated defendant's right to privacy because the conduct was an act of public, rather than private, solicitation. Also, Okla. City Municipal Code ch. 30, § 30-151, 30-152 (1993) did not violate defendant's right to equal protection. Although Okla. City Municipal Code ch. 30, § 30-151(1)(b) created an exception for married persons in the definition of lewdness, such exemption recognized that such solicitations might be a consequence of the marital relationship. Thus, the marital exemption was rationally related to the legitimate governmental interest of protecting citizens from sexual solicitations.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's judgment.

Richie v. State


No. F-93-1095


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 67; 908 P.2d 268; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 73



November 7, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Writ of certiorari denied Richie v. Oklahoma, 519 U.S. 837, 136 L. Ed. 2d 64, 117 S. Ct. 111, 1996 U.S. LEXIS 5034 (1996)
Post-conviction relief denied at Richie v. State, 1998 OK CR 26, 957 P.2d 1192, 1998 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 25 (Okla. Crim. App., 1998)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF TULSA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE B.R. BEASLEY, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgments and Sentences of the trial court are AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from a decision of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant for the crimes of kidnapping for extortion, robbery with a firearm, murder in the first degree, unauthorized use of a debit card, and larceny of an automobile. The district court set punishment at 99 years imprisonment for Count I, 60 years for Count II, death for Count III, and 20 years for Count IV, and 30 years for Count V.


OVERVIEW: The trial court convicted defendant on various charges, including kidnapping, robbery, murder in the first degree, unauthorized use of a credit card, and larceny, and sentenced defendant to death. On appeal, the court concluded that the prosecution of defendant in Tulsa County for kidnapping and murder was not barred merely because the murder may have occurred in Pawnee County. The murder offense was preceded by the offense of kidnapping. The murder could neither be considered in isolation, nor as factually distinct from the antecedent kidnapping. Although the court found that the jury's finding of felony murder was invalid, the court affirmed defendant's conviction for first degree murder with malice aforethought. The alternative murder charge of malice aforethought was supported by sufficient evidence and the jury instructions for this count were proper. The information charging defendant with first degree murder with malice aforethought sufficiently charged all essential elements of that crime. Further, the court found that the aggravating circumstances outweighed the mitigating circumstances and that the sentence of death was factually substantiated and appropriate.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

Berget v. State


Case No. PC-94-1125


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 66; 907 P.2d 1078; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 74



November 6, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Certiorari Denied June 10, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 3776.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE RICHARD W. FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed from order of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which denied post-conviction relief from his conviction on guilty a plea to murder, burglaries, and a firearm charge, and his death sentence for the murder. He raised a laundry list of alleged errors, including denial of due process and ineffective assistance of trial and appellate counsel.


OVERVIEW: Defendant pled guilty to first-degree murder, burglary, and a firearm charge. He was sentenced to death for the murder. His motion to withdraw his plea was denied. His convictions were affirmed after his request for certiorari to vacate the death sentence was denied. On his direct appeal, the court found that there was more than enough evidence of his intent to avoid arrest by the murder. In this first application for post-conviction relief, he raised 14 errors, primarily related to ineffective assistance. The court's consideration was strictly limited by the statutory rules establishing its post-conviction authority. Most of the alleged errors were barred by res judicata, waived, or not preserved. The court refused to follow the federal Galloway procedure on ineffective assistance, noting significant differences between Oklahoma's Post-Conviction Procedure Act and 28 U.S.C.S. § 2255. To refuse to hear such a claim except in a post-conviction proceeding when defendant was not entitled to appointed counsel potentially denied the right to have the claim heard. Such a claim should have been brought on direct appeal or it was waived. The judgment was affirmed.


OUTCOME: The denial of post-conviction relief was affirmed. The court was unable to conclude that the denial was in error. Defendant's unsubstantiated assertions were insufficient to persuade the court that a collateral issue should be decided on post-conviction. He presented no evidence of ineffective assistance or conflict between trial and appellate counsel. There was sufficient evidence of his participation in the murder.

Johnson v. State


No. F-91-884


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 62; 911 P.2d 918; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 67; 66 O.B.A.J. 3506



October 23, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Granted February 20, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 11.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PITTSBURG COUNTY. THE HONORABLE STEVEN W. TAYLOR, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and Sentence is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged his conviction for first-degree malice aforethought murder and his sentence to death entered by the District Court of Pittsburg County (Oklahoma) upon a jury's verdict.


OVERVIEW: Defendant shot and stabbed his friend's wife to death upon the friend's promise to pay defendant for the act. Defendant told his wife that he had killed the friend's wife. A conversation between defendant and a third party in which defendant admitted to the murder was intercepted by the police because the third party was wearing an eavesdropping device. On appeal, the court determined (1) that the tape recording of defendant's conversation with the third party was not inadmissible because the third party implicitly consented to the recording of the conversation; (2) that the admission of defendant's wife's testimony was not covered by privilege because defendant discussed the same subject matter with others abrogating the confidential nature of defendant's discussions with his wife; (3) that defendant's confession was corroborated by substantial independent evidence so that it was considered trustworthy; and (4) that defendant's state of drunkenness did not render his waiver of his Miranda rights involuntary. The court found also that the trial court properly instructed the jury on the mitigating circumstances and the aggravating factors the jurors were to consider in sentencing.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for first-degree malice aforethought murder and defendant's sentence of death.

Duckett v. State


No. F-89-644


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 61; 919 P.2d 7; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 68; 66 O.B.A.J. 3318



October 17, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied July 25, 1996, Reported at: 1996 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 34. Certiorari Denied February 18, 1997, Reported at: 1997 U.S. LEXIS 1019.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES B. BLEVINS, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree, concealing stolen property, and larceny of an automobile, and, upon the jury's recommendation, sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: The evidence presented indicated that defendant beat the victim to death with a fireplace poker and wooden ashtray stand. The jury found him guilty of first degree, murder, concealing stolen property, and larceny, and found evidence of five aggravating circumstances, including defendant's history of violent felony convictions, the heinousness of the crime, and that defendant constituted a continuing threat to society. The jury set defendant's punishment at death, and he appealed, noting 32 propositions of error, relating primarily to the punishment imposed. The court affirmed the conviction, holding that although the prosecutor made inappropriate comments to the effect that the victim had a right to live and that sending defendant to prison would not be justice, such comments did not have the cumulative effect of denying defendant a fair trial. In addition, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 13(2) (1981) and Okla. Const. art. II, § 20 did not give defendant a statutory or constitutional right to address his sentencing jury where he had elected counsel to make closing argument. Finally, the jury instructions regarding aggravating factors did not direct the jury to disregard mitigating evidence.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed.

CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction by the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma) for oral sodomy and anal sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1991). He also challenged his sentence to five years imprisonment on the oral sodomy count, and 10 years on the anal sodomy count, to be served consecutively.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged with first degree rape, forcible oral sodomy, and forcible anal sodomy. A jury returned verdicts of not guilty to the primary charges, but the jury found defendant guilty of consensual oral and anal sodomy, in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886 (1991), as lesser included offenses to the non-consensual sodomy charges. Defendant brought an appeal, arguing, first, that consensual heterosexual sodomy was not a crime and, because the jury acquitted defendant of committing any forcible act on the complainant, his two convictions for non-forcible sodomy must be dismissed. Second, he argued that the sentences should be modified. The court found that because the jury obviously found that the complainant consented to the sexual acts, rather than the acts being forced upon her, prosecution for sodomy under § 886 was improper. Prior decision demonstrated that a conviction for consensual sodomy between heterosexual adults was unconstitutional. Because the court reversed defendant's convictions and ordered dismissal of the charges, defendant's arguments regarding his sentence were moot.

Applegate v. State


No. F-94-0319


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 49; 904 P.2d 130; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 61; 66 O.B.A.J. 2908



September 13, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected October 11, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CREEK COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DONALD D. THOMPSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and Sentence of the District Court in case number CRF-93-101 is AFFIRMED. The Judgment and two twenty year terms in case number CRF-93-240 are also AFFIRMED, however, the sentence of life without parole is MODIFIED to fifty years imprisonment.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his conviction in the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma) for six counts of lewd molestation after two former lewd molestation convictions under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1123(A) (Supp. 1992), two counts of forcible sodomy under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 888 (1991), and his sentence of life without parole of the lewd molestation convictions and 20 years for the forcible sodomy convictions.


OVERVIEW: Defendant had been convicted for molesting two young boys, one of which had been living with him. The court modified defendant's sentence of life without parole for the sole count of lewd molestation of one boy to 50 years imprisonment because the evidence did not indicate that the boy was molested after the effective date of the amended punishment provision. Thus, defendant had been subjected to an ex post facto violation under U.S. Const. art. I, § 10 and Okla. Const. art. II, § 15. The court held that defendant's sentence was not inherently cruel and unusual punishment in violation of U.S. Const. art. VIII, and Okla. Const. art. II, § 9 because life without parole for some noncapital offenses was constitutional and that some mandatory life without parole terms were also constitutional. Although the sentences were severe, they were within the range provided by law and were not excessive because they did not shock the conscience of the court. The court affirmed the convictions, finding that defendant had not been convicted upon uncorroborated testimony because the two boys' statements were consistent at trial and had been subjected to cross-examination.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction for lewd molestation and forcible sodomy, but modified the sentence of life without parole for the lewd molestation conviction to 50 years imprisonment.

 

782 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cannon v. State


No. F-93-526


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 45; 904 P.2d 89; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 50; 66 O.B.A.J. 2779



September 8, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied October 6, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 64. Certiorari Denied March 18, 1996, Reported at: 1996 U.S. LEXIS 50.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS C. SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County, which convicted defendant of first-degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7, third-degree arson in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1403(A), first-degree rape in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1114, and forcible anal sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886(B), and sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first-degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7, third-degree arson in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1403(A), first-degree rape in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1114, and forcible anal sodomy in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 886(B). Defendant was sentenced to death for the murder conviction. On appeal, defendant argued, inter alia, that his custodial statement was involuntary and inadmissible because it was obtained through an illegal arrest, that the trial court erred in instructing the jury, and that the rape and sodomy convictions were improper. The court affirmed the convictions and sentence imposed for murder and arson, holding that the arrest was valid and that defendant's statements were not fruits of the poisonous tree. The court also rejected defendant's challenge to the instructions, holding that read as a whole, the instructions clearly required the jury to find that defendant's conduct caused the victim's death and that he intended to take a life. The court reversed the rape and sodomy convictions, holding that there was insufficient evidence of the element of penetration in either crime.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions of first degree murder and third-degree arson, holding that defendant's arrest was lawful and that the death sentence imposed was proper because the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, and cruel. The court reversed the rape and sodomy convictions with instructions to dismiss because the state failed to establish penetration, which was an essential element of the crime.

 

783 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Braun v. State


Case No. C-93-993


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 42; 909 P.2d 783; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 47; 66 O.B.A.J. 2675



August 7, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CARTER COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS S. WALKER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment of the District Court of Carter County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of one count of first degree murder, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7, two counts of shooting with intent to kill, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 652, and two counts of robbery with firearms, Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 801. Defendant was sentenced to death on the murder count, 25 years on each robbery count, and life on each shooting with intent to kill count.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions arose out of the robbery of a flower shop where he ordered a customer and two employees to the back of the shop. Defendant shot each person in the back of the head, killing one, when they were on the floor. After the trial court sentenced defendant to death for the murder, he filed a motion to withdraw his nolo contendere plea, which the trial court denied. On appeal, the court held that defendant was not denied effective assistance of counsel in the hearing on his motion to withdraw his plea. Although his counsel did not show up, defendant intelligently and understandingly rejected the offer of other counsel. Defendant knew what he was doing when he proceeded in the hearing without counsel. He was also not denied effective assistance when his trial counsel failed to file a motion for change of venue because a change of venue, even if properly asserted, would in all probability have not been successful. The court also found that defendant was not misled into believing that he would get life without parole on the murder charge. Neither the State nor the trial court promised a life without parole sentence on a guilty plea.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of the trial court.

 

784 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Moore v. State


Case No. F-90-471


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 39; 900 P.2d 996; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 44; 66 O.B.A.J. 2559



July 25, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF MUSKOGEE COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE THOMAS A. ALFORD, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The court sua sponte decided to review a decision of the Emergency Appellate Division (Oklahoma), which reversed defendant's conviction and sentence after finding that two strikes of two African-American veniremen were racially motivated, and finding that the peremptory challenge statute, Okla. Stat. tit. 22, § 654, violated the due process principles of Okla. Const. art. II, §§ 7, 20.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was convicted of first degree burglary and assault and battery with a dangerous weapon, both after former conviction of two felonies, and was sentenced to 20 years' imprisonment for each conviction. The appeals court reversed, finding that two peremptory strikes were racially motivated and that the peremptory challenge statute was unconstitutional. Reversing, the court held that one venireman was properly struck as she stated that she preferred not to sit on the jury as her experience as a youth guidance counselor led her to believe that defendant was guilty. The court found that another venireman's statement that he would not convict on the basis of the victim's testimony alone, along with his youth and prior service on another jury were neutral reasons for striking him. The court held the statute to be constitutional. The court found that defendant's lineup was error because he was dressed differently so as to be suggestive, but that this error was not prejudicial because the victim had previous sufficient opportunity to view the perpetrator.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the appeals court's judgment and affirmed the judgment and sentence of the trial court.

Powell v. State


No. F-91-431


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 37; 906 P.2d 765; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 42; 66 O.B.A.J. 2415



July 14, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Corrected by, On rehearing at Powell v. State, 902 P.2d 1119, 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 57 (Okla. Crim. App., 1995)
Habeas corpus proceeding at Spears v. Mullin, 2003 U.S. App. LEXIS 16586 (10th Cir. Okla., Aug. 12, 2003)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT IN GARVIN COUNTY. THE HONORABLE J. KENNETH LOVE, DISTRICT JUDGE.

Order Granting Rehearing Previously Reported at: 902 P.2d 1119 and Withdrawn from the Bound Volume.
Spears v. State, 1995 OK CR 36, 900 P.2d 431, 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 43 (Okla. Crim. App., 1995)



DISPOSITION: We AFFIRM.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged the judgment from the District Court in Garvin County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of murder in the first degree. The jury found two aggravating circumstances pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 701.12(4),(5) (1981)and the trial court sentenced defendant to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was jointly tried for beating and stabbing the victim to death. The jury found under Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 701.12(4),(5) (1981)that the murder was especially heinous, atrocious, or cruel and was committed for the purpose of avoiding or preventing a lawful arrest or prosecution. The court affirmed. The trial court was within its discretion in refusing to disqualify a prospective juror for cause. Defendant was not prejudiced by the introduction of his non-testifying co-defendant's hearsay statement because defendant confessed that he intended to kill the victim. The court found that the killing could precede, coincide with, or follow the robbery and still be done in the commission of robbery with a dangerous weapon. Because the State proved both malice and felony murder, the jury's failure to indicate the basis of its finding of guilt was not error. Prosecutorial remarks were harmless error. The evidence was not sufficient to support voluntary intoxication and first degree diminished capacity manslaughter instructions. Defendant received effective assistance of counsel. The court granted rehearing to correct an omission in the opinion but no relief was warranted.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment that convicted defendant of murder in the first degree and sentenced him to death.

Tiger v. State


Case No. C-91-973


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 30; 900 P.2d 406; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 36



June 23, 1995, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected August 15, 1995.



DISPOSITION: Certiorari granted and vacated the judgment and sentence to the trial court. Remanded to the trial court for further proceedings consistent with this order.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: On a writ of certiorari and mandatory sentence review on the imposition of the death penalty, defendant sought review of a judgment of the District Court of Mayes County (Oklahoma), which, following defendant's guilty plea sentenced him to death by lethal injection and denied defendant's motion to change his plea. Defendant was charged with first degree malice aforethought murder.


OVERVIEW: At his formal arraignment, defendant entered a not guilty plea. The State filed a second amended information and alleged two aggravating circumstances. Defendant sought to change his plea, and before the jury was sworn the trial court accepted his plea of guilty to the second amended information. This blind plea was entered without any recommendation by the State for an appropriate punishment. After an extensive sentencing hearing in which both aggravating and mitigating evidence were presented, the trial court found the existence of the two aggravating circumstances and sentenced defendant to die. The trial court denied defendant's application to withdraw his guilty plea. The court vacated and remanded. The court found that the second amended information did not recite facts to allege every essential element of the crime charged. Therefore, the court stated that such information failed to charge a crime and failed to confer subject matter jurisdiction on the trial court. The court held that a criminal information that did not allege all the essential elements of the offense charged was insufficient, and the defect went to the jurisdiction of the court and was not waivable.


OUTCOME: The court granted certiorari and vacated the judgment and sentence and remanded.

Hill v. State


No. F-94-0207


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 28; 898 P.2d 155; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 33; 66 O.B.A.J. 1853



May 19, 1995, FILED



DISPOSITION:  [***1] REVERSE and REMAND


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) convicting him of possession of a firearm while committing a felony, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 1287 (1991), and possession of a controlled dangerous substance without a tax stamp, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 68, § 450.3 (1991).


OVERVIEW: Defendant was a passenger in a car that was found to have cocaine and a gun. Defendant attempted to flee during his arrest. The drug charge was based on the Oklahoma Controlled Dangerous Substance Tax Act, Okla. Stat. tit. 68, §§ 450.1-450.9. The court rejected defendant's claim that the nominally civil Act was unconstitutional, holding that there was insufficient proof that the Act was a pretext for inflicting additional criminal punishment for possession of controlled dangerous substances. Although the trial court erred by failing to include part of Okla. Unif. Jury Instructions Crim. No. 806, the error did not require reversal because the flight instruction was cured by other instructions. The court reversed defendant's convictions because the prosecutor questioned defendant about his withdrawn guilty plea and introduced the plea into evidence in contravention of Okla. Stat. tit. 12, § 2410 (1991). The admission of and questioning about the withdrawn guilty plea was an abuse of discretion that likely had a substantial influence on the outcome of the trial. However, because there was other sufficient evidence to support the convictions, the court remanded for a new trial.


OUTCOME: The court reversed defendant's convictions and remanded the case for a new trial.

LaFevers v. State


No. F-93-324


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 26; 897 P.2d 292; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 31; 66 O.B.A.J. 1681



May 16, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied June 21, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 35.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE THOMAS C. SMITH, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first degree malice aforethought murder in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1991), and third degree arson in violation of § 1403(A) (1981), and sentenced him to death for the murder conviction and 40 years incarceration for the arson. Defendant challenged his conviction and the imposition of the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's original conviction for malice murder, third arson, rape, and forcible sodomy were reversed, but the conviction for kidnapping, burglary, robbery, and motor vehicle larceny were affirmed. Defendant was convicted at retrial of malice murder and third degree arson, and appealed. Defendant alleged numerous errors committed by the trial court that related to his death sentence and conviction. The court affirmed the judgment of conviction. The court held that the admission of defendant's pretrial statements to police had not violated defendant's right to counsel. The court found that defendant's request for counsel was ambiguous and that defendant had not unequivocally said that he wanted an attorney while he was being questioned by the police, or that he wanted questioning to end. The court found that defendant's words had not invoked his right to counsel, and therefore it was waived. Defendant's subsequent statement of "I'll talk to you" resolved any ambiguity that may have existed as to defendant's waiver of his right to counsel. Reinitiation by the police was not an issue because there was no prior exercise of defendant's right of counsel.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Tate v. State


No. F-87-982


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 24; 896 P.2d 1182; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 29; 66 O.B.A.J. 1663



May 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] As Corrected May 16, 1995.
Magistrate's recommendation at, Habeas corpus proceeding at Tate v. Addison, 2009 U.S. Dist. LEXIS 122136 (W.D. Okla., Nov. 30, 2009)


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JACK R. PARR, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: Counts II and III are AFFIRMED. Appellant's conviction for the murder of Rosalee Tate is AFFIRMED, but his death sentence is REVERSED and the matter REMANDED to District Court for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a decision of the District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which entered convictions for first degree murder in the death of his former wife, Count I; first degree murder in the death of the wife's friend, Count II; and one count of pointing a firearm in the district court, Count III. The district court imposed the death penalty for Count I, life imprisonment for Count II, and 10 years for Count III.


OVERVIEW: While in the parking lot of a supermarket, defendant shot to death his former wife and her friend. On appeal, defendant argued that the retrospective competency determination violated his due process rights. The court disagreed and affirmed the convictions. In doing so, the court held that (1) the trial court properly found that a retrospective competency determination was feasible; (2) competent evidence existed from which the jury could have made meaningful determination of defendant's competency at the time of his trial, in that the examining psychiatrist, three defense attorneys, and the psychiatrist's written report were available; and (3) there was no due process violation in requiring defendant to prove his incompetence by clear and convincing evidence. However, the court did reverse the death sentence for the murder of defendant' former wife because the trial court erred when it gave life imprisonment and death as the only sentencing options for Counts I and II. Pursuant to Okla. Stat. tit. 21, §§ 701.9 and 701.10 (Supp.1987), which came into effect just prior to defendant's trial, the jury should have also been instructed on the punishment of "life without parole."


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions but reversed the death sentence for Count I. The action was remanded to the district court for resentencing. The sentences for Count II and III were affirmed.

Perry v. State


No. F-90-1295


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 20; 893 P.2d 521; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 26; 66 O.B.A.J. 1350



April 7, 1995, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a decision by the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma) that rendered judgment upon a jury verdict convicting defendant of first degree murder and imposed the recommended sentence of death.


OVERVIEW: At the trial, a medical examination of the victim revealed a stab wound to the chest, a blow to the head, and small bruises to the face. At the sentencing stage, the jury found two aggravating circumstances warranting the death penalty, which included a finding that the murder was heinous and that defendant was a continuing threat to society. Defendant contended, inter alia, that he was incompetent to stand trial and that aggravating circumstances were not proven. The court ruled that his sentence should be modified to life without parole. The court held that: (1) although the lower court erred in taking judicial notice of the doctor's report on defendant's competency, the error was harmless because defendant offered no evidence to sustain his burden of showing that he was incompetent; (2) defendant's right to a fair trial was not violated because the judge's conversation with the jurors about their motel did not have a reasonably substantial relation to defendant's ability to defend against the charges; and (3) the aggravating circumstances were not proven because there was no evidence of conscious physical suffering or evidence that defendant had a pattern of criminal conduct.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment of conviction and modified the death sentence to life imprisonment.

Wallace v. State


Case No. C-91-309


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 19; 893 P.2d 504; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 24; 66 O.B.A.J. 1150



March 27, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF LeFLORE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE TED A. KNIGHT, ASSOCIATE DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant challenged a judgment of the District Court of LeFlore County (Oklahoma) convicting him upon his plea of guilty to two charges of murder in the first degree, a violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7(A) (Supp. 1989). The district court ordered defendant sentenced to death by lethal injection on each count. Defendant refused to present a defense during his sentencing hearing; and in fact requested the death penalty.


OVERVIEW: Defendant admitted that on two occasions he had posed as a police officer, "arrested" teenage boys, beat them, shot them, and dragged their bodies to a pond and left them there. Defendant was found competent in two competency hearings. Affirming, the court held that defendant was entitled to waive the presentation of mitigating evidence, and could do so without running afoul of the ban against arbitrary and unreliable application of the death penalty implicit in the Eighth Amendment to the United States Constitution.The court found that a rule requiring the presentation of mitigating evidence would not be enforceable, noting that courts were not able to force an unwilling defendant to provide mitigating evidence to his attorney.The prosecution was required to present evidence of aggravating circumstances, which the trial court was required to find beyond a reasonable doubt before it could impose the death sentence; the trial court was required to afford defendant the opportunity to present mitigating evidence, which it did; and the court was required to review the evidence in the case to determine if the sentence was imposed in an arbitrary or unreliable manner, which it was not.


OUTCOME: The judgments and the sentences of the district court, finding defendant guilty of two counts of first degree murder and sentencing him to death by lethal injection, was affirmed.
