Valdez v. State


F-90-461


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 18; 900 P.2d 363; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 23; 66 O.B.A.J. 1126



March 15, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Rehearing Denied April 14, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY: AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF GRADY COUNTY. THE HONORABLE JAMES R. WINCHESTER, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of a judgment from the District Court of Grady County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced defendant to death after defendant allegedly killed a man because of the man's homosexuality. In seeking review, defendant raised pretrial and jury selection issues, guilt/innocence issues, sentencing stage issues, prosecutorial misconduct issues, and ineffective assistance of counsel issues.


OVERVIEW: After leaving a bar, defendant killed the victim because of the victim's homosexuality. Thereafter, defendant was convicted of first-degree murder and sentenced to death. Upon review, the court held that defendant had failed to overcome the presumption of competency and had lacked a right to individual voir dire. The court also upheld a confession's admissibility because defendant's Miranda rights had been waived. Moreover, the court held that defendant's right to counsel under U.S. Const. amends. V, VI had not barred an immigration officer's interrogation. Furthermore, the court held that defendant had not been entitled to second degree murder and voluntary intoxication instructions because the evidence had not warranted either instruction. In addition, the court held that the jury would have imposed the death sentence absent an invalid great risk of death aggravator. Likewise, the court held that even though the prosecutor had acted improperly by having defendant reenact the murder, the misconduct had not contributed to the verdict. Finally, the court rejected defendant's ineffective assistance of counsel claims because the alleged deficiencies had been non-prejudicial.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment which convicted defendant of first-degree murder and sentenced defendant to death.

 

794 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


White v. State


No. F-93-1156


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 15; 900 P.2d 982; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 90



February 23, 1995, FILED


PRIOR HISTORY:  [**1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF ATOKA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DOUG GABBARD II, JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed his convictions by the District Court of Atoka County (Oklahoma) for trafficking in illegal drugs in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 2-415 (1991) and unlawful possession of a controlled dangerous substance without a tax stamp in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 63, § 450.4 (1991).


OVERVIEW: As a passenger in a vehicle pulled over for a traffic infraction, defendant was seen trying to hide drugs. Defendant claimed that he lacked possession of the drugs and that the Oklahoma Drug Tax Stamp Act unconstitutionally infringed his rights against self-incrimination. The court held that the convictions were proper. There was circumstantial evidence that defendant was trafficking the drugs when he exercised power and dominion over them when he tried to hide them. The police officer's testimony did not have to be corroborated. The Act did not unconstitutionally infringe defendant's rights against self-incrimination because defendant did not have to be identified because he did not have to buy the stamps but only affix them. Also, the Act provided immunity through its confidentiality and anonymity provisions, which prevented a disclosure of defendant's identity if he bought the stamps, and thus, the revenue agents were prevented from forwarding defendant's name to prosecuting authorities. Thus, the Act provided use and derivative-use immunity arising form the purchase of the stamps. The sentences were properly enhanced by defendant's guilty pleas to two earlier felonies.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the convictions.

Rogers v. State


No. F-92-65


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 8; 890 P.2d 959; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 9; 66 O.B.A.J. 378



January 24, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied March 8, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 22.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF PAYNE COUNTY. THE HONORABLE DONALD L. WORTHINGTON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant sought review of his conviction and sentence to death after a jury trial in the District Court of Payne County (Oklahoma) on charges of first-degree malice aforethought murder, first-degree robbery, first-degree rape, and larceny of a motor vehicle.


OVERVIEW: Defendant ordered a pizza. Defendant robbed the delivery woman, drove her to an ATM and made her withdraw cash, then took her to her apartment, raped her, and stabbed her to death. The jury returned a guilty verdict on the first-degree murder and other charges, finding aggravating circumstances warranting the death penalty. The trial court entered a judgment of conviction and sentenced defendant to death. The court affirmed the conviction and the sentence, holding that (1) defendant did not show that he was prejudiced by a lack of expert assistance at state expense, nor was his right to effective assistance of counsel violated by the trial court's denial of such funds; (2) the information charging defendant with rape was not defective because it alleged a date and victim certain and every material element of rape, which could have been phrased in terms of statutory language because the jury was instructed that penetration was required; (3) double jeopardy did not attach on two robbery charges because the transactions were separate and each required dissimilar proof; and (4) the evidence presented at trial was sufficient to support the jury's aggravating circumstance findings.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's conviction and sentence to death on charges of first-degree malice aforethought murder, first-degree robbery, first-degree rape, and larceny of a motor vehicle.

 

796 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Cooper v. State


Case No. F-92-533


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 2; 889 P.2d 293; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 4; 66 O.B.A.J. 166



January 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied February 13, 1995. Released for Publication February 13, 1995. As Corrected March 24, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE RICHARD J. FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment and sentence for First Degree Murder is AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed a judgment from the District Court Of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma), which convicted defendant of murder in the first degree in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (Supp.1989) and sentenced him to death.


OVERVIEW: Defendant challenged a finding that he was competent to stand trial, the jury venire, the jury charges, the competency of counsel, and the sentence. The court found no error warranting modification or reversal. The presumption of competency and the burden of proving incompetency by clear and convincing evidence did not offend Due Process, and the evidence supporting defendant's competency was sufficient. It was unnecessary for the state to prove a juror's bias against the death penalty with unmistakable clarity. Any error in giving a flight instruction was harmless because it referred to an uncharged crime, possession of drug paraphernalia. The denial of a request to charge on reasonable doubt was proper regardless of who requested it. Defendant failed to overcome the strong presumption of the competency of his counsel. The Oklahoma death penalty statutes were constitutional. The finding of an aggravating circumstance of commission of the offense while imprisoned for a felony was proper because defendant's enrollment in the Pre-Parole Conditional Supervision program was still incarceration. There was no evidence that the death sentence was imposed under any arbitrary factor.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the judgment.

Clayton v. State


No. PC-94-180


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1995 OK CR 3; 892 P.2d 646; 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 21; 66 O.B.A.J. 874



January 10, 1995, Decided  
January 10, 1995, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY:  [***1] Released for Publication March 6, 1995.



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner, who was convicted of murder in the first degree and sentenced to death, appealed from the order of the District Court of Tulsa County (Oklahoma), which denied his application for post-conviction relief.


OVERVIEW: Petitioner was convicted of murder and sentenced to death. His conviction was affirmed on appeal. The trial court denied defendant's application for post-conviction relief. The court affirmed the order and held that, although the trial court should have determined that admission of a purported expert witness's blood spatter testimony was error because the witness overstated his qualifications and affidavits concluded that the witness was not qualified to testify, the error was harmless because there was other overwhelming evidence to have supported aggravating circumstances such that they precluded a manslaughter instruction. The court also held that the 60-day filing period for post-conviction relief did not violate petitioner's right to due process because it satisfied the legislative intent to expedite review of capital post conviction petitions and protected his ability to timely file a federal petition for writ of habeas corpus upon exhaustion of state remedies. Nor were petitioner's equal protection rights violated because he did not have a fundamental right to post conviction review. The court also held that petitioner's counsel was not ineffective.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the trial court's order denying post-conviction relief to defendant.

 

798 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Lambert v. State


No. F-88-388


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 79; 888 P.2d 494; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 92; 65 O.B.A.J. 4111



December 8, 1994, FILED


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Counsel Amended December 28, 1994. Rehearing Denied January 9, 1995. Released for Publication January 9, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF CREEK COUNTY. BEFORE THE HONORABLE DONALD D. THOMPSON, DISTRICT JUDGE.



DISPOSITION: The Judgment of the trial court is AFFIRMED as to the convictions and sentences for Kidnapping, Robbery with Firearms, Larceny of an Automobile and Third Degree Arson. The convictions for Murder (Counts I and II) are REVERSED AND REMANDED FOR A NEW TRIAL.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant appealed the judgment of the District Court of Creek County (Oklahoma), which convicted him of two counts each of murder in the first degree, kidnapping, robbery with firearms, and larceny of an automobile and one count of arson in the third degree after a two-stage jury trial. Defendant challenged both the guilty verdicts and the sentences imposed for the crimes.


OVERVIEW: Defendant's convictions were based on the death of two victims that occurred when defendant and an accomplice stole a car, kidnapped and robbed its occupants, and set the car on fire. A two-stage jury trial was conducted. On appeal, the court found no merit to defendant's challenge to the constitutionality of both the competency proceedings in general and as applied to him retrospectively or his claim that the jury was allowed to consider improper evidence, that his request for a change of venue or individual voir dire should have been granted, and that the jury was improperly instructed as to the burden of proof and the effect of their decision. The court, however, found that though the information was sufficient insofar as it contained the essential elements of the crimes of first degree malice afore-thought murder, kidnapping, armed robbery, larceny of an automobile and third degree arson, and was sufficient to bar future prosecution for those offenses, it failed to also charge felony murder. The jury instruction on felony murder after defendant had relied on the information to his detriment was reversible error.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the murder conviction and remanded for a new trial. However, the court affirmed the remaining convictions.

 

799 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


State v. Saunders


No. S-94-0177


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 76; 886 P.2d 496; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 87



November 29, 1994, Decided  
November 29, 1994, FILED


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The State appealed a decision of a trial court (Oklahoma), which granted defendant's pre-trial motion to dismiss, finding that Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1173 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional.


OVERVIEW: Defendant was charged by information with stalking. He filed a motion to dismiss, alleging that Okla. Stat. art. 21, § 1173 (Supp. 1993) was unconstitutional. The trial court granted the motion, finding that the statute was unconstitutional in that it violated the due process clause, as well as the Fifth Amendment, presumption of innocence, and that it was vague, overbroad, and could not be reasonably interpreted by anyone subject to the statute with common knowledge and understanding. On appeal, the court reversed. The court found that § 1173 gave fair notice of the proscribed activity and was not void for vagueness on its face where by the use of the phrases "repeatedly," and "willfully and maliciously," the legislature had added to the required specific intent and provided that the perpetrator's intent was to trigger the statute. The court also found a rational connection between the facts proved (a course of conduct, a request by the victim that it stop, and a continuation of the conduct), and the facts presumed (that the victim actually felt terrorized, frightened, etc.), so the statute's rebuttable presumption did not unconstitutionally shift the burden of proof to defendant.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the trial court's grant of defendant's pre-trial motion to dismiss.

 

800 of 1460 DOCUMENTS


Hooker v. State


No. F-88-915


COURT OF CRIMINAL APPEALS OF OKLAHOMA


1994 OK CR 75; 887 P.2d 1351; 1994 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 86; 65 O.B.A.J. 3845



November 14, 1994, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Rehearing Denied January 23, 1995, Reported at: 1995 Okla. Crim. App. LEXIS 6. Released for Publication January 23, 1995.


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] AN APPEAL FROM THE DISTRICT COURT OF OKLAHOMA COUNTY. THE HONORABLE LEAMON FREEMAN, DISTRICT JUDGE



DISPOSITION: AFFIRMED.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendant was charged with two counts of first degree murder with malice aforethought in violation of Okla. Stat. tit. 21, § 701.7 (1982), and the jury found him guilty of both charges. The District Court of Oklahoma County (Oklahoma) imposed the death penalty, and defendant appealed.


OVERVIEW: Defendant stabbed his common law wife and her mother to death after the common law wife refused to return to him. Witnesses testified that they saw defendant leaving the victims' apartment wearing bloody clothes. Defendant claimed that the lower court erred in admitting evidence that he attacked his common law wife with a pool cue on a prior occasion and in admitting portions of a victim's protective order that she obtained against him. The court held that (1) the pool cue incident was probative of motive or intent; (2) the portions of the victim's protective order indicating that the common law wife was afraid that defendant would harm her were admissible under the state of mind exception to the hearsay rule; (3) the portions of the order referring to the fact that defendant had killed others in the past were inadmissible, but the error was harmless beyond a reasonable doubt; (4) defendant was not entitled to a lesser-included instruction on second degree murder and manslaughter because his defense was that he committed no crime at all, not that he committed a lesser offense; and (5) the evidence was sufficient to support defendant's convictions.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed defendant's convictions.
